Makruh Times for Nafl After Fajr and After Asr
States ruling and evidences for prohibition of nafl after fajr and asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on nafl prayers after Fajr and Asr, identify the evidence from hadith, and explain why the Hanafi school classifies it as makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Nafl after Fajr and Asr is makruh tanzihi; fard and wajib prayers remain permissible.

This lesson examines a specific ruling regarding voluntary prayers (nafl) at certain times. The text states that after the Fajr prayer (both its sunnah and fard) and after the Asr fard, it is makruh to perform nafl. However, missed obligatory prayers or wajib prayers like witr are allowed. We will explore the hadith evidence and the Hanafi reasoning behind this classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the first part of the text: after the sunnah and fard of Fajr, and after Asr fard, nafl is makruh. Note that the text explicitly states 'however one may pray another fard or wajib'.
2
Locate the Evidence
The text cites three hadith: from Ibn Umar (لا صلاة بعد الفجر الا سجدتین), from Ibn Abbas (نهى عن الصلاة بعد الصبح حتى تشرق الشمس وبعد العصر حتى تغرب), and from Amr ibn Abasah (similar prohibition).
3
Analyze the Dalil
The first hadith explicitly prohibits any prayer after Fajr except the two prostrations (the sunnah of Fajr). The second and third hadith forbid prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. Together, they establish a prohibition during these times.
The prohibition is general but Hanafis interpret it as specific to nafl because the hadith itself excludes the two sunnah of Fajr, and other hadith allow fard/wajib.
4
Understand the Hanafi Interpretation
Hanafi scholars classify this as makruh tanzihi (disliked, not sinful) rather than haram because the prohibition is for nafl only. The evidence points to a mild discouragement, not an absolute prohibition.
This is based on the principle that the imperative in 'no prayer' is interpreted as karahah when there is evidence that fard/wajib are exempted.
5
Note the Practical Consequence
In practice, one may still pray fard (missed or current), wajib (e.g., witr), or the two sunnah of Fajr during these times. Only non-sunnah nafl (voluntary prayers) are discouraged.
The ruling applies from true dawn (subh sadiq) until sunrise for Fajr, and after Asr until sunset for Asr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاوقات المكروهة
سنته و بعد صلوته وبعد صلوة العصر (۳۱۶) وقبل صلوة المغرب
پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ [۳] اسی طرح عصر کے فرض کے بعد کوئی نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ کوئی اور فرض یا واجب پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
وجه : (1) عن ابن عمر أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : لا صلاة بعد الفجر الا سجدتین ۔(ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء لا صلاة بعد طلوع الفجر الا ركعتین ،ص ۱۱۳، نمبر ۴۱۹/ مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب ركعتی سنته الفجر الخ ، ص ۲۹۳، نمبر ۷۲۳/ ۱۶۷۸ أبو داود شریف ، باب من رخص فیهما اذا كانت الشمس مرتفعة، ص ۱۹۱، نمبر ۱۳۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صبح صادق کے بعد دوسنتوں سے زیادہ نہ پڑھے،اسلئے دوسنتوں کے علاوہ نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فجر کے فرض کے بعد کوئی نفل نہ پڑھے۔ عن ابن عباس .... أن النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن الصلاة بعد الصبح حتى تشرق الشمس ، و بعد العصر حتى تغرب (بخاری شریف، باب الصلاة بعد الفجر حتى ترتفع الشمس ،ص ۸۲ نمبر ۸۵۸۱ مسلم شریف ، باب اسلام عمر و بن عبسته ، ص ۱۳۳۴، نمبر ۱۹۳۰/۸۳۲) ۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ قال عمرو بن عبسة السلمى .... فقلت : يا نبی الله أخبرنــي عـمـا عـلـمك الله و أجهله ، أخبرني عن الصلاة ؟ قال : صل صلاة الصبح ، ثم اقصر عن الصلاة حتى تطلع الشمس حتى ترتفع ..... حتى تصلى العصر ، ثم اقصر عن الصلاة حتى تغرب الشمس فانها تغـرب بين قرني الشيطان و حينئذ يسجد لها الكفار (مسلم شريف، باب اسلام عمر و بن عبستہ ۔ ابواب صلاۃ المسافرین ،ص ۳۳۴، نمبر ۱۹۳۰/۸۳۲ سنن نسائی ، باب انھی عن الصلاة بعد العصر ص ۷۹ نمبر ۵۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فجر کے فرض کے بعد کوئی نفل نہ پڑھے۔ اور عصر کے فرض کے بعد بھی کوئی نفل نہ پڑھے۔
Chapter on disallowed times. Its sunnah and after its prayer and after Asr prayer (316) and before Maghrib prayer. It is makruh. [3] Similarly, after the fard of Asr, praying any nafl is makruh. However, one may pray another fard or wajib. Proof: (1) From Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: No prayer after Fajr except two prostrations. (Tirmidhi, Muslim, Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that after true dawn, do not pray more than two sunnahs, so praying nafl besides the two sunnahs is makruh. (2) This hadith states that no nafl after fajr fard. From Ibn Abbas... that the Prophet forbade prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. (Bukhari, Muslim) (3) This hadith also. Amr ibn Abasah said... I said: O Prophet, tell me about prayer. He said: Pray the morning prayer, then abstain from prayer until the sun rises and rises high... until you pray Asr, then abstain from prayer until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of Satan and then the disbelievers prostrate to it. (Muslim, Nasa'i) This hadith indicates that after fajr fard, no nafl, and after asr fard also no nafl.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding makruh times for nafl prayers. The text first states the general ruling: after the sunnah of Fajr, after the fard of Fajr, and after Asr prayer, it is makruh to pray nafl. However, one may pray fard or wajib prayers. Then three hadith are provided as evidences. The first hadith from Ibn Umar explicitly says there is no prayer after Fajr except the two prostrations (i.e., the two sunnah rak'ahs), which means any additional nafl is makruh. The second hadith from Ibn Abbas states the Prophet forbade prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. The third hadith from Amr ibn Abasah gives the same prohibition. The Hanafi school takes these hadith as indicating karahah tanzihiyyah (dislike) rather than absolute prohibition, since fard and wajib prayers are still allowed at these times.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an action that is not sinful but is discouraged. In Hanafi fiqh, makruh tanzihi is less severe than makruh tahrimi.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory and sunnah prayers.
صبح صادق (subh sadiq): The true dawn, when the light spreads horizontally on the horizon, marking the beginning of Fajr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is nafl after Fajr and Asr considered makruh rather than haram?
A) Because the hadith prohibition is only for nafl, and fard/wajib are allowed
B) Because the hadith are weak
C) Because consensus allows it
D) Because the Prophet himself prayed nafl after Asr

Key Takeaway
Nafl after Fajr and Asr is makruh tanzihi; fard and wajib are permitted, and the two sunnah of Fajr are exempted.

Nafl Before Maghrib: Makruh Tanzihi in the Hanafi School
Ruling with proof on nafl before Maghrib with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl before Maghrib, identify the key proofs, and explain why it is makruh tanzihi rather than haram.

Core Idea
Praying nafl before Maghrib is makruh tanzihi: permissible but better avoided.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on voluntary prayer (nafl) before the obligatory Maghrib prayer. While other schools permit it, Hanafis consider it lightly disliked (makruh tanzihi). We will explore the proofs: the hadith urging early Maghrib, the Companions' practice, and the permissive hadith that prevents it from being forbidden.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify that the act of praying nafl before Maghrib is classified as makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the first proof
The hadith of Abu Ayyub: the Prophet said the community remains in good as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine. This implies one should not occupy oneself with nafl before Maghrib.
Reference: Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah.
3
Identify the second proof
The practice of the Companions: Ibn Umar said he did not see anyone in the Prophet's time praying two rak'ahs before Maghrib.
Reference: Abu Dawud.
4
Identify the permissive proof
The hadith of Abdullah al-Muzani: the Prophet said 'Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib for whoever wishes,' indicating permissibility.
The Prophet's fear that it might become a sunnah shows it is not recommended.
5
Understand the tarjih
Hanafis weigh the discouraging proofs (early Maghrib, Companion practice) over the permissive proof, resulting in makruh tanzihi rather than haram or mubah.
The permissive proof prevents it from being makruh tahrimi or haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۱۶) [۴] اور مغرب کی نماز سے پہلے ۔ تشریح : مغرب کے فرض سے پہلے نفل پڑھنا حنفیہ کے نزدیک مکروہ تنزیہی ہے، دوسرے ائمہ کے یہاں جائز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ فقام اليه ابو ایوب ... وقال اما سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول لا تزال امتى بخير او قال على الفطرة مالم يؤخروا المغرب الى ان تشتبك النجوم ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی وقت المغرب ص اے؟ نمبر ۴۱۸ وابن ماجه ، باب وقت صلاة المغرب ،ص ۹۷، نمبر ۶۸۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کو جلدی پڑھنا خیر کی چیز ہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور کے زمانے میں صحابہ مغرب کے بعد اور فرض سے پہلے نفل نہیں پڑھتے تھے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ سئل ابن عمر عن الركعتين قبل المغرب فقال : ما رأيت أحدا على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصليهما ، و رخص في الركعتين بعد العصر (ابوداود شریف، باب الصلاة قبل المغرب ، ص۱۹۲، نمبر۱۲۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب سے پہلے نفل نہ پڑھے۔(۳) لیکن اگر پڑھ لیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔حدیث یہ ہے۔عن عبد الله المزني قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : صلوا قبل المغرب ركعتين ، ثم قال : صلوا قبل المغرب ركعتين لمن شاء . خشية أن يتخذها الناس سنة - ابوداود شریف، باب الصلاة قبل المغرب ، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۱۲۸۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کوئی پڑھنا چاہے تو پڑھے۔
Translation: (316) [4] And before Maghrib prayer. Explanation: Praying nafl before the fard of Maghrib is makruh tanzihi according to the Hanafis; according to other imams, it is permissible. Proof: (1) The hadith: Abu Ayyub stood up... and said: Did you not hear the Messenger of Allah say: 'My community will remain in good (or on fitrah) as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine.' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah) This hadith indicates that praying Maghrib early is good. (2) A hadith that in the time of the Prophet, the Companions did not pray nafl before Maghrib. The hadith: Ibn Umar was asked about two rak'ahs before Maghrib, and he said: I did not see anyone in the time of the Messenger of Allah praying them, and he allowed two rak'ahs after Asr. (Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates not to pray nafl before Maghrib. (3) But if one prays, it is permissible because there is evidence. The hadith: Abdullah al-Muzani said: The Messenger of Allah said: Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib, then he said: Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib for whoever wishes, fearing that people might take it as a sunnah. (Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that whoever wants to may pray.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding nafl prayer before Maghrib. The text first gives the translation of the heading (316) and then an explanation: for Hanafis, it is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), while other imams permit it. Three proofs are given: (1) The hadith encouraging praying Maghrib early, which implies that one should not delay it by praying nafl beforehand. (2) The practice of the Companions, as narrated by Ibn Umar, who said he did not see anyone in the Prophet's time praying two rak'ahs before Maghrib. (3) However, if one does pray, it is valid, as evidenced by the hadith of Abdullah al-Muzani, where the Prophet permitted it while fearing it might become a regular sunnah. The Hanafi position balances these evidences: it is disliked but not forbidden, hence makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms
مكروه تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): Lightly disliked; an action that is not sinful but better avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider nafl before Maghrib makruh tanzihi rather than haram?
A) Because the hadith permitting it are authentic
B) Because the prohibition is only based on the lack of practice of Companions
C) Because the Prophet himself prayed it
D) Because the hadith encouraging early Maghrib implies one should not delay with nafl

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules nafl before Maghrib as makruh tanzihi, balancing discouraging proofs with permissive evidence.

Prohibition of Nafl During Jumu'ah Khutbah
Ruling with evidence for prohibition of nafl during Jumu'ah khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl during the Jumu'ah khutbah and identify the exception for tahiyyah al-masjid.

Core Idea
Nafl during the Friday khutbah is makruh, but two rak'ahs of tahiyyah al-masjid are an exception.

The source explains that from the time the khatib appears until Jumu'ah prayer ends, it is disliked to pray any nafl. However, if you enter the mosque during the khutbah and have not yet prayed the two rak'ahs of tahiyyah, you should pray them lightly. This ruling is based on Quranic command to listen and silent, and hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying any nafl (supererogatory prayer) from the moment the khatib comes out for the khutbah until the Jumu'ah fard prayer finishes. The ruling stated is 'makruh'.
Note that the text says 'makruh', not 'haram'. The presence of an exception indicates it is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
2
Understand the primary evidence
The Quranic verse (7:204) commands listening and silence when the Quran is recited. Since the khutbah includes Quran recitation, praying would prevent listening. A hadith in Bayhaqi says the imam's coming out cuts off both speech and prayer.
The dalil is both Quran (qati al-thubut) and hadith (zanni al-thubut), but the ruling is derived from combining both.
3
Recognize the exception and its evidence
The exception is for two rak'ahs when one enters the mosque during the khutbah. The hadith from Jabir in Bukhari and Muslim shows the Prophet commanding a latecomer to pray two rak'ahs. This indicates the general prohibition is not absolute.
These two rak'ahs are typically considered tahiyyah al-masjid or the sunnah of Jumu'ah that was missed.
4
Determine the type of karahah
Because the exception is allowed, the karahah is tanzihiyyah (light dislike), not tahrimiyyah (prohibited). The Hanafi authorities consider it better not to pray, but permissible to do so for the two rak'ahs.
Authority weight is from later Hanafi fatwa works (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if you are present from the start of the khutbah, you should not pray any nafl. If you enter late and have not prayed the two rak'ahs, you should pray them quickly and then listen.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۱۷) (۵) اور خطبہ کے لئے خطیب کے نکلنے کے وقت سے نماز جمعہ سے فارغ ہونے تک۔ تشریح : جمعہ کے دن خطیب خطبہ کے لئے نکل جائے اس کے بعد سے لیکر جمعہ کے فرض سے فارغ ہوتے وقت تک نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے کہ قرآن پڑھا جائے تو اسکو کان لگا کر سنو اور چپ رہو اور خطبے کے وقت بھی قرآن پڑھا جاتا ہے اسلئے اس وقت بھی کان لگا کر سننا ہوگا اور چپ رہنا ہوگا ، اور نماز بھی نہیں پڑھنی ہوگی، کیونکہ نماز پڑھے گا تو نہ چپ رہ سکے گا اور نہ سن سکے گا ۔ آیت یہ ہے۔اذا قرء القرآن فاستمعوا له و انصتوا لعلکم ترحمون ( آیت ۲۰،سورۃ الاعراف ۷) (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ امام خطبے کے لئے نکل جائے تو کلام اور نماز دونوں منقطع ہو جاتی ہیں۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عـن ابـی هــيــرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : خروج الامام يوم الجمعة للصلاة يعنى يقطع الصلاة و كلامه يقطع الكلام ۔ (سنن بیھقی، باب الصلاة يوم الجمعة نصف النهار وقبله و بعده حتی یخرج الامام، ج ثالث ،ص۲۷۴، نمبر ۵۶۸۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام کا نکلنا کلام اور نماز دونوں کو منقطع کر دیتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس وقت نماز بھی نہ پڑھے۔ (۳) تاہم اگر پڑھ لیا تو جائز ہے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمع جابر قال دخل رجل يوم الجمعة والنبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يخطب فقال اصلیت؟ قال لا ! قال قم فصل ركعتين . (بخاری شریف، باب من جاء والا مام يخطب صلی رکعتین ف خفیفتین ،ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۹۳۱) (۴) سمعت جابر بن عبد الله ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خطب فقال اذا جاء احدكم يوم الجمعة وقد خرج الامام فليصل ركعتين ۔ (مسلم شریف ،فصل من دخل المسجد والامام يخطب صل من دخل المسجد والامام يخطب فليصل رکعتین ، ص ۲۸۷، نمبر ۲۰۲۲/۸۷۵ وابو داود شریف، باب اذادخل والامام مخطب ،ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۱۱۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام خطبہ دے رہے ہوں اور سنت نہ پڑھی ہو تو دو رکعت پڑھ لے، اسلئے پڑھنا جائز تو ہے البتہ نہ پڑھے تو اچھا ہے۔
Translation: (317) (5) And from the time the khatib comes out for the khutbah until the Jumu'ah prayer is finished. Explanation: On Friday, after the khatib comes out for the khutbah until the fard of Jumu'ah is finished, praying nafl is makruh. Proof: (1) The verse: When the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent (7:204). Since the Quran is recited during the khutbah, one must listen and be silent, and cannot pray because prayer would prevent listening. (2) A hadith: When the imam comes out for the Friday prayer, he cuts off prayer, and his speech cuts off speech. (Bayhaqi) So do not pray at that time. (3) However, if one prays, it is permissible, as evidenced by the hadith: Jabir said a man entered while the Prophet was delivering the khutbah, and he said: Have you prayed? No, then stand and pray two rak'ahs. (Bukhari) (4) I heard Jabir: The Prophet said: When one of you comes on Friday and the imam has come out, let him pray two rak'ahs. (Muslim, Abu Dawud) So praying is permissible, but not praying is better.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding nafl during the Friday khutbah. The text states that from the time the khatib (preacher) comes out for the khutbah until Jumu'ah prayer ends, it is makruh to pray nafl. The proofs include: (1) Quranic verse 7:204 commanding silence when the Quran is recited, which applies to the khutbah. (2) A hadith that the imam's coming out cuts off both speech and prayer. (3) However, there is an exception: if a person enters the mosque during the khutbah and has not prayed the two sunnah rak'ahs (tahiyyah al-wudu' or sunnah of Jumu'ah), he should pray two light rak'ahs, as commanded by the Prophet. Thus, it is permissible to pray those two rak'ahs, but it is better not to pray any other nafl. The Hanafi ruling is that praying nafl during the khutbah is makruh tanzihi, but the two rak'ahs of tahiyyah are an exception and are recommended.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Friday prayer.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; but here it is qualified by an exception, indicating it is not strictly forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Nafl During Iqamah and the Exception for Fajr Sunnah
Ruling on nafl during iqamah with exception for Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on nafl prayer during iqamah and identify the exception for Fajr sunnah along with its condition.

Core Idea
Nafl is forbidden during iqamah except for Fajr sunnah, which may be prayed if you hope to catch the second rak'ah.

When the iqamah for a fard prayer is called, the congregation is about to begin. The strong recommendation is to join immediately. However, the sunnah of Fajr holds a special status, as it is the most emphasized sunnah prayer. This lesson clarifies the ruling and the precise condition that allows a brief delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is starting a nafl prayer while the iqamah for a fard prayer is being recited. The ruling is that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to do so.
This applies to all nafl prayers, whether sunnah or other voluntary prayers.
2
Note the exception
The only exception is the sunnah of Fajr (the two rak'ahs before Fajr fard). This sunnah is so emphasized that it may be prayed even during the iqamah.
3
State the condition for the exception
The exception is conditional: one must have hope of catching the second rak'ah of the fard congregation. If one fears missing the entire fard, then even the Fajr sunnah should be abandoned.
The phrase 'hope of catching the second rak'ah' means there is a reasonable chance that the congregation will still be in prayer when you finish the two sunnah rak'ahs.
4
Understand the rationale
The Fajr sunnah is the most emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and is strongly recommended even in the presence of the iqamah. This is a unique privilege given to Fajr due to its virtue.
Other sunnah prayers do not share this exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۱۸) [۶] اور اقامت کے وقت سوائے فجر کی سنت کے۔ تشریح : کسی فرض نماز کی جماعت کی اقامت کہی جارہی ہو تو نفل نہ پڑھے بلکہ اس کو چھوڑ کر جماعت میں شامل ہو جائے۔ البتہ فجر کی سنت اتنی اہم ہے کہ اگر فرض کی اقامت کہی جارہی ہو اور دوسری رکعت کے پانے کی امید ہو تو فجر کی سنت پڑھ لے۔
Translation: (318) [6] And at the time of iqamah except for the sunnah of Fajr. Explanation: When the iqamah for a fard prayer congregation is being said, do not pray nafl, but rather leave it and join the congregation. However, the sunnah of Fajr is so important that if the iqamah for the fard is being said and there is hope of catching the second rak'ah, then pray the sunnah of Fajr.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding nafl during iqamah. The text states that when the iqamah (call to commence the congregational prayer) is being recited, one should not start a nafl prayer. Instead, one should stop any nafl and join the congregation. The only exception is the sunnah of Fajr: because of its great importance, if the iqamah is called and one hopes to catch the second rak'ah of the fard, one may quickly pray the two sunnah rak'ahs first. This exception is specific to Fajr. The ruling is makruh tanzihi for other nafl prayers during iqamah.

Key Terms
اقامت (iqamah): The second call to prayer recited just before the congregation stands for the fard prayer.
سنت فجر (sunnah fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah before the fard of Fajr, considered highly emphasized (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Praying Nafl During the Friday Sermon: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling with proofs on nafl during Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nafl during the Friday sermon, identify the proofs (Quran and Hadith) used, and distinguish between the general prohibition and the exception for tahiyyat al-masjid.

Core Idea
Praying nafl during the Friday sermon is makruh tanzih — valid but disliked — because listening is obligatory.

This passage explains the legal ruling and reasoning behind praying supererogatory (nafl) prayers during the Friday sermon. The Hanafi school holds that it is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked) to pray any nafl from the time the khatib steps out until the Friday prayer is completed. However, an important exception exists for the two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid (greeting of the mosque) or the Fajr sunnah, based on the Prophet's own instruction. Let's walk through the proofs and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: praying nafl when the khatib has come out for the Friday sermon. State the hukm: makruh tanzih (lightly disliked).
The ruling is specific to the time from the khatib's exit until the conclusion of Friday prayer.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (Surah al-A'raf 7:204) commands attentive listening and silence when the Quran is recited. Since the sermon contains Quranic recitation, this obligation applies, and prayer would conflict with listening.
This is a qat'i thubut (certain transmission) but zanni dalala (interpretation), as the command is general.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
A hadith in Sunan al-Bayhaqi states that the imam's coming out cuts off both prayer and speech, implying one should not start or continue prayer at that time.
This is a zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Understand the exception
In Bukhari and Muslim, the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed a man who entered while he was delivering the sermon to pray two rak'ahs (tahiyyat al-masjid). This shows the prohibition is not absolute; these specific prayers are exempted.
The exception applies to tahiyyat al-masjid and, by analogy, the Fajr sunnah if missed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Thus the relied-upon Hanafi position is that praying nafl during the sermon is makruh tanzih, but it is allowed and even recommended if one has not yet performed the two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid or Fajr sunnah.
The Shafi'i school holds it as permissible generally, based on the same exception hadith.

Chapter on Disliked Times. (317) And when the khatib comes out, until he finishes the prayer. (318) And at the time of iqamah, except for the sunnah of Fajr. Al-Muzani said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib,' then he said: 'Pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib for whoever wishes,' fearing that people would take it as a sunnah. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Salat Qabl al-Maghrib, p.192, no.1281) In this hadith it says that if someone wishes, he may pray. Translation: (317) [5] And from the time the khatib comes out for the sermon until the Friday prayer is finished. Explanation: On Friday, after the khatib comes out for the sermon until the completion of the Friday obligatory prayer, it is makruh to pray nafl. Reason: (1) The verse says: 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent,' and during the sermon the Quran is recited, so at that time one must listen and be silent, and one should not pray because if one prays, one cannot remain silent nor listen. The verse is: 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent, that you may receive mercy.' (Surah al-A'raf 7:204) (2) The hadith says that when the imam comes out for the sermon, both speech and prayer are cut off. The hadith is: From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam's coming out on Friday for the prayer cuts off prayer, and his speech cuts off speech.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Salat yawm al-Jumu'ah... vol.3, p.274, no.5687) This hadith states that the imam's coming out cuts off both speech and prayer. Therefore, one should not pray at that time. (3) However, if someone did pray, it is permissible. The proof is this hadith: Jabir said: A man entered on Friday while the Prophet (peace be upon him) was delivering the sermon. He said: 'Have you prayed?' He said: 'No.' He said: 'Stand and pray two rak'ahs.' (Bukhari, Bab man ja'a wa al-imam yakhutb... p.149 no.931) (4) I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When any of you comes on Friday and the imam has come out, let him pray two rak'ahs.' (Muslim, Bab man dakhala al-masjid wa al-imam yakhutb... p.287 no.2022/875; Abu Dawud, Bab idha dakhala wa al-imam yakhutb p.166 no.1117) This hadith indicates that if the imam is delivering the sermon and one has not prayed the sunnah, one should pray two rak'ahs. Therefore, praying is permissible, but it is better not to pray.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs (dalil) about praying nafl (supererogatory) prayers during the Friday sermon. The author, following the Hanafi school, states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray any nafl from the time the khatib (preacher) steps out to deliver the sermon until the Friday obligatory prayer is completed. The primary proof is the Quranic command to listen attentively when the Quran is recited (Surah al-A'raf 7:204), which applies to the sermon since it contains Quranic verses. The second proof is a hadith stating that the imam's coming out cuts off both speech and prayer. However, the author notes an exception based on authentic hadith: if a person enters the mosque during the sermon and has not yet prayed the two-rak'ah tahiyyat al-masjid (greeting of the mosque) or the Fajr sunnah, they should pray them quickly. This is derived from the Prophet's instruction to the man who had not prayed. Thus, the ruling is that praying nafl during the sermon is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) but not sinful; if one does pray out of necessity, it is valid. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the obligation to listen conflicts with the concentration required in prayer.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an act whose omission is better than its commission, but not sinful.
خطیب (khatib): The person delivering the Friday sermon (khutbah).
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is mustahabb (recommended).

Praying nafl during the Friday sermon is makruh tanzih, but an exception exists for the two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid or Fajr sunnah based on the Prophet's instruction.

Ruling on Nafl Before and After Eid Prayer
Ruling on nafl before and after Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nafl before and after Eid prayer, cite the supporting hadith, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The Prophet did not pray nafl before or after Eid at the musalla – thus it is makruh tanzih to do so.

Many students assume Eid prayer has sunnah prayers like Jumu'ah. However, the Hanafi school holds that it is disliked (makruh tanzih) to pray any nafl at the musalla before or after the Eid prayer. This ruling is based on the explicit practice of the Prophet. In this lesson, we will examine the textual proof, the Hanafi position, and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? Praying nafl (voluntary prayer) before and after the Eid prayer at the musalla. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked) according to the Hanafi school.
The text also mentions 'even if at home' as disliked, but this is a stricter view.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Abbas states that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs of Eid and did not pray before or after it. This is the primary proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's deliberate omission indicates that it is not recommended to pray nafl at that time. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) can indicate istihbab or karahah depending on context.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers it permissible to pray nafl before and after Eid at the musalla, based on a different interpretation of the same hadith or other evidence.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi should not pray nafl at the musalla, while a Shafi'i may do so. This affects the practice of congregants at Eid gatherings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۱۹) [۷] اور نماز عید سے پہلے خواہ مکان ہی میں ہو ،[۸] اور عید گاہ میں نماز کے بعد ۔ تشریح : عید کے دن عید کی تیاری کرنے کے لئے کوئی اور نفل نہ پڑھے، اور عید کے بعد عید گاہ میں نہ پڑھے تاکہ لوگوں کو یہ محسوس نہ ہو کہ عید کی نماز دوبارہ پڑھ رہا ہے۔ وجه : عن ابن عباس ان النبي الله خرج يوم الفطر فصلى ركعتين لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها ومعه بلال . ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوة قبل العيد و بعدها، ص ۱۵۹، نمبر ۱۹۸۹ مسلم شریف ، باب ترک الصلاة قبل العيد و بعدها فی المصلی بص ۱۳۵۶، نمبر ۲۰۵۷/۸۸۴ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب الصلوة بعد صلوۃ العید ، ص ۱۷۳ نمبر ۱۱۵۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید سے پہلے اور بعد میں بھی نماز نفل نہیں پڑھنی چاہئے۔
Translation: (319) [7] And before Eid prayer, even if at home, [8] and after it at the musalla. Explanation: On the day of Eid, one should not pray any other nafl to prepare for Eid, and after Eid at the musalla one should not pray, so that people do not feel that he is repeating the Eid prayer. Reason: From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) went out on the day of Fitr and prayed two rak'ahs, not praying before it nor after it, with Bilal. (Bukhari, Bab al-Salat qabl al-Eid wa ba'daha, p.159 no.1989; Muslim, Bab tark al-salah qabl al-Eid wa ba'daha fi al-musalla, p.1356 no.2057/884; Abu Dawud, Bab al-salah ba'd salat al-Eid, p.173 no.1159) From this hadith it is known that one should not pray nafl before or after Eid.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with a proof from the Sunnah regarding praying nafl prayers on the day of Eid. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh (disliked) to pray any nafl before or after the Eid prayer at the musalla (prayer ground). The text mentions an even stricter view that it is disliked even if at home, though some Hanafi scholars differentiate. The reasoning is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet did not pray any nafl before or after the two rak'ahs of Eid. This indicates that the Eid prayer has no associated sunnah or nafl before or after it at the place of prayer. The wisdom ('illah) given is to avoid the impression that one is repeating the Eid prayer. However, if one prays nafl at home before going to the musalla, some Hanafis allow it, but the text here includes 'even if at home' as disliked, reflecting a cautionary position.

Key Terms
عید گاہ (musalla): The designated outdoor or large prayer ground for Eid prayers.
نفل عید (nafl of Eid): Voluntary prayers associated with Eid; typically avoided according to this ruling.

A) Only at home.

C) Both at home and at the musalla.

Key Takeaway
Praying nafl before or after Eid prayer at the musalla is makruh tanzih in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice.

No Nafl Between Combined Prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah
Ruling on nafl between combined prayers with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nafl between combined prayers during Hajj and cite the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Do not pray nafl between combined prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah — follow the Prophet's action.

During Hajj, at Arafat and Muzdalifah, the Prophet combined Zuhr with Asr and Maghrib with Isha. A key question for pilgrims is whether they may pray voluntary prayers (nafl) between these combined prayers. The Hanafi school, relying on the explicit practice of the Prophet narrated by Jabir ibn Abdullah, rules that no nafl should be prayed between them. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, and the practical implications for pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is praying nafl (voluntary prayers) between combined prayers at Arafat (Zuhr/Asr) and Muzdalifah (Maghrib/Isha). The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) to pray anything between them.
The ruling applies both between the two prayers and after the second prayer (e.g., after Asr at Arafat).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah describing the Prophet's Hajj: 'Then he called the adhan, then iqamah, then prayed Zuhr, then iqamah, then prayed Asr, and did not pray anything between them.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud)
This hadith is a sound (sahih) report, but it is ahad (single-chain), so its epistemological weight is zanni.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's deliberate omission of any prayer between the two combined prayers indicates that doing so is not part of the established practice (sunnah). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's leaving off an act can indicate it is not recommended.
This is further supported by the fact that the regular sunnah prayers of Zuhr and Maghrib are also omitted.
4
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'is) permit praying the regular sunnah prayers between combined prayers, arguing that general permission for nafl remains unless specifically prohibited. The Hanafi school restricts this to follow the Prophet's specific practice.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi pilgrim will omit these prayers, while a Shafi'i may pray them.
5
Apply the ruling to both locations
At Arafat: between Zuhr and Asr, and after Asr, do not pray any nafl. At Muzdalifah: between Maghrib and Isha, do not pray any sunnah (including the regular two rak'ahs of Maghrib sunnah or Isha sunnah).
The same ruling applies to any nafl prayer, including tahiyyat al-masjid if one is in a tent or mosque.

ترجمه : (۳۲۰) [۹] ، اور عرفہ اور [۱۰] مزدلفہ میں دو نمازوں کو جمع کرنے کے مابین۔ تشریح : میدان عرفہ میں جب ظہر اور عصر جمع کرے تو دونوں کے درمیان کوئی نفل نہ پڑھے اور عصر کے بعد بھی نہ پڑھے۔ اسی طرح جب مزدلفہ میں مغرب اور عشاء جمع کرے تو دونوں کے درمیان کوئی سنت نہ پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله فسال عن القوم حتى انتهى الى .... ثم اذن ثم اقام فصلى الظهر ثم اقام فصلى العصر و لم يصل بينهما شيئا . (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۱۳۹۶، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ص ص ۲۷۰ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دونوں نمازوں کے درمیان نفل نہیں پڑھی ۔(۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مغرب اور عشاء کے درمیان سنت نہیں پڑھی ۔ قال دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله ... حتى أتى المزدلفة
Translation: (320) [9] And between the two combined prayers at Arafat and [10] Muzdalifah. Explanation: In the plain of Arafat, when one combines Zuhr and Asr, one should not pray any nafl between them, nor after Asr. Similarly, when one combines Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, one should not pray any sunnah between them. Reason: (1) We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... and he asked about the people until he reached... then he called the adhan, then iqamah, then prayed Zuhr, then iqamah, then prayed Asr, and did not pray anything between them. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p.1396 no.2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.270 no.1905) This hadith states that he did not pray nafl between the two prayers. (2) In this hadith, he did not pray sunnah between Maghrib and Isha... He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... until he came to Muzdalifah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding praying nafl (voluntary) prayers during the combined prayers at two key Hajj locations: Arafat and Muzdalifah. The Hanafi position is that it is not recommended to pray any nafl between the combined prayers (Zuhr/Asr at Arafat, Maghrib/Isha at Muzdalifah) or after them at these places. The proof is the action of Jabir ibn Abdullah narrating the Prophet's Hajj, where the Prophet did not pray any nafl between the combined prayers. This establishes a practice that is followed as a sunnah for pilgrims. The ruling is based on the idea that during these intense rituals, the focus should be on the obligatory prayers and other Hajj rites. The text mentions 'sunnah' specifically for Maghrib/Isha, indicating that even the regular sunnah prayers associated with these times are omitted to follow the Prophet's example.

Key Terms
جمع بین الصلاوتین (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers (Zuhr with Asr, or Maghrib with Isha) at one time, specifically during Hajj at Arafat and Muzdalifah.
عرفہ (Arafat): The plain where pilgrims gather on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah.
مزدلفہ (Muzdalifah): The area between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a pilgrim do regarding nafl prayers between combined prayers at Arafat?
A) Pray the regular sunnah before Zuhr and after Asr as usual.
B) Pray any nafl only if time permits.
C) Not pray any nafl between them.
D) Pray two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid.

Key Takeaway
At Arafat and Muzdalifah, the Prophet did not pray any voluntary prayers between the combined prayers, so the Hanafi school holds that it is better to omit them.

Disliked Times for Performing Optional Prayers
Rulings with proof on disliked times for nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four disliked times for nafl prayer in the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer is disliked at four specific times to prioritize fard and ensure khushu.

This lesson covers the four specific times when performing optional (nafl) prayers is disliked in the Hanafi school. The rulings are derived from authentic hadith and aim to preserve the significance of obligatory acts and maintain concentration in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four disliked times
Scan the passage to locate the four scenarios: before/after Eid prayer, between combined prayers at Arafah and Muzdalifah, when the time for an obligatory prayer is narrow, and when one is distracted by bodily needs or the presence of food.
2
Match each time with its hadith proof
For each ruling, find the hadith cited by the author. Note the sources (e.g., Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi) and the key phrases used.
The proofs include hadith from Ibn Abbas, Jabir, Abu Hurairah, and Aisha.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
Reflect on why nafl is disliked in each case: to avoid confusion of repeating Eid prayer, to avoid interfering with combined prayers, to ensure the fard is not missed, and to maintain khushu (concentration).
4
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Recognize that other schools may have different rulings (e.g., Shafi'i permits nafl before Eid in the mosque). This affects fatwa but not the core Hanafi position.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Consider how these rulings apply today, such as praying nafl in the mosque before Eid or performing voluntary prayers when one is in a hurry to catch the congregation.

Section on disliked times. (319) Before Eid, even if at home, and after it in the mosque. (320) Between two prayers being combined at Arafah and Muzdalifah. (1) Do not perform any nafl prayer. Its proof is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the iqamah is called for prayer, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' (Tirmidhi, Bab...). This hadith indicates that when the congregation is ready, there is no prayer. (2) The sunnah of Fajr is important, so he should pray it. Its proof is: From Aishah, she said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The two rakat of Fajr are better than the world and everything in it.' (Tirmidhi, Bab...). This hadith indicates that the sunnah of Fajr is more virtuous than the world. (3) Also in this hadith: From Aishah, she said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) did not emphasize any nawafil as much as he emphasized the two rakat of Fajr. (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that the sunnah of Fajr is muakkadah (emphasized) because he would emphasize it greatly. Translation: (319) [7] Before Eid prayer, even if at home, [8] and after it at the Eidgah. Explanation: On Eid day, he should not pray any other nafl in preparation for Eid, and after Eid he should not pray at the Eidgah so that people do not think he is repeating the Eid prayer. Proof: From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) went out on the day of Fitr and prayed two rakat, not praying before or after it, with Bilal. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith shows that nafl prayer should not be performed before or after Eid. Translation: (320) [9] Between combining two prayers at Arafah and [10] Muzdalifah. Explanation: At Arafah, when combining Zuhr and Asr, he should not pray any nafl between them, nor after Asr. Similarly, at Muzdalifah, when combining Maghrib and Isha, he should not pray any sunnah between them. Proof: (1) We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he called the adhan and iqamah, prayed Zuhr, then iqamah, prayed Asr, and did not pray anything between them. (Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that he did not pray nafl between the two prayers. (2) This hadith indicates that one should not pray sunnah between Maghrib and Isha: ... until he came to Muzdalifah and prayed Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and two iqamahs, and he did not glorify anything between them. (Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith shows that at Muzdalifah, nafl is not to be prayed between Maghrib and Isha. Translation: (321) [11] And when the time for obligatory prayer is narrow. Explanation: When the time for obligatory prayer becomes narrow, he should hurry to pray the fard so that it does not become qada. Therefore, he should not engage in nafl at that time. Proof: (1) 'Guard your prayers, especially the middle prayer' (Quran 2:238). This verse means perform prayers on time, so the fard time takes precedence, so he should not pray nafl at that time. (2) If the iqamah for congregation has been called, he should not pray nafl; then if there is risk of missing the prayer, it is even more so. The hadith is: From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When the iqamah is called for prayer, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' (Tirmidhi). This hadith indicates that when the congregation is ready, there is no prayer, so if there is risk of qada, he should not pray nafl. Translation: (322) [12] At the time of pressing need for urine or stool, [13] and when food is present and he desires it, [14] and any matter that distracts the heart and disrupts khushu. Explanation: If there is a strong need to urinate or defecate, or extreme hunger that eliminates khushu, then he should not pray nafl at such moments. Proof: He said: I and al-Qasim were talking with Aishah... I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'There is no prayer when food is present, nor when one is resisting the two impurities.' (Muslim, Bab...). This hadith indicates that one should not pray when needing to urinate, defecate, or when extremely hungry. Lexicon: 'Mudafa'ah' means repelling, where urine or stool is pressing so hard that one wants to quickly relieve himself. 'Akhbathayn' is derived from 'khabath' meaning impure things; here it refers to the need for urine and stool. 'Tawaqu' is derived from 'taqa' meaning desire or inclination of the heart. 'Bal' means heart.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof lesson from the Hanafi text Thamaratun Najah. The author lists four specific times when performing optional (nafl) prayers is disliked, along with their respective proofs from hadith. The first ruling (319) prohibits nafl before Eid prayer (even at home) and after it at the Eidgah, to avoid the appearance of repeating the Eid prayer. The second (320) prohibits nafl between combined prayers at Arafat (Zuhr and Asr) and Muzdalifah (Maghrib and Isha), as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not pray any voluntary prayers at those moments. The third (321) prohibits nafl when the time for an obligatory prayer is so narrow that it might be missed; here the priority is performing the fard on time. The fourth (322) prohibits nafl when one is distracted by a pressing need to use the toilet, intense hunger, or any other factor that would disrupt khushu (concentration) in prayer. Each point is supported by authentic hadith, and the author's commentary in Urdu explains the reasoning clearly. The Hanafi school holds that these prohibitions are based on the principle that nafl should not interfere with the performance of fard or with the proper state of humility in prayer.

Key Terms
الأوقات المكروهة (al-awqāt al-makrūhah): Times during which performing optional prayers is disliked according to the Hanafi school.
مدافعة الأخبثين (madāfa‘at al-akhbathayn): Pressing need to relieve oneself of urine or stool, which distracts from prayer.
خشوع (khushū‘): Full concentration and humility in prayer, which is a required state for validity and reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is a time when performing nafl prayer is disliked?
A) After Fajr prayer until sunrise
B) When the iqamah for congregation is called
C) During the last third of the night
D) After Maghrib prayer

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, performing nafl prayer is disliked at four specific times: before/after Eid, between combined prayers at Arafat/Muzdalifah, when the fard time is narrow, and when one is distracted by bodily needs or hunger.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Disliked Times for Nafl Prayer (Awqat Makruhah)
States and proves disliked times for performing salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions under which nafl prayer is makruh tanzihi according to the Hanafi school and cite the Quranic and prophetic proofs for each.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer is disliked when it risks missing the fard or disrupts khushu — the purpose of prayer is devotion, not distraction.

In this passage, the author identifies four specific situations in which performing nafl (supererogatory) prayers is considered makruh tanzihi (disliked) in the Hanafi school. The underlying reason is either the risk of missing the obligatory prayer due to time constraints or the loss of the essential spirit of prayer—khushu—due to physical distractions. Each ruling is supported by clear proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, demonstrating that Hanafi fiqh is built on textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four situations
Extract the four cases listed: (1) when the fard time is narrow, (2) when one is in urgent need of relieving oneself, (3) when desired food is present, (4) when any other thing occupies the mind and harms khushu.
These are the 'awqat makruhah' — times when nafl is disliked.
2
Determine the hukm level
All four situations render nafl prayer makruh tanzihi (disliked), not haram. The prayer is still valid if performed but reward is diminished and it is against the sunna.
Hanafi usul: negation 'la salata' in hadith indicates karahah, not tahrim, because other proofs show validity.
3
Trace the proof for narrow fard time
Quran 2:238 commands guarding prayers, i.e., praying on time. Hadith 'when the prayer is established, there is no prayer but the obligatory' (Tirmidhi) directly prohibits nafl when fard has started, and by analogy when fard time is so narrow it might be missed.
The imperative 'hafizu' indicates priority of fard over nafl.
4
Trace the proof for physical distractions
Hadith in Muslim: 'There is no prayer when food is present nor when one is fighting against the two filths.' This covers urgent need to relieve oneself and intense hunger. The negation indicates dislike due to loss of khushu.
The term 'mudafa'at al-akhbathayn' specifically refers to extreme urgency.
5
Apply the unifying principle
The common factor is the absence of khushu or the risk of missing fard. The rule: avoid nafl when these conditions exist. If one prays despite them, the prayer is valid but makruh.
This shows that Hanafi fiqh balances textual evidence with the spirit of worship.

Chapter on Disliked Times. Muzdalifah (321) and when the time for the obligatory prayer is narrow (322) and when one is fighting against the two filths (urination/defecation) and when there is food present that one's soul desires, and anything that occupies the mind and spoils khushu. He prayed Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and two iqamas and did not pray anything optional between them. (Muslim, Hajjat al-Nabi, p.515 no.2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.271 no.1905) This hadith says that in Muzdalifah one does not pray nafl between Maghrib and Isha. Translation: (321) [11] And when the time for the obligatory prayer is narrow. Explanation: When the time for the obligatory prayer becomes narrow, then one should hasten to pray the fard so that it does not become qada; therefore at that time one should not engage in nafl. Proof: (1) 'Guard strictly the prayers, especially the middle prayer' (Surah Baqarah 2:238). This verse says to guard the prayers, i.e., pray on time; therefore the time for fard takes precedence, so one should not pray nafl at that time. (2) (1) When the congregation's iqama has been given, then no one should pray nafl. So if there is fear of qada, then even more so one should not pray nafl. The hadith for this is: Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a idha uqimat al-salat... p.113 no.42) This hadith says that when the congregation is standing, there is no prayer; therefore if there is danger of qada, then also one should not pray nafl. Translation: (322) [12] And at the time of fighting against urine and stool [13] and when food is present and one desires it [14] and at the time of anything that occupies the heart and harms khushu. Explanation: If there is urgent urination or defecation, or very intense hunger that removes khushu and khudu, then at such a time one should not pray nafl. Proof: He said: I and Qasim were discussing with Aisha... I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'There is no prayer when food is present nor when one is fighting against the two filths.' (Muslim, Bab Karahiyat al-Ta'am bi Hadrat al-Ta'am..., p.226 no.1246/560) This hadith says that at the time of urgent urination, defecation, and intense hunger, one should not pray. Vocabulary: mudafa'ah: pushing away, urine or stool being so urgent that one wants to quickly finish. akhbathayn: derived from khubth, filthy thing; here meaning need to urinate or defecate. tatawwaqu: from taq, desire, inclination of the heart. al-bal: heart.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah discusses the disliked times for performing prayer, specifically nafl prayers, and provides the legal proofs. The author begins by listing the situations: (1) When the time for the obligatory prayer is narrow, meaning the remaining time is only enough to perform the fard itself. In such a case, one must not delay with optional prayers but hasten to fulfill the fard. The proof is the Quranic command to guard the prayers and the hadith that when the iqama is called, there is no prayer but the obligatory one. (2) When one is in urgent need of relieving oneself (urine or stool). This disturbs khushu and makes prayer invalid in spirit. (3) When food is present and one strongly desires it. The hadith explicitly says there is no prayer in such situations. (4) Any other thing that occupies the heart and harms khushu. The author uses these proofs to establish the ruling that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to engage in nafl prayers under these conditions. The vocabulary section clarifies key terms like mudafa'ah (urgent need) and akhbathayn (the two filths). This is a standard Hanafi position based on strong proofs.

Key Terms
الاوقات المكروهة (al-awqat al-makruhah): The times in which it is disliked to perform certain prayers (especially nafl) due to distracting conditions or conflict with fard obligations.
مدافعة الاخبثين (mudafa'at al-akhbathayn): The state of urgently needing to relieve oneself from urine and feces, which disturbs concentration (khushu) in prayer.
خشوع (khushu): Humility and attentiveness in prayer, which is required for the spiritual validity of salah; its absence due to distractions makes prayer disliked.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayers, as opposed to fard (obligatory) prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a disliked time for nafl prayer?
A) When the time for the fard prayer is narrow
B) When one is in good health and has no distractions
C) When the weather is hot
D) When one is in a state of wudu

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer is disliked in situations that threaten the performance of fard on time or undermine khushu, and the Hanafi proofs for this are rooted in both Quran and Sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Ruling of Adhan and Iqamah
States ruling of adhan and iqamah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of adhan and iqamah for men and women, identify the Quranic and hadith proofs, and apply the ruling to various scenarios.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for men, makruh for women; a woman's voice is 'awrah.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah establishes the legal status of the call to prayer (adhan) and the second call (iqamah) according to the Hanafi school. While many assume adhan is only for congregational prayer in mosques, the text clarifies it is recommended even for a person praying alone or at home. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between the categories of sunnah mu'akkadah and makruh, and appreciating the evidence from the Quran and mutawatir sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Understand what is being ruled: adhan and iqamah. For men, the ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah; for women, it is makruh.
Note that the ruling applies to the five daily obligatory prayers (fara'id).
2
Locate the primary dalil
Identify the proofs cited: the Quranic verse (Jum'ah 62:9) and the mutawatir hadith of Ibn Umar about Bilal.
The verse mentions 'when the call is proclaimed' – this establishes the concept of a call to prayer.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how each proof leads to the ruling. The verse indicates adhan is prescribed; the hadith shows the Prophet directly commanded Bilal to give adhan, demonstrating it as a sunnah.
The hadith also shows the consensus of the Companions in establishing the adhan.
4
Note the scope and conditions
The text states adhan and iqamah are sunnah for fard prayers whether one is alone or in congregation, on time or making up, traveling or at home.
This broadens the application beyond the mosque and jama'ah.
5
Recognize the gender distinction
For women, both are makruh because a woman's voice is considered 'awrah (need to conceal).
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; other schools may allow women to give adhan quietly or for other women.

(آیت ۹سورة الجمعۃ (۶۲) اور اس کے لئے حدیث متواتر یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر كان يقول كان المسلمون حين قدموا المدينة يجتمعون فيتحينون الصلوة ليس ينادى لها فتكلموا يوما في ذلك فقال بعضهم اتخذوا ناقوسا مثل ناقوس النصارى وقال بعضهم بل بوقا مثل قرن اليهود فقال عمر اولا تبعثون رجلا ينادى بالصلوة؟ فقال رسول الله يا بلال! قم فناد بالصلوة. Chapter on Adhan. (323) The adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for the obligatory prayers, whether one is alone or in congregation, performing on time or making up, traveling or at home, for men. Chapter: Regarding adhan. Necessary note: Adhan means announcement; in adhan, prayer is announced, hence it is called adhan. Its proof is from the verse: 'O you who believe! When the call is proclaimed for the prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (Surah Jum'ah 62:9). And for it there is a mutawatir hadith: Ibn Umar said: When the Muslims arrived in Medina, they would gather and guess the prayer time, but there was no call. One day they discussed this; some said use a bell like the Christians, some said a horn like the Jews. Umar asked: 'Will you not send a man to call for the prayer?' So the Messenger of Allah said: 'O Bilal! Get up and call for the prayer.' (Bukhari, Bad' al-Adhan, p.100 no.204; Muslim, Bad' al-Adhan, p.161 no.837/377) This hadith indicates that calling adhan for prayer is sunnah. Translation: (323) Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah whether alone, on time or making up, traveling or at home, for men; and for women, both adhan and iqamah are makruh. Explanation: For men, praying fard in congregation is better, so whether alone or with congregation, traveling or at home, qada or ada, adhan and iqamah are sunnah. For women, both are makruh because a woman's voice is also 'awrah, so she should not give adhan nor say iqamah. Proof: (1) A traveler should give adhan and iqamah; for this there is the hadith of Malik ibn Huwairith: Two men came to the Prophet intending to travel. The Prophet said: 'When you two go out, then give adhan, then let one of you lead the prayer.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Adhan lil-Musafirin..., p.104 no.630; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi al-Adhan fi al-Safar, p.57 no.205) This hadith shows that a traveler should give adhan and iqamah. (2) During the expedition of Khaybar, they were traveling and the prayer became qada, so the Prophet also ordered adhan and iqamah. Hadith: Abu Huraira said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Move away from your place that was overtaken by heedlessness.' He ordered Bilal, so he gave adhan and iqamah and prayed. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi man nama 'an salat aw nasiyaha, p.74 no.436) This hadith mentions adhan and iqamah in a journey, and that prayer was qada. (3) If one prays at home, one should also give adhan and iqamah; for this there is the hadith of Umm...
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the ruling of adhan and iqamah. The author states that both are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) for the five daily obligatory prayers for men, whether one is praying alone or in congregation, whether performing the prayer on time or making it up later, whether traveling or at home. This establishes that adhan is not restricted to mosques or jama'ah but is recommended for every man praying fard. However, for women, both adhan and iqamah are makruh (disliked) because a woman's voice is considered 'awrah (to be concealed) in the Hanafi school. The passage then provides proofs from the Quran and sunnah, including the verse of Jumu'ah and the hadith of Bilal, as well as specific proofs for travelers and those making up prayers. The hadith of Malik ibn Huwairith shows that even travelers should give adhan. The hadith of Abu Huraira about the Khaybar expedition shows that adhan is given even for qada prayers. The final proof (though cut off) indicates that adhan is recommended even when praying at home. This comprehensive evidence makes the sunnah nature of adhan clear for all men.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, announced to inform the community that the time for salah has entered.
اقامة (iqamah): The second call immediately before the prayer begins, similar to adhan but with added phrases.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized Sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged; leaving it is blameworthy but not sinful.
مکروه (makruh): Disliked; the act is not prohibited but performing it is contrary to the preferred practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling of adhan for women?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Makruh
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for men in all fard prayers, and makruh for women due to voice being 'awrah.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Adhan and Iqamah: Ruling with Proofs
Ruling on sunnah status of adhan/iqamah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for men and women, explain the evidence, and distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
Adhan is a confirmed Sunnah for men, not an obligation; for women, it is disliked.

The adhan and iqamah are well-known practices associated with the obligatory prayers. In this lesson, we examine their legal status according to the Hanafi school. We will explore the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, and understand why the Hanafis consider them Sunnah Mu'akkadah rather than obligatory, and why women are instructed not to perform them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the precise ruling for adhan and iqamah according to the Hanafi school. Note the different ruling for men versus women.
The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah for men and makruh tanzihi for women.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary proofs cited: the Quranic verse (62:9) and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar on the origin of adhan. Also note the additional hadith for specific contexts.
The Quranic verse is used as supporting evidence; the primary proof is the Sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith demonstrates that adhan is sunnah, not fard. The Prophet's command to Bilal was not in the form of an obligation, and the Companions initially discussed other methods, showing it was not divinely mandated.
The absence of punishment for leaving it further supports the sunnah status.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Contrast the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers adhan fard kifayah. Understand each school's evidence.
The dispute hinges on whether the command for adhan indicates obligation or recommendation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school considers the sunnah position as mufta bihi. The key is that the hadith indicate consultation and choice, not obligation.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is that leaving adhan is makruh, not sinful.

Source Text

باب الاذان
ضروری نوٹ: الاذان کے معنی اعلان کے ہیں، اذان میں نماز کا اعلان کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے اس کو اذان کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہے يايها الذين آمنوا اذا نودي للصلوة من يوم الجمعة فاسعوا الى ذكر الله. (آیت ۹سورة الجمعۃ (۶۲) اور اس کے لئے حدیث متواتر یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر كان يقول كان المسلمون حين قدموا المدينة يجتمعون فيتحينون الصلوة ليس ينادى لها فتكلموا يوما في ذلك فقال بعضهم اتخذوا ناقوسا مثل ناقوس النصارى وقال بعضهم بل بوقا مثل قرن اليهود فقال عمر اولا تبعثون رجلا ينادى بالصلوة؟ فقال رسول الله يا بلال! قم فناد بالصلوة. (بخاری شریف، باب بدا الاذان ، ص ۱۰۰، نمبر ۲۰۴ / مسلم شریف ، باب بداء الاذان ، ص ۱۶۱، نمبر ۸۳۷٫۳۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز کے لئے اذان دینا سنت ہے۔
(۳۲۳) سُنَّ الاذان والاقامة سنة مؤكدة للفرائض ولو منفردا اداء او قضاء سفرا او حضرا للرجال وكرهتا للنساء.
ترجمه : (۳۲۳) اذان اور اقامت سنت موکدہ ہے چاہے اکیلا ہو، یا ادا ہو یا قضا ہو،سفر ہو یا حضر ہو،مردوں کے لئے اور عورتوں کے لئے اذان اور اقامت دونوں مکروہ ہیں ۔
تشریح : مرد کے لئے جماعت سے فرض نماز پڑھنا افضل ہے اس لئے اکیلا ہو یا جماعت کے ساتھ ہو،اسی طرح سفر میں ہو یا حضر میں ہو، قضا نماز ہو یا ادا نماز ہو آذان دینا، اور اقامت کہنا سنت ہیں، اور عورت کیلئے دونوں مکروہ ہیں، کیونکہ عورت کی آواز بھی پردہ ہے اس لئے یہ نہ آذان دے اور نہ اقامت کہے۔ وجه : (۱) مسافر اذان دے اور اقامت کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن مالک بن الحويرث قال : أتى رجلان النبي لا يريدان السفر فقال النبي : اذا انتما خرجتما فأذنا ثم ليوء مكما أكبر كما ۔ ( بخارى شريف، باب الا ذان للمسافرين اذا کانوا جماعة الخ ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۶۳۰ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الاذان فی السفر ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسافر اذان دے اور اقامت کہے۔ (۲) غزوہ خیبر والے سفر میں تھے اور نماز قضا ہو گئی تو بھی آپ نے اذان دلوائی اور اقامت کہلوائی ۔ حدیث یہ ہے ـ عن أبي هريرة في هذا الخبر قال : فقال رسول الله : تحولوا عن مكانكم الذي أصابتكم فيه الغفلة ، قال فأمر بلالا فأذن وأقام وصلی ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب فی من نام عن صلوة أونسیھا ،ص۷۴، نمبر ۴۳۶) اس حدیث میں سفر میں اذان اور اقامت کہی گئی ہے۔ اور وہ نماز قضا تھی اس میں آذان دلوائی اور اقامت کہلوائی ۔ (۳) اور گھر میں نماز پڑھے تب بھی آذان دے اور اقامت کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ام ورقة الانصارى أن رسول الله كان يقول : انطلقوا بنا الى الشهدة فنزورها ،فأمر أن يؤذن لها و يقام و يوم اهل دارها في الفرائض - ( سنن بیھقی ، باب سنۃ الاذان والاقامة في البيوت و غیرها، ج اول ص ۵۹۷، نمبر ۱۹۰۹؎ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۶ فی الرجل یصلی فی بیتہ یو وزن و تقسیم ام لا ، ج اول ، ص ۱۹۹، نمبر ۲۲۸۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے گھر میں اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی۔ (۴) عورت کے لئے آذان دینا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن أسماء قالت قال رسول الله : ليس على النساء أذان ولا اقامة و لا جمعة و لا اغتسال جمعة و لا تقدمهن امرأة و لكن تقوم وسطهن - سنن بیھقی ، باب لیس علی النساء أذان ولا اقامة ، ج اول ص ۶۰۰ نمبر ۱۹۲۱ر مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ٣٢ في النساء من قال لیس علیھن اذان ولا اقامته ، ج اول ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۲۳۱۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت پر آذان اور اقامت نہیں ہیں۔
Chapter of Adhan
Necessary note: Adhan means announcement; in adhan, the prayer is announced, so it is called adhan. Its proof is from this verse: 'O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on Friday, proceed to the remembrance of Allah.' (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) And for it there is a mutawatir hadith: From Ibn 'Umar, he said: The Muslims when they arrived in Medina used to gather and guess the time of prayer, and there was no call for it. So they talked one day about that. Some said: Take a bell like the bell of the Christians. Some said: Rather a horn like the horn of the Jews. 'Umar said: Would you not send a man to call for prayer? So the Messenger of Allah said: O Bilal! Stand up and call for prayer. (Sahih Bukhari, Book of Beginning of Adhan, p. 100, no. 204; Sahih Muslim, Book of Beginning of Adhan, p. 161, no. 837/377). From this hadith it is known that giving adhan for prayer is Sunnah.
(323) Adhan and iqamah are a confirmed Sunnah for obligatory prayers, even if alone, whether performing on time or making up, traveling or staying at home, for men, and they are disliked for women.
Translation: (323) Adhan and iqamah are Sunnah Mu'akkadah, whether alone, performing on time or making up, traveling or staying at home, for men; and for women both are makruh.
Explanation: For a man, praying obligatory prayer with congregation is better, so whether alone or with congregation, similarly whether traveling or staying at home, whether making up or performing on time, giving adhan and saying iqamah are Sunnah. And for a woman both are makruh, because a woman's voice is also 'awrah, so she should not give adhan nor say iqamah. Evidence: (1) A traveler should give adhan and say iqamah; for this there is this hadith: From Malik ibn al-Huwayrith, he said: Two men came to the Prophet intending to travel. The Prophet said: When you go out, give adhan, then let the oldest among you lead you. (Sahih Bukhari, Book of Adhan for Travelers when they are a group, etc., p. 104, no. 630; Tirmidhi, Book of What has Come About Adhan in Travel, p. 57, no. 205) From this hadith it is known that a traveler gives adhan and says iqamah. (2) In the expedition of Khaybar they were traveling and the prayer was missed, so the Prophet had adhan called and iqamah said. The hadith: From Abu Hurayrah in this report: He said: The Messenger of Allah said: Move from your place where forgetfulness overtook you. He said: He ordered Bilal, so he gave adhan and iqamah and prayed. (Sunan Abi Dawud, Book of Who Slept through a Prayer or Forgot It, p. 74, no. 436) In this hadith, adhan and iqamah are mentioned in travel. And that prayer was a make-up, and he had adhan called and iqamah said. (3) And if one prays at home, he should also give adhan and say iqamah. For this there is this hadith: From Umm Waraqah al-Ansariyyah that the Messenger of Allah said: Go with us to the martyr to visit him, and he ordered that adhan be called for her and iqamah said, and he led the people of her house in the obligatory prayers. (Sunan Bayhaqi, Book of Sunnah of Adhan and Iqamah in Houses and Elsewhere, vol. 1, p. 597, no. 1909; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 26: Regarding a man who prays in his house, does he call adhan and iqamah or not?, vol. 1, p. 199, no. 2284) In this hadith, the Prophet prayed at home with adhan and iqamah. (4) Giving adhan is makruh for women. For this there is this hadith: From Asma', she said: The Messenger of Allah said: There is no adhan nor iqamah upon women, nor Friday prayer, nor Ghusl for Friday, nor should a woman lead them (in prayer), but she should stand in the middle of them. (Sunan Bayhaqi, Book of There is No Adhan nor Iqamah upon Women, vol. 1, p. 600, no. 1921; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 32: Regarding women: who said there is no adhan nor iqamah for them, vol. 1, p. 202, no. 2313) In this hadith, there is no adhan and iqamah upon women.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the legal status of adhan and iqamah. The author establishes that adhan and iqamah are Sunnah Mu'akkadah (confirmed Sunnah) for men for all obligatory prayers, whether performed on time (ada) or as make-up (qada), in travel or residence, and even if one is praying alone. For women, both are makruh (disliked). The author provides Quranic and hadith proofs. The Quranic verse (62:9) is cited as evidence for the call to prayer on Friday, and the hadith about the origin of adhan from Ibn 'Umar shows that the Prophet established adhan as a practice. Additional hadith are given to demonstrate that adhan is prescribed for travelers, for make-up prayers, for prayers at home, and that it is not prescribed for women. The Hanafi position is that adhan and iqamah are not fard but sunnah mu'akkadah, which means leaving them is disliked but not sinful. The proof from the hadith indicates the Prophet commanded Bilal to call, but it was not an obligatory command. The author also explains the reasoning for women: their voice is awrah, so raising it in adhan would be improper.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases announced at the time of obligatory prayers.
اقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer immediately before the prayer begins, similar to adhan but with minor differences in wording.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed Sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged; leaving it is disliked but not sinful.
مكروہ (makruh): Disliked; an act that is not forbidden but is better to avoid. Here it refers to tanzihi (slightly disliked).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of adhan for women?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Makruh
C) Mubah
D) Fard kifayah

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqamah are Sunnah Mu'akkadah for men and Makruh Tanzihi for women; leaving them does not invalidate the prayer.

Wording of Adhan: Four Takbirs and Doubled Phrases
Enumeration of adhan phrases with repetition counts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact 15 phrases of the Hanafi adhan, identifying which are repeated twice and which once, and explain the absence of tarji'.

Core Idea
The Hanafi adhan has 15 phrases: four takbirs at start, all phrases twice except final tahlil once — no tarji'.

The adhan (call to prayer) is a sunnah mu'akkadah with a specific wording established by the Prophet's approval of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd's dream. In this lesson, you will memorise the exact structure of the Hanafi adhan, noting the number of repetitions and the absence of tarji' (soft repetition of shahadah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall structure
The adhan consists of a beginning (four takbirs), a middle (all other phrases repeated twice), and an end (one 'La ilaha illallah').
The total number of phrases is 15.
2
List each phrase and its repetition count
Write down the phrases in order: Allahu Akbar (4x), ashhadu an la ilaha illallah (2x), ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah (2x), Hayya 'alas-salah (2x), Hayya 'alal-falah (2x), Allahu Akbar (2x), La ilaha illallah (1x).
Memorise the sequence and counts.
3
Verify with the hadith evidence
Read the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd to confirm the exact wording and repetition pattern.
The hadith is the primary source and shows no tarji'.
4
Contrast with other schools
Note that the Shafi'i school includes tarji' (repeating shahadah softly before raising the voice), while the Hanafi school does not.
This difference affects the total number of phrases and the method of delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۲۴) اذان کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ شروع میں چار مرتبہ اللہ اکبر کہے، اور باقی الفاظ آخیر تک دودومرتبہ کہے (اس کے بعد ایک بار لا اله الا الله " کہے) تشریح : آذان کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ شروع میں چار مرتبہ اللہ اکبر کہے، اور باقی جتنے الفاظ ہیں وہ دودومرتبہ کہے، اور اخیر میں ایک مرتبہ لا اله الا الله کہے اور کل الفاظ ۱۵ ہو جائیں گے۔
وجه : حدثنی ابی عبد الله بن زيد قال : لما امر رسول الله بالناقوس يعمل ليضرب به للناس لجمع الصلوة ، طاف بي ، و أنا نائم ، رجل يحمل ناقوساً في يده ، فقلت : يا عبد الله ! أتبيع الناقوس ؟ قال : ما تصنع به ؟ فقلت : ندعو به الى الصلوة ، قال : افلا أدلك على ما هو خير من ذالك؟ فقلت له بلی ، قال : فقال تقول : الله اكبر ، الله اکبر : الله اکبر، الله اکبر ، اشهد ان لا اله الا الله ، اشهد ان لا اله الا الله اشهد ان محمدا رسول الله اشهد ان محمدا رسول الله ، حي على الصلاة ، ، حي على الصلاة ، حي على الفلاح ، حی على الفلاح ، الله اکبر ، الله اکبر ، لا اله الا الله . (ابوداود شریف، باب کیف الا ذان ،ص ۷۸، نمبر ۴۹۹ را بن ماجہ شریف ، باب بدء بدء الاذان ص ۱۰۰ نمبر ۷۰۶) اس حدیث میں تفصیل موجود ہے، اور اس میں ترجیع بھی نہیں ہے، اور کل ۱۵ کلمات ہیں۔
Translation: (324) The method of adhan is that at the beginning he says 'Allahu Akbar' four times, and the remaining words until the end he says twice (after that he says 'La ilaha illallah' once). Explanation: The method of adhan is that at the beginning he says 'Allahu Akbar' four times, and all the remaining words he says twice, and at the end he says 'La ilaha illallah' once, and the total words become 15. Evidence: My father 'Abdullah ibn Zayd narrated to me: When the Messenger of Allah ordered the bell to be made to strike for gathering the people for prayer, I saw in a dream a man carrying a bell in his hand. I said: O slave of Allah, will you sell the bell? He said: What will you do with it? I said: We call to prayer with it. He said: Shall I guide you to something better than that? I said: Yes. He said: Say: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar. Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah, Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah. Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah. Hayya 'alas-salah, Hayya 'alas-salah. Hayya 'alal-falah, Hayya 'alal-falah. Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar. La ilaha illallah. (Sunan Abi Dawud, Book of How the Adhan is, p. 78, no. 499; Ibn Majah, Book of Beginning of Adhan, p. 100, no. 706). In this hadith there is detail, and there is no tarji' in it, and the total words are 15.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage describes the specific wording of the adhan as established in the Hanafi school. The author states that the adhan consists of 15 phrases: four takbirs at the beginning, then the shahadah (Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah) twice, the shahadah for Muhammad (Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah) twice, 'Hayya 'alas-salah' twice, 'Hayya 'alal-falah' twice, two more takbirs, and finally one 'La ilaha illallah'. The hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Zayd, which is a dream but approved by the Prophet, is the primary evidence for this wording. The author emphasizes that there is no tarji' (i.e., repeating shahadah in a low voice before raising it) in this adhan. This is the standard Hanafi practice, differing from the Shafi'i school which includes tarji'.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'. In adhan, it is repeated four times at the beginning and twice near the end.
ترجیع (tarji'): Repeating the shahadah in a low voice before raising it; the Hanafi school does not include this in adhan.
شہادتین (shahadatayn): The two testimonies: 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah' and 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 20

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi adhan consists of exactly 15 phrases: 4 takbirs at start, all other phrases twice except the final tahlil once, with no tarji'.
