No Tarji' in the Shahadatayn of Adhan
Ruling statement on tarji' in adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tarji' in adhan and distinguish it from the Shafi'i practice.

Core Idea
Tarji' in the shahadatayn is not part of the Hanafi adhan; it is a Shafi'i sunnah.

This lesson clarifies an important difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i adhan. The term tarji' refers to repeating the shahadah in a low voice before raising it. The Hanafi school holds that this practice is not part of the sunnah adhan, while the Shafi'is include it. Understanding this helps preserve the correct form of adhan according to the Hanafi methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled
The act in question is tarji' in the shahadatayn (the two testimonies) of the adhan. Recognize that this is a specific practice within the adhan.
2
Define tarji' precisely
Tarji' means to repeat the shahadah in a low voice first, then aloud. This is distinct from simply saying the shahadah twice in a normal voice.
3
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school states that there is no tarji' in the shahadatayn of the adhan. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is to not practice it.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Note the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school includes tarji' as a sunnah of the adhan. This is a legitimate difference of opinion.
Some narrations from Imam Muhammad allowed it, but the majority rejected it.
5
Understand the authority
The Hanafi position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon view. Any addition of tarji' is considered a deviation from the sunnah practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۲۵) شہادتین میں ترجیع نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : ترجیع کا ترجمہ ہے لوٹانا، یہاں مراد ہے شہادتین یعنی اشهد ان لا اله الا الله ، اور اشهد ان محمدا
Translation: (325) There is no tarji' in the shahadatayn. Explanation: Tarji' means to repeat; here it refers to the shahadatayn i.e., 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah' and 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan'.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This brief passage clarifies that there is no tarji' (repetition in a low voice) in the two testimonies (shahadatayn) of the adhan. The Hanafi school does not include tarji' as part of the adhan, unlike the Shafi'i school. Tarji' means to say the shahadah quietly first and then repeat it loudly. The text states that in the Hanafi adhan the shahadatayn are said only once each (but actually twice in the adhan? Wait, the earlier lesson said they are said twice each. Here tarji' is a separate issue. Tarji' is about saying the shahadah in a low voice before raising it. The Hanafi adhan says the shahadah twice each, but without the low voice repetition. The lesson emphasizes that there is no such practice. The author likely included this to prevent confusion with the Shafi'i practice.

Key Terms
ترجیع (tarji'): The act of repeating the shahadah in a low voice before saying it aloud in adhan. Hanafis do not practice this.
شہادتین (shahadatayn): The two testimonies of faith: 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah' and 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi adhan does not include tarji'; the shahadatayn are said twice each without low-voice repetition.

Adhan is Disliked for Women
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women giving adhan, identify the supporting hadith, and explain why it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) rather than invalid.

Core Idea
Women's adhan is valid but disliked – the adhan is a public office not prescribed for women.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that it is makruh for women to perform the adhan. The ruling is based on a prophetic hadith explicitly removing the obligation of adhan from women. We will analyze the textual evidence, the school's reasoning, and the practical implications for women's involvement in the call to prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the grammatical form 'kariha' (disliked) and determine the exact hukm level: makruh tanzihi, meaning the act is valid but contrary to the sunnah.
The word 'kariha' in Hanafi fiqh usually indicates makruh tanzihi unless otherwise specified.
2
Identify the dalil
Locate the proof: the hadith narrated by Asma bint Yazid. Note the source (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) and its chain. The hadith states 'ليس على النساء أذان ولا إقامة'.
This is a hadith ahad (single narration), giving zanni (probable) knowledge.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the phrase 'ليس على النساء أذان' indicates dislike. Negation of obligation does not necessarily mean prohibition; the context of other injunctions (e.g., not leading men) suggests that adhan is not a woman's role, thus makruh.
The word 'ليس' here negates prescription, not validity.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school permits women's adhan without dislike, based on a different interpretation of the same hadith. Understand the basis of their view.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the broader Sunni tradition.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi relied-upon position is that adhan is makruh for women but if performed, it is valid and the prayer is acceptable.
The tarjih is based on the explicit wording and the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking pretexts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره للنساء. عن أسماء قالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ليس على النساء أذان ولا إقامة ولا جمعة ولا اغتسال جمعة ولا تقدمهن امرأة ولكن تقوم وسطهن. (سنن البيهقي، باب ليس على النساء أذان ولا إقامة، ج1 ص600، رقم 1921؛ مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، 32 في النساء من قال ليس عليهن أذان ولا إقامة، ج1 ص202، رقم 2313).
And it is disliked for women. From Asma who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Upon women there is no adhan, no iqamah, no Friday prayer, no ghusl for Friday, and a woman does not lead men; rather she stands in the middle of them.'
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that it is makruh for women to give the adhan. The proof is a hadith from Asma bint Yazid (or Asma bint Abi Bakr) where the Prophet explicitly states that women are not required to perform adhan or iqamah. The ruling is based on the principle that the adhan is a public announcement for congregation, which is not expected of women. The Hanafi position is that women may give adhan silently for themselves but it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) for them to do so loudly or in the presence of men.

Key Terms
كره (kariha): Disliked; an action that is discouraged but not sinful (makruh tanzihi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on women giving the adhan?
A) It is wajib upon women.
B) It is makruh (disliked) for women.
C) It is haram (forbidden) for women.
D) It is sunnah mu'akkadah for women.

Key Takeaway
Women's adhan is valid but makruh tanzihi; it is not required and is discouraged due to its public nature.

The Iqamah is Like the Adhan
Explains iqamah wording and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the wording of iqamah, cite the supporting hadith, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, the iqamah is recited exactly like the adhan except for adding 'qad qamat as-salah' twice after 'hayya ala al-falah'.

This lesson examines the wording of the iqamah (the second call to prayer) according to the Hanafi school. The passage affirms that the iqamah follows the same pattern as the adhan—each phrase is recited twice—with a single addition: 'qad qamat as-salah' after 'hayya ala al-falah'. The Hanafis rely on explicit hadith evidence, while the Shafi'i school holds that iqamah phrases are said only once. Understanding this difference is essential for proper congregational prayer practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the recitation of the iqamah. Its ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah). The specific wording and repetition are part of the sunnah as transmitted from the Prophet (s.a.w.).
The iqamah is not fard; it is a highly recommended sunnah.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
Two hadith are cited: (1) From Abdullah ibn Zaid: the adhan and iqamah of the Prophet were in pairs (shaf'an). (2) From Ibn Abi Layla: he recited the iqamah like the adhan, adding 'qad qamat as-salah'.
These are considered sahih evidence by the Hanafis.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith establishes that the iqamah, like the adhan, has each phrase repeated twice. The second hadith explicitly shows the addition of 'qad qamat as-salah' after 'hayya ala al-falah'. Together they form the complete Hanafi iqamah wording.
The doubling (shaf'an) is a key feature distinguishing from the Shafi'i view.
4
Note the opposing school
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the iqamah phrases are said once (fardi), meaning each phrase is recited a single time. He relies on other hadith or the practice of the people of Medina.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the sunnah.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
Thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis recite 11 phrases (counting the doubled phrases and the addition), while Shafi'is recite fewer (typically 7 phrases). This affects congregational prayer if a muadhdhin follows a different school.
The mufta bihi within the Hanafi school is the position stated in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاقامة مثله۔ ہاں حی علی الفلاح کے بعد قد قامت الصلوة دوبار زیادہ کہے۔ تشریح: امام شافعی کے یہاں اقامت فردی فردی ہے، دو دو مرتبہ نہیں ہے، اور حنفیہ کے یہاں اقامت بھی اذان کی طرح ہے، البتہ جی علی فلاح کے بعد قد قامت الصلوۃ، زیادہ کرے۔ جس سے کل کلمات سے ہوتے ہیں۔ وجه: (۱) اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن زيد قال كان اذان رسول الله الله شفعا شفعا في الاذان والاقامة - ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ان الاقامته من شنی، ص ۴۸، نمبر ۱۹۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اذان کی طرح اقامت بھی مثنی شنی ہے(۲) سمعت ابن ابی لیلی فاذن ثم قعد قعدة ثم قام فقال مثلها الا انه يقول قد قامت الصلوة (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب کیف الا ذان ، ص ۸۵ نمبر ۵۰۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قد قامت الصلوۃ، زیادہ کرے۔
And the iqamah is like it (the adhan). Yes, after 'hayya ala al-falah', he says 'qad qamat as-salah' twice. Explanation: According to Imam Shafi'i, iqamah is single (fardi fardi), not repeated twice; according to the Hanafis, iqamah is like adhan, except that after 'hayya ala al-falah' he adds 'qad qamat as-salah'. So the total words become... Proof: (1) The evidence is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Zaid who said: The adhan of the Messenger of Allah was in pairs, both in adhan and iqamah. (Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that iqamah is also doubled like adhan. (2) I heard Ibn Abi Layla: he gave adhan, then sat for a while, then stood and said the like, except that he said 'qad qamat as-salah'. (Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that he adds 'qad qamat as-salah'.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that the iqamah is recited in the same manner as the adhan, i.e., each phrase is repeated twice (masna masna), with the sole addition of 'qad qamat as-salah' twice after 'hayya ala al-falah'. The commentary highlights the disagreement with Imam Shafi'i, who holds that the iqamah phrases are said once only (fardi). The Hanafi proof relies on two hadith: the first from Abdullah ibn Zaid indicating the general practice of the Prophet (s.a.w.) of doubling in both adhan and iqamah; the second from Ibn Abi Layla specifically noting the addition of 'qad qamat as-salah'. The Hanafi position is thus that the iqamah consists of 11 phrases (considering the doubling and the extra phrase).

Key Terms
اقامة (iqamah): The second call to begin the congregational prayer, recited after the adhan.
شفع (shaf'an): In pairs, meaning each phrase is recited twice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'As-salamu alaykum'
B) 'Qad qamat as-salah'
C) 'Allahu akbar'
D) 'La ilaha illallah'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi iqamah is recited like the adhan, with each phrase repeated twice, and the addition of 'qad qamat as-salah' after 'hayya ala al-falah'.

Addition of 'As-Salah Khayrun min an-Nawm' in Fajr Adhan
Ruling with proof on tathwib in Fajr adhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tathwib and explain the two hadith proofs that establish it as sunnah.

Core Idea
Saying 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' twice in Fajr adhan is sunnah muakkadah, confirmed by prophetic approval.

The Fajr adhan holds a unique feature: after 'hayya ala al-falah', the caller adds 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' twice. This phrase, known as tathwib, is a distinct sunnah of the Hanafi school. This lesson examines the ruling and its two primary hadith evidences from Bilal and Abu Mahdhura.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the specific addition: 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' twice in the Fajr adhan. The matn also mentions 'qad qamat as-salah' in the iqamah, but focus on the adhan addition.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib or fard.
2
Analyze the first hadith (Bilal)
Read the hadith of Bilal: he came to the Prophet and said the phrase spontaneously. The Prophet approved and it became established. Note that the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) is a source of Sunnah.
The hadith is from Ibn Majah, thubut is zanni but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Analyze the second hadith (Abu Mahdhura)
Read the hadith of Abu Mahdhura: the Prophet explicitly instructed him to include the phrase during the adhan on the day of Hunayn. This gives direct prophetic command.
Darqutni records this, strengthening the proof.
4
Understand the Hanafi position
Based on these proofs, the Hanafi school considers the addition a sunnah muakkadah. It is specific to Fajr, not other prayers. The phrase is said twice, not once.
Some other schools view it as bid'ah, but Hanafis follow the hadith.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the mu'adhdhin should add the phrase after the second 'hayya ala al-falah'. Omitting it loses a sunnah, but the adhan remains valid. Adding it in other adhan is bid'ah.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲۷) ويزيد بعد فلاح الفجر الصلوة خير من النوم مرتين وبعد فلاح الاقامة قد قامت الصلوة مرتين . ترجمه : (۳۲۷) اور صبح کی اذان میں حی علی الفلاح‘ کے بعد الصلوۃ خیر من النوم دوبار زیادہ کہے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن بلال أنه أتى النبي عل يوذنه بصلاة الفجر ، فقيل : هو نائم ، فقال : الصلاة خيــر مـن الـنـوم ، الصلاة خير من النوم ، فأقرت في تأذين الفجر فثبت الامر علی ذالک ، (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب السنتہ فی الاذان ، ص ۱۰۳، نمبر ۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے حضرت بلال کو الصلاۃ خیر من النوم کہنے کے لئے کہا اور یہ ہمیشہ کے لئے ہو گیا ۔ (۲) سمعت ابا محذورة صلى الله يـقـول كنت غلاما صبيا فاذنت بين يدى رسول الله علم الفجر يوم حنين فلما بلغت حي على الصلوة،حى على الفلاح قال رسول الله الحق فيها الصلوة خير من النوم - دارقطنی ، باب ذكر الاقامة واختلاف الروايات فيها ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۸۹۹) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ صبح کی نماز میں الصلوۃ خیر من النوم کہنا چاہئے۔
(327) And he adds after the hayya ala al-falah of Fajr, 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' twice, and after the hayya ala al-falah of the iqamah, 'qad qamat as-salah' twice. Translation: In the Fajr adhan, after 'hayya ala al-falah', he says 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' twice extra. Proof: (1) The hadith: from Bilal that he came to the Prophet to inform him of Fajr prayer, it was said: He is sleeping. So he said: 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm, as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' and it was established in the Fajr adhan, so the matter became fixed. (Ibn Majah) This hadith shows that the Prophet told Bilal to say it and it became permanent. (2) I heard Abu Mahdhura say: I was a young boy and I gave adhan before the Messenger of Allah on the day of Hunayn for Fajr, and when I reached 'hayya ala al-salah, hayya ala al-falah', the Messenger of Allah said: Include in it 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm'. (Darqutni) So it is established that this phrase should be said in the Fajr prayer.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that in the Fajr adhan, after the second 'hayya ala al-falah', one adds 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' twice. The matn also mentions the iqamah addition of 'qad qamat as-salah' twice, which was already covered in the previous ruling. The focus here is on the Fajr addition, known as al-tathwib. The proofs are two hadith: one from Bilal showing that the Prophet approved of Bilal's spontaneous addition and made it permanent for Fajr; the second from Abu Mahdhura where the Prophet explicitly instructed him to include it. These hadith are considered strong evidence (dalil) for this sunnah. The Hanafis consider this addition a sunnah of the Fajr adhan.

Key Terms
تثويب (tathwib): The addition of 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' in the Fajr adhan.

The Hanafi school relies on prophetic approval and command to include 'as-salah khayrun min an-nawm' twice in the Fajr adhan as a sunnah muakkadah.

Reciting Adhan Slowly and Iqamah Quickly
Commands to recite adhan slowly and iqamah quickly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the manner of reciting adhan and iqamah, identify the hadith proof, and explain why it is mustahabb.

Core Idea
Adhan with deliberation, iqamah with haste — a recommended pattern, not obligatory.

This lesson addresses a common question: should the adhan and iqamah be recited in a particular manner? The source passage provides the Hanafi position based on a direct instruction from the Prophet to Bilal. We will examine the proof, the ruling classification, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage covers two acts: adhan and iqamah. For each, a specific manner is prescribed: adhan with tamahhul (deliberation) and iqamah with ihdar (haste). Note the hukm level is mustahabb.
Mustahabb means recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Jabir where the Prophet tells Bilal: 'When you give adhan, do it slowly; when you give iqamah, hasten.' This hadith is from Tirmidhi and is ahad.
Classify the hadith as Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command (amr) 'فترسل' and 'فاحدر' indicates a recommendation. In Hanafi usul, such commands are understood to indicate recommendation (nadb) unless there is a qarina that elevates to obligation.
No such qarina exists here.
4
Note the hukm level and cross-madhhab status
Hanafis classify this as mustahabb. Some other schools consider it sunnah muakkadah. The practical difference is minimal, but the epistemic weight differs.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲۸) ويتمهل في الاذان ويسرع فى الاقامة . ترجمه : (۳۲۸) اور اذان آہستہ ( ٹھہر ٹھہر کر ) اور اقامت جلدی کہے۔ وجه : حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر ان رسول الله علل الله قال لبلال يا بلال! اذا اذنت فترسل في ذلك واذا اقمت فاحدر - ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الترسل فی الاذان ، ص ۲۸، نمبر ۱۹۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اذان ٹھہر ٹھہر کر دے اور اقامت میں جلدی کرے۔ یہ مستحب ہے۔ لغت "تمل" ٹھہر ٹھہر کر بات کرنا۔ "ي سرع" جلدی کرنا۔
(328) And he should be deliberate (slow) in the adhan and hasten in the iqamah. Translation: And recite the adhan slowly (pausing) and the iqamah quickly. Proof: In the hadith: from Jabir that the Messenger of Allah said to Bilal: O Bilal! When you give adhan, then do it slowly (tarsal), and when you give iqamah, then hasten (ihdur). (Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that adhan should be given slowly and iqamah quickly. It is mustahabb. Lexicon: 'tamahhul' means to speak slowly; 'yusri' means to hasten.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling on the manner of recitation: the adhan should be recited with deliberation (tamahhul), meaning each phrase is stretched and paused, while the iqamah should be recited quickly (ihdar), meaning with haste. The proof is a hadith from Jabir where the Prophet instructs Bilal to do so. The commentary notes that this is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The lexicon clarifies the meanings of the key terms.

Key Terms
تمهل (tamahhul): To recite slowly with deliberation, pausing between phrases.
احدر (ihdar): To hasten, recite quickly without excessive pausing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The adhan should be recited slowly and iqamah quickly as a recommended practice, not an obligation; the calls remain valid if done otherwise.

Adhan Must Be in Arabic: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on adhan language

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on adhan in a non-Arabic language and identify the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Adhan in a non-Arabic language is invalid according to the mufta bihi, even if the meaning is understood.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses whether adhan can be delivered in Persian. While Imam Abu Hanifa permitted it, the Sahibayn argued that adhan, like Quran recitation, must be in Arabic. The text adopts the Sahibayn's position as the relied-upon ruling. Let us unpack the reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its source
The matn states that adhan in Persian is not valid, even if people know it is adhan. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah, the formally transmitted authority.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that adhan in Persian is valid if the meaning is conveyed, while the Sahibayn hold it invalid. The text sides with the Sahibayn.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn analogize adhan to Quran recitation: Quran is defined as Arabic in wording and meaning (citing verses). Since non-Arabic recitation invalidates salah, the same applies to adhan.
4
Understand the opposing view
Imam Abu Hanifa focuses on the objective of adhan—conveying the message—so meaning suffices even if wording is non-Arabic.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text adopts the Sahibayn's position, making it the operative ruling for fatwa. Adhan must be in Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲۹) ولا يجزئ بالفارسية وان علم انه . ترجمه : (۳۲۹) اور اذان فارسی میں جائز نہیں، اگر چہ اس کا اذان ہونا معلوم ہو جائے ، ظاہر روایت میں۔ تشريح : اذان کے عربی الفاظ کے معانی فارسی زبان میں ادا کر دے اور لوگوں کو معلوم ہو جائے کہ یہ اذان ہے پھر بھی ظاہر روایت یہی ہے کہ یہ جائز نہیں ، اذان عربی میں ہی ہونی چاہئے ۔ یہاں اصل اختلاف یہ ہے کہ عربی کے علاوہ میں قرآۃ کرے تو نماز ہو جائے گی یا نہیں، امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہو جائے گی، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نہیں ہوگی ، یہاں صاحبین کا مسلک اختیار کرتے ہوئے یہ فرمایا کہ اذان نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه : (۱) انکی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آیت میں عربی الفاظ کو قرآن کہا ہے، آیت یہ ہے۔ إنا أنزلناه قرآنا عربيا لعلكم تعقلون ۔ ( آیت ۲ ، سورۃ یوسف (۱۲) (۲)، وكذالك أنزلناه قرآنا عربيا و صرفنا فيه من الوعيد ( آيت ١٣،سورة ۲۰) (۳) ، إنا جعلناه قرآنا عربيا لعلكم تعقلون - ( آیت ۳ سورة الزخرف ۴۳) ان آیتوں میں قرآن کو عربی کہا ہے اسلئے عربی لفظ اور معنی دونوں کے مجموعے کا نام قرآن ہے۔ اس لئے جب قرآت دوسری زبان میں جائز نہیں ہے تو اذان بھی
(329) And it is not valid in Persian even if he knows that it [is adhan]. Translation: And the adhan is not valid in Persian, even if people know that it is adhan, in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). Explanation: If he conveys the meanings of the Arabic words in the Persian language and people know that this is adhan, still the apparent narration is that it is not valid; adhan must be in Arabic. Here the original disagreement is about whether reciting Quran in a language other than Arabic is valid for prayer. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is valid; according to the Sahibayn, it is not. Here, adopting the position of the Sahibayn, it is said that adhan is not valid. Proof: Their evidence is that the Quran is called Arabic in the verses: 'Indeed We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran...' (Surah Yusuf 2, Surah Ta-Ha 113, Surah Zukhruf 3). So the Quran is the combination of Arabic words and meanings. Therefore, when reciting Quran in another language is not valid, then adhan is likewise.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on delivering the adhan in a non-Arabic language. The matn states that adhan is not valid in Persian, even if the listeners understand it, according to the Zahir al-Riwayah (the formally transmitted position of the school). The commentary explains the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa held that reciting the Quran (and by analogy adhan) in a non-Arabic language is valid if the meaning is correct, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) held it is not. The text indicates that the mufta bihi (operative ruling) here is the position of the Sahibayn, so adhan in Persian is invalid. The proof is a qiyas (analogy) to Quran recitation: since the Quran must be in Arabic (as per Quranic verses), and adhan contains Quranic phrases, it must also be in Arabic. The verses cited establish that the Quran is Arabic in both wording and meaning, so merely conveying the meaning in another language is insufficient.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The formally transmitted narration of the school from Imam Muhammad's six books, considered the primary authoritative source.
صاحبين (al-Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid and recommended
B) Valid but disliked
C) Invalid and must be in Arabic
D) Valid only if no Arabic speaker is present

Key Takeaway
Adhan must be in Arabic; performing it in another language invalidates it, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

The Addition of 'Al-Salatu Khayrun Min al-Nawm' in Fajr Adhan
Ruling with proof for the two additions in Fajr adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the addition of 'الصلاة خير من النوم' in Fajr adhan and iqamah, and identify the hadith proofs that establish it as sunnah.

Core Idea
The phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is a sunnah addition in Fajr adhan, not wajib, confirmed by the Prophet's approval.

In this lesson, we examine the specific additions that distinguish the Fajr adhan and iqamah from other prayer calls. The Hanafi school holds that adding 'الصلاة خير من النوم' twice after 'حي على الفلاح' in the Fajr adhan, and 'قد قامت الصلاة' twice in the iqamah, is an established sunnah. The proof comes from authentic hadith narrations from Bilal and Abu Mahdhurah (may Allah be pleased with them).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the addition of specific phrases in the Fajr adhan and iqamah. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (stressed recommended act).
The addition is not fard or wajib; if omitted, the adhan remains valid.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Bilal (ra) and one from Abu Mahdhurah (ra). They are from reliable sources: Ibn Majah, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Daraqutni.
These are ahad hadith, so their indication is zanni (probable).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the Bilal hadith, the Prophet's approval (أقرت) indicates recommendation. In the Abu Mahdhurah hadith, the explicit command (الحق فيها) also indicates sunnah, not obligation.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-nadb (command indicates recommendation) unless qarinah specifies obligation.
4
Determine the hukm level
Because the dalil is zanni and the context shows the Prophet accepted it as a good practice, the ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
If it were wajib, the omission would require sajdah al-sahw, but that is not the case.
5
Note the scope and differences
These additions are specific to Fajr adhan and iqamah. They are not used for other prayers.
Some schools may have slightly different wordings, but the Hanafi practice is as stated.

ترجمه : (۳۲۷) اور صبح کی اذان میں حی علی الفلاح‘ کے بعد الصلوۃ خیر من النوم دوبار زیادہ کہے۔

Chapter of Adhan. (327) And he adds after 'hayya ala al-falah' in Fajr 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' twice, and after 'hayya ala al-falah' in iqamah 'qad qamati al-salah' twice. Translation: (327) And in the Fajr adhan, after 'hayya ala al-falah', say 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' twice extra. May Allah bless him. Proof: (1) This hadith: From Bilal that he came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) to call the Fajr prayer, and it was said: He is asleep. So he said: 'Al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm, al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm.' So it was confirmed in the adhan of Fajr, and the matter was established upon that. (Ibn Majah, Bab al-Sunnah fi al-Adhan, p. 103, no. 6; al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Tathwib fi Adhan al-Subh, vol. 1, p. 623, no. 1983). This hadith states that the Prophet told Bilal to say 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' and it became permanent. (2) I heard Abu Mahdhurah (may Allah be pleased with him) say: I was a young boy and I called the adhan before the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for Fajr on the day of Hunayn. When I reached 'hayya ala al-salah, hayya ala al-falah', the Messenger of Allah said: 'Add to it: al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm.' (al-Daraqutni, Bab Dhikr al-Iqamah wa Ikhtilaf al-Riwayat fiha, p. 244, no. 899). From this it is understood that one should say 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' in the Fajr prayer.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the specific additions in the Fajr adhan and iqamah. The ruling states that in the Fajr adhan, after the phrase 'hayya ala al-falah', the mu'adhdhin adds 'al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' twice. Similarly, in the iqamah, after 'hayya ala al-falah', he adds 'qad qamati al-salah' twice. This is an established sunnah. The proof is provided through two hadith: one from Bilal (ra) showing the Prophet's instruction and approval, and another from Abu Mahdhurah (ra) where the Prophet directly commanded the addition. These hadith are from reliable sources (Ibn Majah, al-Bayhaqi, al-Daraqutni). The passage then explains that this practice is confirmed and should be followed. The 'tathwib' (the addition) is specific to the Fajr adhan in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تثويب (tathwib): The addition of 'الصلاة خير من النوم' in the Fajr adhan.
اقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer, immediately before the prayer begins, with additional phrase 'قد قامت الصلاة'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that adding 'الصلاة خير من النوم' twice in Fajr adhan and 'قد قامت الصلاة' twice in iqamah is a sunnah, proven by authentic hadith, and its omission does not invalidate the call.

Pace of Adhan and Iqamah: Deliberate in Adhan, Quick in Iqamah
Ruling with proof recommending slow pace in adhan and quick pace in iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended pace for adhan and iqamah according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The adhan should be slow, the iqamah quick – a sunnah, not an obligation.

The adhan and iqamah are calls to prayer with distinct functions. This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on their pace, supported by a direct prophetic instruction to Bilal. Understanding this sunnah helps preserve the prophetic practice while recognizing that deviation does not invalidate the call.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage rules that the adhan should be recited slowly (tamahhul/tarsul) and the iqamah quickly (isra'/hadr). This is a sunnah (recommended) practice.
The ruling applies to both the mu'adhdhin and the reciter of iqamah.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah (ra) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed Bilal: 'When you call the adhan, proceed slowly, and when you call the iqamah, be quick.' This hadith is recorded by al-Tirmidhi.
The hadith is an ahad (single-narrator) tradition, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative verbs 'فترسل' (proceed slowly) and 'فاحدر' (be quick) indicate a command. According to Hanafi usul, an imperative implies obligation (wujub) only if there is no evidence (qarinah) diverting it to recommendation. Here, the context and lack of reproach for doing otherwise show it is mustahabb.
The Hanafi principle: 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub illa bi qarinah' but the qarinah here diverts to sunnah.
4
Determine the hukm level
The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah (emphatic sunnah) or mustahabb. It is not fard or wajib. The hadith is a strong recommendation, but the validity of the adhan/iqamah does not depend on pace.
The Hanafi position is that if one deliberately or accidentally recites adhan quickly or iqamah slowly, the call is still valid (sahih).
5
Note the consequence of opposite action
If the recommended pace is not followed, the adhan or iqamah remains valid. No compensatory act (like sajdah al-sahw) is required, but the sunnah is missed.
This differs from omitting a wajib element, which would require compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Proof: There is a hadith: From Jabir that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to Bilal: 'O Bilal! When you call the adhan, proceed slowly in it, and when you call the iqamah, be quick.' This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the pace of the adhan and iqamah. The ruling states that the adhan should be recited slowly and deliberately (tamahhul), while the iqamah should be recited quickly (isra'). The proof is a hadith from Jabir (ra) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed Bilal to be deliberate in adhan and quick in iqamah. The commentary clarifies that this is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The passage then provides lexical notes: 'تمهل' means to speak slowly, and 'يسرع' means to hasten. This ruling is based on the sunnah and is a recommended practice in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الترسل (al-tarsul): Deliberateness and slowness in recitation, specifically in adhan.
الحدر (al-hadr): Quickness and hastening in recitation, specifically in iqamah.

Adhan in Persian is Not Valid
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on adhan in Persian; ruling that it is not valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position that adhan in Persian is invalid and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute and its Quranic basis.

Core Idea
Adhan in non-Arabic is invalid because it is worship with fixed Arabic wording, not merely an announcement.

Adhan is the call to prayer, a central ritual in Islam. But what language must it be in? This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute: Is adhan valid in Persian (or any non-Arabic language) if the meaning is understood? The relied-upon position requires Arabic, and the reasoning connects to the nature of adhan as worship and the Quran's own description as an Arabic revelation. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify when form trumps function in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify that the dispute is about the validity of adhan in a non-Arabic language. Abu Hanifa holds it valid; Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it invalid. The mufta bihi is Sahibayn's view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both sides use different principles.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's dalil
They cite Quranic verses (12:2, 20:113, 43:3) that call the Quran 'Arabic'. For them, the Quran's essence includes both words and meaning, so recitation in another language is invalid. By analogy, adhan—as a form of dhikr and worship—must also be in Arabic.
The key phrase is 'قرآنا عربيا' (an Arabic Quran).
3
Contrast with Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa focuses on the purpose (maqsad): adhan is for notification and remembrance. If the meaning is conveyed, the objective is achieved, so the language is not integral.
His view is preserved in the nawadir but not acted upon in fatwa.
4
Understand the tarjih mechanism
The author says 'في الأظهر' (in the most apparent view), signaling that Sahibayn's position is the stronger, mufta bihi position in the school. This was settled by later Hanafi masters.
The term 'azhar' indicates a preferred view among conflicting narrations.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
In any masjid, the muazzin must recite the adhan in Arabic. If he recites in another language, the adhan is invalid and must be repeated in Arabic.
This applies even if all listeners understand the translation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲۹) ولا يجزئ بالفارسية وان علم انه اذان في الاظهر .
ترجمه : (۳۲۹) اور اذان فارسی میں جائز نہیں، اگر چہ اس کا اذان ہونا معلوم ہو جائے ، ظاہر روایت میں۔
تشريح : اذان کے عربی الفاظ کے معانی فارسی زبان میں ادا کر دے اور لوگوں کو معلوم ہو جائے کہ یہ اذان ہے پھر بھی ظاہر روایت یہی ہے کہ یہ جائز نہیں ، اذان عربی میں ہی ہونی چاہئے ۔ یہاں اصل اختلاف یہ ہے کہ عربی کے علاوہ میں قرآۃ کرے تو نماز ہو جائے گی یا نہیں، امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہو جائے گی، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نہیں ہوگی ، یہاں صاحبین کا مسلک اختیار کرتے ہوئے یہ فرمایا کہ اذان نہیں ہوگی۔
وجه : (۱) انکی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آیت میں عربی الفاظ کو قرآن کہا ہے، آیت یہ ہے۔ انا أنزلناه قرآنا عربيا لعلكم تعقلون ۔ ( آیت ۲ ، سورۃ یوسف (۱۲) (۲)، و كذالك أنزلناه قرآنا عربيا و صرفنا فيه من الوعيد ( آيت ١٣،سورة ۲۰) (۳) ، انا جعلناه قرآنا عربيا لعلكم تعقلون - ( آیت ۳ سورة الزخرف ۴۳) ان آیتوں میں قرآن کو عربی کہا ہے اسلئے عربی لفظ اور معنی دونوں کے مجموعے کا نام قرآن ہے۔ اس لئے جب قرآت دوسری زبان میں جائز نہیں ہے تو اذان بھی
دوسری زبان میں جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ بھی ذکر اور عبادت ہے،صرف اعلان نہیں ہے۔
(329) And it is not valid in Persian, even if it is known that it is adhan in the most apparent [view]. Translation: (329) And adhan is not permissible in Persian, even if its being adhan is known, according to the apparent narration. Explanation: If one renders the meanings of the Arabic words of adhan in the Persian language and people know that it is adhan, even then the apparent narration is that it is not permissible. Adhan must be in Arabic. The actual dispute here is: if one recites [Quran] in a language other than Arabic, does the prayer become valid? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it does become valid, but according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it does not. Here, adopting the position of the Sahibayn, it is stated that adhan will not be [valid]. Proof: (1) Their evidence is that in the verses, Arabic words are called Quran: 'Indeed, We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran so that you may understand' (Surah Yusuf, 12:2); 'And thus We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran and have diversified therein the warnings' (Surah Ta-Ha, 20:113); 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Quran so that you may understand' (Surah al-Zukhruf, 43:3). In these verses, the Quran is called Arabic, so the name 'Quran' includes both the Arabic words and their meaning. Therefore, when recitation [of Quran] in another language is not valid, then adhan [in another language] is also not valid, because it too is remembrance and worship, not merely an announcement.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of adhan in Persian. The ruling states that adhan is not valid in Persian, even if the listener knows it is adhan, according to the most apparent narration (al-azhar). The commentary explains the dispute: the original issue is whether reciting Quran in a non-Arabic language is valid in prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is valid, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold it is not. In this text, the author adopts the Sahibayn's position for adhan, considering it worship (dhikr and 'ibadah) and not merely an announcement. The proof from the Sahibayn is based on Quranic verses that describe the Quran as Arabic, implying that the Arabic wording is integral. Therefore, just as Quran recitation in another language is invalid, so is adhan. This reflects the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school regarding adhan.

Key Terms
الاظهر (al-azhar): The most apparent or stronger view within the school.
لا يجزئ (la yujzi'): It does not suffice; not valid.
صاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is valid only for the Fajr adhan

Key Takeaway
Adhan must be recited in Arabic; reciting it in any other language invalidates it, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Recommended Qualities of the Mu'adhdhin
Ruling stating recommended qualities of the mu'adhdhin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended qualities of the mu'adhdhin and explain why they are mustahabb based on the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The mu'adhdhin should be righteous, knowledgeable of Sunnah and prayer times—ideal but not required for validity.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah outlines the ideal qualities of the person who calls the adhan. While the adhan is valid even if the caller lacks these attributes, the Prophet ﷺ emphasized choosing the best among you. Let's examine the three recommended qualities and the evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selecting a mu'adhdhin. The ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) to choose one with specific qualities—not obligatory.
2
State the three recommended qualities
The passage mentions three: righteousness (salih), knowledge of the Sunnah related to adhan, and knowledge of the five prayer times.
3
Locate the dalil
Three hadith are cited: (1) from Ibn Abbas: 'Let the best among you call the adhan'; (2) from Abu Huraira: 'The mu'adhdhin is a trustee'; (3) from Abu Mahdhurah: 'The mu'adhdhin are trustees over prayer and suhur.'
All three are ahad hadith, so they indicate recommendation, not obligation.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'ليؤذن' in the first hadith is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) because obligation would be too burdensome. The second and third hadith emphasize trustworthiness, which implies knowledge of time and reliability.
5
Note the hukm level
These qualities are mustahabb (recommended). The adhan is valid even if the mu'adhdhin lacks them, but it is better to choose a qualified person.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

ترجمه : (۳۳۰) [۱] اور مستحب ہے کہ مؤذن نیک بخت ہو ، سنت کو جاننے والا ہو ، اور اور اوقات نماز کو جاننے والا ہو۔ تشریح : یہاں سے اذان کے لئے ۹ مستحبات بیان کر رہے ہیں۔ اور یہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ خود مؤذن میں یہ تین صفتیں ہونا مستحب ہے [1] بہتر ہے کہ مؤذن نیک بخت ہو ۔ [۲] دوسری صفت یہ ہے کہ آذان کے بارے جو سنتیں ہیں انکو جانتا ہو تاکہ سنت کے مطابق اذان دے سکے ، [۳] اذان کے پانچوں اوقات کو بھی جانتا ہو تا کہ وقت پر اذان دے سکے ، اس سے پہلے بھی نہ دے اور وقت گزرنے کے بعد بھی نہ دے۔
صلى الله
وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس قال : قال رسول الله له : ليوء ذن لكم خياركم و ليوء مكم قراوء کم ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب من أحق بالا مامه ، ۹۷، نمبر ۵۹۰ / ابن ماجہ شریف، باب فضل الاذان وثواب الموء ذنین ،ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۷۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تم میں سے جو اچھا ہو وہ اذان دے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن اللهم ارشد الائمة و اغفر للمؤذنين ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء ان الامام ضامن والمؤذن موتمن، ص ۵۸ نمبر ۲۰۷) اس اس حدیث میں ہے کہ موذن امانت دار ہے یعنی وقت پر امانت دار ہے، یعنی اس کو وقت کا پتہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ (۳) عن ابی محذورة قال قال رسول الله له امناء المسلمين على صلاتهم و سحورهم المؤذنون ۔ (سن بیہقی ، باب لا یوزن الا عدل ، الخ، ج ، اول، ص ۶۲۶ نمبر ۱۹۹۹) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ موذن نماز پر امانت دار ہے۔
Translation: (330) [1] And it is recommended that the mu'adhdhin be fortunate/good, knowledgeable of the Sunnah, and knowledgeable of the prayer times. Explanation: From here, 9 recommended acts for adhan are being explained. And he is stating that it is recommended for the mu'adhdhin himself to have these three qualities. [1] It is better that the mu'adhdhin be good and fortunate. [2] The second quality is that he knows the sunnahs related to adhan so that he can give the adhan according to the sunnah. [3] And he also knows the five prayer times so that he can give the adhan on time, neither before nor after. May Allah bless him. Proof: (1) There is a hadith: From Ibn Abbas (ra) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Let the best among you call the adhan for you, and let the best among you lead you in prayer.' (Abu Dawud, Bab man Ahaqq bi al-Imamah, p. 97, no. 590; Ibn Majah, Bab Fadl al-Adhan wa Thawab al-Mu'adhdhin, p. 104, no. 726). This hadith states that the good person should give the adhan. (2) From Abu Huraira (ra) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is a trustee. O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhin.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a an al-Imam Damin wa al-Mu'adhdhin Mu'taman, p. 58, no. 207). This hadith states that the mu'adhdhin is a trustee, meaning he is trustworthy regarding the time, so he must know the time. (3) From Abu Mahdhurah (ra) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The mu'adhdhin are the trustees of the Muslims over their prayers and their suhur.' (al-Bayhaqi, Bab la Yu'adhun illa 'Adl, vol. 1, p. 626, no. 1999). This hadith also states that the mu'adhdhin is a trustee over the prayer.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the recommended qualities of the mu'adhdhin. It states three recommended (mustahabb) attributes: the mu'adhdhin should be righteous (salih), knowledgeable of the sunnahs related to adhan, and knowledgeable of the prayer times. The commentary explains that these are among nine recommended practices for adhan. The proofs are three hadith: one from Ibn Abbas (ra) instructing that the best among you should call the adhan, another from Abu Huraira (ra) describing the mu'adhdhin as a trustee (mu'taman) over time, and a third from Abu Mahdhurah (ra) emphasizing the trustworthiness regarding prayer and suhur. These hadith establish the desirability of these qualities. The Hanafi school considers these attributes mustahabb, not obligatory; if a person lacking them gives the adhan, it is still valid, but the recommended practice is to choose a qualified mu'adhdhin.

Key Terms
مؤتمن (mu'taman): Trustee; the mu'adhdhin is entrusted with the prayer times and must be reliable.
صالح (salih): Righteous; one of the recommended qualities of the mu'adhdhin.
عالم بالسنة (alim bi al-sunnah): Knowledgeable of the Sunnah related to adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Being righteous
B) Being knowledgeable of the Sunnah
C) Being wealthy
D) Knowing the prayer times

Key Takeaway
The mu'adhdhin should ideally be righteous, knowledgeable of Sunnah and prayer times, but the adhan remains valid even if these are missing—the qualities are mustahabb, not conditions.

Wudu for the Mu'adhdhin: Recommended Not Obligatory
Ruling with proof on wudu for adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu for adhan and explain why it is mustahabb, not wajib.

Core Idea
Wudu for adhan is recommended; adhan without it is valid but less virtuous.

The call to prayer (adhan) is an act of worship and remembrance of Allah. Should the one who calls it be in a state of ritual purity? This lesson examines the evidence from the Prophet's hadith and the practice of early Muslims to determine the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (adhan) and what the ruling is (mustahabb/recommended for the mu'adhdhin to have wudu).
The ruling is a recommendation, not an obligation.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the primary evidence: the hadith from Abu Huraira where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'Let no one call the adhan except one who has wudu.'
The hadith uses a prohibition form (la yufa'il), which indicates karahah (dislike) in Hanafi usul when countered by other evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith leads to the ruling. The prohibition shows that adhan without wudu is disliked, not forbidden, because it is overridden by the athar allowing it.
The existence of a permissive athar (from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i) demonstrates that the prohibition is not absolute.
4
Note the ikhtilaf from the athar
Consider the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that states 'There is no harm if one calls the adhan without wudu.' This shows that adhan without wudu is permissible and valid.
The athar is a practice of a tabi'i, which provides practical evidence of permissibility.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Reconcile the two evidences: the hadith recommends wudu, the athar allows without. The Hanafi school gives weight to both, ruling that wudu is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory.
The athar prevents the hadith from being interpreted as a strict command, settling the ruling at the level of sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۳۱) [۲] اور موذن باوضو ہو۔
تشریح : اذان ذکر بھی ہے اور عبادت بھی ہے اس لئے وضو کر کے اذان دینا مستحب ہے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن ابي هريرة عن النبي الله قال لا يؤذن الا متوضی۔ (ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی کراہیتہ الاذان بغیر وضوء، ص ۵۶، نمبر ۲۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغیر وضو کے اذان اور اقامت کہنا اچھا نہیں ۔ (۲) اور اذان دینا جائز ہے اسکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے . عن ابراهيم قال : لا بأس أن يوء ذن علی غیر وضو ء ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، و فی المورذن یور ذن و ھو علی غیر وضوء ، ج اول ص ۱۹۱، نمبر ۲۱۸۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اذان بغیر وضو کے دے تو جائز ہے۔
Translation: (331) [2] And the mu'adhdhin should be with wudu. Explanation: Adhan is both remembrance and worship, so giving adhan with wudu is recommended. Proof: (1) There is a hadith: From Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let no one call the adhan except one who has wudu.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Karahiyat al-Adhan bi Ghayr Wudu, p. 56, no. 200). From this hadith it is understood that saying adhan and iqamah without wudu is not good. (2) And giving adhan is permissible; its evidence is this athar: From Ibrahim [al-Nakha'i] said: 'There is no harm if one calls the adhan without wudu.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab fi al-Mu'adhdhin Yu'adhdhin wa Huwa 'ala Ghayr Wudu, vol. 1, p. 191, no. 2189). From this athar it is understood that if one gives adhan without wudu, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the state of wudu for the mu'adhdhin. It states that it is recommended (mustahabb) for the mu'adhdhin to be in wudu, because adhan is both dhikr (remembrance) and 'ibadah (worship). The proof is a hadith from Abu Huraira (ra) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Let no one call the adhan except one who has wudu.' However, the passage also cites an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i indicating that adhan without wudu is permissible. The balance is that wudu is recommended but not obligatory; adhan without wudu is valid but less virtuous. This reflects the Hanafi position that wudu for adhan is mustahabb, not wajib.

Key Terms
وضوء (wudu): Ritual ablution; the state of cleanliness required for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid (batil)
B) It is valid but makruh/disliked
C) It is recommended
D) It is obligatory to repeat

Key Takeaway
Wudu for adhan is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory; adhan without wudu is valid but slightly disliked.

Facing the Qibla During Adhan
Ruling stating recommendation with exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hukm of facing the qibla during adhan and identify the exception for riders.

Core Idea
Facing qibla for adhan is sunnah muakkadah; riders may face their direction.

This ruling clarifies that while facing the Ka'bah is recommended for the adhan, it is not obligatory. The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah, meaning it is strongly encouraged but the adhan remains valid without it. The exception for riders accommodates practical necessity, showing the school's consideration of circumstance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the call to prayer (adhan). The ruling is that facing the qibla is mustahabb (recommended), not fard or wajib.
This applies to the mu'adhdhin while calling the adhan.
2
Determine the hukm level
The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah). Omission does not invalidate the adhan but loses the reward of following this sunnah.
Compare with fard (obligatory) which would invalidate the adhan if omitted.
3
Apply the exception
The exception is for a rider (e.g., on horseback or in a vehicle). The rider may face the direction of travel and is not required to face the qibla.
The exception is practical: turning on a moving animal or vehicle may be difficult.
4
Confirm the consequence if omitted
If the mu'adhdhin does not face the qibla without a valid excuse, the adhan is still valid (sahih) but he has missed the sunnah.
The adhan is not makruh or haram in such a case; it is simply less reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۳۲) [۳] قبلہ کی طرف ہونا مستحب ہے مگر یہ کہ سوار ہو۔
Translation: (332) [3] Facing the qibla is recommended unless he is riding.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This is a concise ruling stating that it is mustahabb (recommended) for the mu'adhdhin to face the qibla while calling the adhan. The exception is for a rider, who may face his direction of travel. This is part of the nine recommended practices for adhan mentioned earlier. The Hanafi school considers this sunnah; if one faces away, the adhan is still valid but the sunnah is missed.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'bah towards which Muslims pray.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act that is rewarded but not required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) If the mu'adhdhin is a rider
C) If it is the Fajr adhan
D) There is no exception

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla during adhan is sunnah muakkadah, not fard; riders are exempt.

The Mustahabbat (Recommended Acts) of the Adhan
Five recommended rulings for the mu'adhdin and adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five mustahabbat of the adhan and apply the principle that they are recommended, not obligatory.

Core Idea
Five sunnan complete the adhan; omitting them does not break it.

The adhan is a communal duty, but its perfection lies in emulating the Prophet's practice. This passage from the Hanafi matn outlines five recommended acts (mustahabbat) that elevate the call to prayer from merely valid to excellent. These rulings are based on hadith and the practice of Bilal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mu'adhdin's personal qualities
The text requires the caller to be righteous (salih), knowledgeable of sunnah and prayer times, and in a state of wudu. These are recommendations that ensure the caller is reliable and his call is respected.
The Hanafi school stresses knowledge of times to avoid calling at incorrect hours.
2
Note the orientation
Facing the qibla is the default, but the rider is excused due to difficulty. This shows the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj) in recommended acts.
3
Observe the voice amplification
Placing fingers in ears helps raise the voice, following the Prophet's instruction to Bilal.
4
Recognize the turning of the face
At 'hayya 'ala as-salah' turn right, at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' turn left. This is a physical emphasis on the announcements.
Only the face turns, not the whole body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاذان
اذان في الاظهر . (۳۳۰) ويستحب ان يكون المؤذن صالحا عالما بالسنة واوقات الصلوة ( ٣٣١) وعلى وضوء (۳۳۲) مستقبل القبلة الا ان يكون راكبا .
(۳۳۳) وان يجعل اصبعيه في اذنيه (۳۳۴) وان يحوّل وجهه يمينا بالصلوة ويسارا بالفلاح
Chapter of Adhan. Adhan in the most apparent [view]. (330) And it is recommended that the mu'adhdin be righteous, knowledgeable of the Sunnah and the times of prayer. (331) And upon wudu. (332) Facing the qibla unless he is riding. (333) And that he puts his fingers in his ears. (334) And that he turns his face to the right at 'hayya 'ala as-salah' and to the left at 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage lists five recommended acts (mustahabbaat) related to the adhan and the qualities of the mu'adhdin, according to the Hanafi madhhab. The rulings are based on the principle that the adhan is both a form of dhikr and an announcement, so it combines acts of worship with considerations of effectiveness. (330) The mu'adhdin should be righteous (salih), knowledgeable of the Sunnah regarding adhan and the correct prayer times, so he can give the call properly and on time. (331) He should be in a state of wudu because the adhan is an act of worship, as stated in a hadith: 'No one calls the adhan except one who is in wudu.' (332) He should face the qibla while calling, unless he is riding a mount, in which case his direction is excused due to difficulty. (333) He should insert his fingers into his ears to amplify his voice, as the Prophet commanded Bilal to do so, saying it raises the voice. (334) At the phrase 'hayya 'ala as-salah' he turns his head to the right, and at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' to the left, without turning his whole body, following the practice of the Prophet's mu'adhdin. These are all mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory; the adhan remains valid if any are omitted.

Key Terms
مؤذن (mu'adhdin): The person who calls the adhan (call to prayer).
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act; performing it earns reward, omitting it does not incur sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding the mu'adhdin facing the qibla?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) except when riding.
C) It is a condition (shart) for validity.
D) It is only recommended in the minaret.

Key Takeaway
The adhan is valid without any of these five acts, but performing them earns reward and follows the Sunnah.

Spacing Between Adhan and Iqamah: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof for spacing between adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the interval between adhan and iqamah and identify the primary hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
The spacing is a stressed sunnah measured by the time regular attendees need to prepare.

In this lesson, we examine the proper interval between the adhan and iqamah. Though it may seem a minor detail, the Prophet ﷺ explicitly instructed Bilal to leave a pause so that worshippers could finish eating or performing wudu. We will identify the ruling in the Hanafi school, understand the evidence, and see how it applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act under discussion (the interval between adhan and iqamah) and its legal classification in the Hanafi school (sunnah muakkadah).
The ruling is not wajib; it is a recommended practice.
2
Examine the primary hadith evidence
Read the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b where the Prophet ﷺ says to Bilal: 'Place between your adhan and iqamah a pause so that the eater can finish his meal...'
The command is an imperative, but its context shows it is for convenience, not obligation.
3
Understand the Hanafi derivation from the dalil
In Hanafi usul, an imperative indicates obligation unless there is evidence that it is for recommendation. Here, the Prophet's own practice and the context of facilitating worship confirm that it is a sunnah.
The imperative 'اجعل' is interpreted as nadb (recommendation) due to the surrounding evidence.
4
Apply the ruling to Maghrib prayer
For Maghrib, the pause is brief: the length of reciting three short verses or taking three steps, because delaying Maghrib is disliked.
This shows that the length varies by prayer time.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not emphasize a pause; they consider it permissible but not recommended. The Hanafi school adopts a clear recommendation based on the hadith.
The difference affects mosque practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويفصل بين الاذان والاقامة بقدر ما يحضر الملازمون للصلوة مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب (۳۳۶) وفى المغرب بسكتة قدر قراءة ثلاث آيات قصار او ثلاث خطوات. (۳۳۷) تشریح: اذان کے بعد فورا اقامت کہے گا تو لوگ جماعت میں حاضر نہیں ہوسکیں گے، اس لئے اتنی تاخیر کرے کہ جو ہمیشہ کے مصلی ہیں وہ حاضر ہو جائیں۔ وجه: (۱) عن ابی بن کعب قال : قال رسول الله الله : يا بلال اجعل بین اذانک و اقامتک نفسا يفرغ الآكــل مـن طـعـامـه فـي مهل ، و يقضى المتوضى حاجته في مهل (منداحمد ، حدیث المشائخ عن ابی بن کعب، ج سادس ،۱۷۳ نمبر ۱۲۰۷۷۸ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اذان اور اقامت کے درمیان فصل کرنا چاہئے ۔ (۲) ایک دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ اترنے والے فرشتے نے اذان کے بعد تھوڑی دیر کی اسکے بعد اقامت کہی۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن معاذ بن جبل قال احـيـلـت الصلوة ثلاثة احوال .... ثم امهل هنية ، ثم قام فقال مثلها . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب کیف الا ذان ، ص ۸۶، نمبر ۵۰۷رسنن بیھقی ، باب استقبال القبلة بالاذان والاقامة ، ج اول ص ۵۷۶، نمبر ۱۸۳۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اذان کے بعد تھوڑی دیر رک کرا قامت کہی۔
He separates between the adhan and iqamah by as much as the regular attendees of the prayer can arrive, while observing the preferred time. And in Maghrib, by a pause of the length of reciting three short verses or three steps. Explanation: If he says the iqamah immediately after the adhan, people will not be able to attend the congregation, so he should delay so that those who are regular worshippers can attend. Evidence: (1) From Ubayy ibn Ka'b: The Messenger of Allah said: 'O Bilal, place between your adhan and iqamah a pause so that the eater can finish his food leisurely, and the one performing ablution can complete his need leisurely.' (Musnad Ahmad, Hadith of the shaykhs from Ubayy ibn Ka'b) This hadith indicates that there should be a separation between adhan and iqamah. (2) Another hadith: The descending angel paused a little after the adhan and then said the iqamah. Hadith: From Mu'adh ibn Jabal: 'Prayer was prescribed in three stages... then he paused a little, then stood and said the like.' (Abu Dawud, Sunan Bayhaqi) This hadith shows that after the adhan he rested a short while and then said the iqamah.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommended interval between the adhan and iqamah. The author states that there should be enough separation for the regular worshippers to arrive, while observing the preferred prayer time. For Maghrib, the recommended pause is very short, just enough to recite three short verses or take three steps. The author provides two hadith proofs: first, the explicit command of the Prophet to Bilal to allow a pause for people to finish eating or completing wudu; second, the practice of the angel who paused slightly after the adhan. The Hanafi school follows this as mustahabb (recommended). The ruling applies generally, but for Maghrib the brevity is emphasized because delaying the Maghrib prayer is disliked.

Key Terms
فصل (fasl): The interval or separation placed between adhan and iqamah.
ملازمون للصلوة (mulāzimūn li’l-ṣalāh): Those who regularly attend the congregational prayer in the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How long should the spacing between adhan and iqamah be in Maghrib prayer?
A) Enough to recite three long verses
B) Enough to recite three short verses or take three steps
C) Equal to the time for the adhan
D) No spacing at all

Key Takeaway
The spacing between adhan and iqamah is a flexible sunnah measured by the need of regular attendees, with a brief pause for Maghrib.

The Ruling on Tathwib (Second Call) After Adhan
Ruling on making a second call after adhan to invite attendees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tathwib, identify its evidence from the practice of the Salaf and the hadith of Bilal, and distinguish the Hanafi view from the Shafi'i restriction to Fajr.

Core Idea
Tathwib — a reminder after adhan — is recommended in any prayer when heedlessness is feared, not only in Fajr.

You have learned the nine sunan of adhan. Now we turn to a related practice: tathwib, which is an additional call after the adhan to gather worshippers. The Hanafi school holds that this is commendable in all prayers when needed, based on the actions of the early Muslims. This lesson examines the ruling, its proofs, and how it differs from the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Define tathwib and its purpose
First, understand the linguistic and legal meaning: tathwib literally means 'returning', and technically means reminding people of the prayer again after the adhan. Its purpose is to alert the heedless and gather worshippers.
Hanafis derive the generality of the act from the word 'tathwib' itself, which implies repetition, not limitation to a specific prayer.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the hukm level: tathwib is a stressed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) in Fajr and recommended (mustahabb) in other prayers when there is need. The mufta bihi today is that it is commendable in any prayer, with wording like 'as-Salāh, as-Salāh, yā muṣallīn'.
This ruling is based on the practice of the Salaf and the need of the time, not on a specific textual command.
3
Analyze the evidence
Two proofs are cited: (1) The athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, who mentions that the mu'adhdhin of Ibrahim performed tathwib in Zuhr and Asr without objection. (2) The hadith of Bilal, who said 'as-salatu khayrun min an-nawm' in Fajr, and the Prophet approved it. The Hanafis use the first as a general license and the second as a specific instance.
The hadith of Bilal is zanni al-thubut but the Hanafis still act on it, and the athar of Ibrahim provides a qiyas for other prayers.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i view
The Shafi'i school restricts tathwib to Fajr only, with the specific wording 'as-salatu khayrun min an-nawm'. The Hanafis accept this for Fajr but extend it to other prayers based on the general practice and need. The practical difference is that Hanafis encourage tathwib in Zuhr, Asr, and Isha when people are heedless.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools respect the hadith but differ in its application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويثوّب كقوله بعد الاذان الصلوة الصلوة يا مصلين (۳۳۷) تشریح: تاب کا معنی ہے لوٹنا، تھویب کا معنی ہے دوبارہ نماز کی یاددہانی کرانا۔ ظہر عصر عشاء اور خاص کر کے فجر میں مثلا :" الصلوة الصلوة يا مصلين“ کہکر نمازی کو مسجد کی طرف بلانا اس دور میں بہتر ہے، کیونکہ اس دور میں ستی بہت ہوگئی ہے۔ ۔ یہاں تک اذان کے ۹ استحباب گنائے ۔ وجه: (۱) عن ابراهيم قال : كانوا يثوبون فى العتمة و الفجر ، و كان موء ذن ابراهيم يثوب في الظهر و العصر فلا ينهاه - ( مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۶ في التثویب فی ای صلاۃ ھو؟ ، ج اول ص ۱۹۰، نمبر ۲۱۷۵/مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب التخويب فی الاذان والا قامته ، ج اول ص ۳۵۴، نمبر ۱۸۳۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ دوسری نمازوں میں بھی یاد دہانی کرواتے تھے ۔ اسلئے اس دور میں وقت ضرورت یہ مستحسن ہے۔ خاص طور پر مدرسے کے طلبہ جلدی سے مسجد میں نہیں جاتے اسلئے انکے لئے ضروری ہے۔ (۲) اور فجر میں تجویب کا تذکرہ اس طرح ہے۔ عن بلال أنه أتى النبي الا الله يوذنه بصلاة الفجر ، فقيل : هو نائم ، فقال : الصلاة خير من النوم ، الصلاة خير من النوم ، فأقرت في تأذين الفجر فثبت الامر علی ذالک ، (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب السنتہ فی الاذان ، ص ۱۰۳ نمبر ۱۶ے رسن بیھقی ، باب التثویب فی اذان صبح ، ج اول ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۱۹۸۳ ) اس حدیث میں فجر میں تصویب کا تذکرہ ہے۔
And he performs tathwib, like saying after the adhan: 'as-Salāh, as-Salāh, O worshippers!' (337) Explanation: Tawb means to return; tathwib means to remind again of the prayer. For Zuhr, Asr, Isha, and especially Fajr, saying 'as-Salāh, as-Salāh, O worshippers!' to call the worshippers to the mosque is better in this era, because heedlessness has increased. Evidence: (1) From Ibrahim: 'They used to perform tathwib in Isha and Fajr, and the mu'adhdhin of Ibrahim would perform tathwib in Zuhr and Asr, and he did not forbid him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) This athar shows that they also gave reminders in other prayers, so in this time of need it is commendable. (2) As for Fajr, it is mentioned: From Bilal that he came to the Prophet to inform him of Fajr prayer, and it was said: 'He is asleep.' So he said: 'Prayer is better than sleep, prayer is better than sleep,' and this was established in the adhan of Fajr, and the matter continues thus. (Ibn Majah, Sunan Bayhaqi) This hadith mentions tathwib in Fajr.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on tathwib, which is a second call after the adhan inviting people to prayer. The author explains that tathwib means reminding people again of the prayer. While it is traditionally associated with Fajr (saying 'as-salātu khayrun min an-nawm'), the author extends it to other prayers in times of need, saying 'as-Salāh, as-Salāh, yā muṣallīn'. The proof is from the practice of the early Muslims (athar of Ibrahim) who performed tathwib in Isha and Fajr, and the mu'adhdhin of Ibrahim did it in Zuhr and Asr without objection. Also, the hadith of Bilal about Fajr establishes the specific wording for Fajr. The Hanafi position is that tathwib is recommended (mustahabb) especially when people are heedless, and it is not restricted to Fajr.

Key Terms
التثويب (al-tathwīb): Calling out after the adhan to remind people of the prayer, often with 'as-Salāh, as-Salāh'.

A) Only in Fajr prayer
B) In all prayers when there is a need
C) Only in Maghrib
D) It is never recommended

Key Takeaway
Tathwib is a recommended reminder after the adhan in any prayer when heedlessness is feared, supported by the practice of Ibrahim and the hadith of Bilal.

Dislike of Singing (Talhīn) in Adhan
Ruling with proof on dislike of melodious adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talhīn in adhan, identify the evidence from the Tabi'i 'Umar ibn 'Abdul 'Aziz, and distinguish between a recommended pleasant voice and disliked excessive modulation.

Core Idea
Talhīn in adhan is makruh; adhan must be simple and solemn.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on performing the adhan with a melodious, singing style (talhīn). The Hanafi school holds this to be disliked (makruh), based on the practice of the Salaf and a direct injunction from the Tabi'i 'Umar ibn 'Abdul 'Aziz. We will see how the school distinguishes between using a naturally good voice (which is commendable) and artificially modulating the voice like singing (which is disapproved).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the legal classification (hukm) is. The act is talhīn (singing style) in adhan; the ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text says 'wa yukrahu al-talhīn' – and singing is disliked.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Identify the evidence cited. The author quotes a narration from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'Umar ibn 'Abdul 'Aziz told a mu'adhdhin to give adhan plainly or leave.
This is a saying of a Tabi'i (qawl tabi'i), which is a source of law in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
Understand how the evidence proves the ruling. The command 'adh-dhin adhanan samhan' (give adhan plainly) implies that modulation is contrary to the desired simplicity, and the threat 'aw ulla fa'tazilna' (or else leave us) indicates strong disapproval.
The Hanafi principle: a prohibition (or strong discouragement) indicates karahah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Recognize that some other schools allow a certain degree of melody as long as the meaning is not distorted. The Hanafi position is stricter.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that excessive melody (tatrib) is makruh, while a pleasant voice without affectation is recommended. This is based on the practice of the Salaf.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره التلحين .(۳۳۹) تشریح: اذان میں کیا کیا مکروہات ہیں ان میں سے ۵ کو بیان فرما ر ہے ہیں ۔ پھر محدث کی اذان کے تحت ۸ آدمیوں کی اذان مکروہ ہے اس کو بیان کر رہے ہیں ، سب ملا کر یہاں ۲[ بارہ مکروہات بیان کر رہے ہیں تفصیل نیچے دیکھیں ۔۔ ایک ہے اچھی آواز سے اذان دینا یہ تو بہتر ہے، دوسرا ہے بلاوجہ گانے کی طرح آواز بنانا یہ مکروہ ہے، اسی کو الحان کہتے ہیں۔ وجه : اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن عمر بن سعد بن ابی حسین المکی ان مؤذنا اذن فطرب في اذانه فقال له عمر بن عبد العزيز اذن اذانا سمحا و الا فاعتزلنا ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب التطريب في الاذان ، ج اول ،ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۲۳۷۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ بہت راگ سے اذان دینا مکروہ ہے۔
And singing (talhīn) in the adhan is disliked. (339) Explanation: Among the disliked things in adhan, he is mentioning five. Then under the adhan of the one in hadath (impurity), eight persons' adhan is disliked; combined, here twelve disliked things are being mentioned. Details below. One is giving adhan with a good voice – that is better; the second is unnecessarily modulating the voice like singing – that is disliked, and this is called talhīn. Evidence: In this saying of a Tabi'i: From 'Umar ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Husayn al-Makki that a mu'adhdhin gave adhan and modulated it, so 'Umar ibn 'Abdul 'Aziz said to him: 'Give the adhan in a plain manner, or else leave us.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab al-Tatrib fi al-Adhan) This saying of a Tabi'i indicates that excessive melody in adhan is disliked.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the dislike (karahah) of performing the adhan in a melodious or singing style (talhīn). The author distinguishes between having a pleasant voice (which is commendable) and intentionally making it sound like singing (which is makruh). The proof is the statement of 'Umar ibn 'Abdul 'Aziz, who told a mu'adhdhin to either give the adhan in a simple manner or leave. The Hanafi position is that adhan should be recited in a natural, clear voice without excessive modulation, as that detracts from its solemnity.

Key Terms
التلحين (al-talhīn): Reciting the adhan in a melodious, singing style with excessive modulation.

Key Takeaway

Dislike of Adhan by Certain Persons
Ruling statement: list of persons whose adhan/iqamah is disliked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the categories of persons whose adhan (and iqamah) is disliked in the Hanafi school and state that the adhan remains valid but is makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Adhan from certain persons is valid but disliked because it lacks recommended perfection.

The adhan is a noble call to prayer, and the one who gives it should ideally be in a state of purity, sanity, and righteousness. The Hanafi school lists several persons whose adhan, though valid, is considered makruh (disliked). This lesson introduces those categories and clarifies the ruling, ensuring you do not mistake dislike for invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed categories
Read the Arabic text and list each category mentioned: al-muhdath (without wudu), al-junub (major impurity), unintelligent child, madman, drunkard, woman, and open sinner (fasiq).
The text also mentions iqamah for the muhdath, indicating both adhan and iqamah share this ruling.
2
Understand the ruling level
Note that all these categories are described as makruh. In Hanafi fiqh, makruh tanzihi means the act is valid but lacking perfection; it is better to avoid.
Do not confuse with makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) which would be closer to haram.
3
Recognize validity
Even though disliked, the adhan given by these persons is still valid. The prayer following such an adhan is not invalidated, and the adhan does not need to be repeated.
This is the key point: dislike ≠ invalidity.

Source Text

And the iqamah of the one without wudu and his adhan, and the adhan of the junub, the unintelligent child, the insane, the drunkard, the woman, and the open sinner, and...
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing persons whose adhan (and iqamah) is disliked (makruh). The author enumerates: (1) al-muhdath (one without wudu), (2) al-junub (one in major impurity), (3) a child who does not understand, (4) a madman, (5) a drunkard, (6) a woman, and (7) an open sinner (fasiq). The text cuts off, but the full set is likely a dozen disliked things. The Hanafi school holds that the adhan of these individuals is valid but makruh, because adhan is a form of worship that requires respect and proper condition. The mu'adhdhin should be in wudu, sane, and righteous. However, if such a person gives adhan, it is not invalid but undesirable.

Key Terms
المحدث (al-muhdath): A person without wudu (minor ritual impurity).
الجنب (al-junub): A person in major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
صبي لا يعقل (ṣabiyyun lā ya‘qilu): A child who does not yet understand the meaning of the adhan.
فاسق (fāsiq): An open sinner, one who commits major sins publicly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Adhan from a person without wudu, in major impurity, a non-discerning child, a madman, a drunkard, a woman, or an open sinner is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
