Rulings on Tathwib, Alhan, and Disqualified Persons in Adhan
Commentary on adhan rulings with proofs from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on tathwib, alhan, and the eight categories whose adhan is makruh, and explain the evidence from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Adhan is valid from disqualified persons but disliked; tathwib is recommended; melodious chanting is disliked.

This lesson draws from a classical Hanafi commentary on the rules of adhan. You will learn three distinct rulings: the recommendation of tathwib (repeating the call after adhan), the dislike of alhan (sing-song melody), and the eight categories of people whose adhan or iqamah is considered makruh tanzih (lightly disliked). Each ruling is supported by proofs from the statements of the Prophet ﷺ, the Companions, and early Muslims, giving you both the legal rule and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on tathwib
Locate the statement in the text: 'ويثوّب كقوله بعد الاذان الصلوة الصلوة يا مصلين'. Determine whether tathwib is wajib, sunnah, or mustahabb based on the commentary.
The text cites practice of Salaf and hadith of Bilal indicating recommendation.
2
Understand the ruling on alhan
Find the phrase 'ويكره التلحين'. Note that a pleasant voice is recommended but excessive melody (taghanni) is makruh.
Proof from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz rebuking a mu'adhdhin who sang.
3
Enumerate the eight categories of disqualified persons
From the text: 'واقامة المحدث واذانه واذان الجنب وصبي لا يعقل ومجنون وسكران وامرأة و فاسق و شریف' – list each and understand why they are makruh.
The commentary explains each with specific evidence.
4
Analyze the legal weight: why makruh tanzih not invalid
The text states the adhan is valid though disliked. The proofs (e.g., 'لا يؤذن الا متوضی') are interpreted as karahah, not tahrim.
This is the standard Hanafi usul: prohibition in adhan defaults to dislike due to its devotional nature.
5
Examine the proofs and their wajh al-dalalah
For each ruling, identify the specific dalil and how it yields the ruling. E.g., the hadith 'ليس على النساء أذان' shows negation of obligation, extended to karahah.
Use the dalil_block in the lesson to see the two provided proofs.

ترجمه : (۳۳۸) [1] اور اذان میں الحان مکروہ ہے۔
تشریح : اذان میں کیا کیا مکروہات ہیں ان میں سے ۵ کو بیان فرما ر ہے ہیں ۔ پھر محدث کی اذان کے تحت ۸ آدمیوں کی اذان مکروہ ہے اس کو بیان کر رہے ہیں ، سب ملا کر یہاں ۲[ بارہ مکروہات بیان کر رہے ہیں تفصیل نیچے دیکھیں ۔۔ ایک ہے اچھی آواز سے اذان دینا یہ تو بہتر ہے، دوسرا ہے بلاوجہ گانے کی طرح آواز بنانا یہ مکروہ ہے، اسی کو الحان کہتے ہیں۔
وجه : اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن عمر بن سعد بن ابی حسین المکی ان مؤذنا اذن فطرب في اذانه فقال له عمر بن عبد العزيز اذن اذانا سمحا و الا فاعتزلنا ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب التطريب في الاذان ، ج اول ،ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۲۳۷۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ بہت راگ سے اذان دینا مکروہ ہے۔
ترجمه : (۳۳۹) [۲] اور محدث (بے وضو ) کی اذان واقامت مکروہ ہے۔ [۳] اور جنسی اور بے سمجھ بچہ اور دیوانہ اور نشہ والا اور عورت اور فاسق کی اور بیٹھ کر اذان دینا مکروہ ہے۔
تشریح : یہاں آٹھ قسم کے آدمیوں کی اذان کو مکر وہ بتارہے ہیں۔ ہر ایک کی تفصیل یہ ہے۔ [1] جو آدمی بے وضو ہو اس کی اذان اور اقامت دونوں مکروہ ہیں ۔ حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے [۲] جو جنبی ہو یا غسل کی ضرورت ہو اس کی اذان مکروہ ہے ۔ اور اقامت تو مکروہ ہے ہی، کیونکہ جب محدث کی اذان اور اقامت مکروہ ہے تو جنبی کی اذان اور اقامت بدرجہ اولی مکروہ ہوگی ۔ [۳] ایسا بچہ جواز ان کو سمجھتا نہ ہواس کی اذان مکروہ ہے، ہاں جو اس عمر میں ہو کہ اذان کو سمجھتا ہو اس کی اذان مکروہ نہیں ہے ۔[۴] مجنون کی اذان مکروہ ہے، [۵] نشہ کی حالت میں اذان دینا مکروہ ہے۔ [۲] عورت کی اذان دینا مکروہ ہے، اس کے لئے حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے ۔ [۷] فاسق کی اذان مکروہ ہے ، اس سے وہ فاسق مراد ہے جس کا فسق بالکل ظاہر ہو اور لوگ اس سے کراہیت کرتے ہوں -[۸] بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ کر اذان دینا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اذان اعلان کے لئے ہے اس لئے کھڑا ہو کر دینا چاہئے۔ وجه : (۱) [۱] محدث [۲] اور جنسی کی اذان اور اقامت مکروہ ہے، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة عن النبي قال لا يؤذن الا متوضی- ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کراہیتہ الاذان بغیر وضوء، ص ۵۶، نمبر ۲۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغیر وضو کے اذان اور اقامت کہنا اچھا نہیں۔ (۲) یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن عطاء انــه كــره ان يؤذن الرجل و هو على غير وضو ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کره ان يؤذن وھو غیر طاہر ، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۲۱۹۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ بغیر وضو کے اذان مکروہ ہے۔ (۳) [۳] بے سمجھ بچے ، [۴] اور مجنون [۵] نشہ والے کی اذان مکروہ ہے، اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال لا بأس ان يؤذن الغلام اذا احسن الاذان قبل ان يحتلم - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی اذ ان الغلام قبل ان محتکلم ، ج اول ص ۲۰۵، نمبر ۲۳۵۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ اگر اچھا اذان دیتا ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، اسی سے یہ پتہ چلا کہ اذان سمجھتا نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے، اور اسی طرح مجنون اور نشہ والا اذان سمجھتا نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کی اذان بھی مکروہ ہوگی۔ (۴) [۶] عورت کی اذان مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن أسماء قالت قال رسول الله له : ليس على النساء أذان و لا اقامة ولا جمعة و لا اغتسال جمعة ولا تقدمهن امرأة و لكن تقوم وسطهن سنن بیھقی ، باب ليس على النساء اذان ولا اقامته ، ج اول ، ص ۲۰۰، نمبر ۱۹۲۱ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ،٣٢ في النساء من قال ليس علیهن اذان ولا اقامته ، ج اول ص ۲۰۲ نمبر ۲۳۱۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت پر آذان اور اقامت نہیں ہیں۔ (۵) یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن على قال : لا توذن و لا تقيم (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ٣٢ في النساء من قال لیس علیھن اذان ولا اقامه ، ج اول، ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۲۳۲۰) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت اذان نہ دے۔ (۶) [۷] فاسق اذان نہ دے اس کا اشارہ اس حدیث میں ہے۔۔ عن ابن عباس قال : قال رسول الله الله : ليوء ذن لكم خياركم و ليوء مكم قراوء کم ۔(ابوداود شریف ، باب من أحق بالا مامه ، ۹۷، نمبر ۵۹۰ / ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب فضل الاذان و ثواب الموء ذنین ، ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۷۲۶ ) اس
Chapter of Adhan. Steps. (337) And he performs tathwib like saying after the adhan: 'as-salah, as-salah, O worshippers.' (338) And alhan (melodious chanting) is makruh. (339) And the iqamah of the one in a state of hadath (without wudu) and his adhan, and the adhan of the junub, and the child who does not understand, and the madman, and the drunkard, and the woman, and the fasiq, and the noble [sitting]. Commentary...
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the rules of the adhan (call to prayer). It begins by discussing tathwib — the act of repeating the call to prayer after the adhan to remind the congregation, especially in the Fajr prayer and, in this era, in Zuhr, Asr, and Isha as well, because people are neglectful. The author cites an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the early Muslims used to do tathwib in Isha and Fajr, and that the mu'adhdhin of Ibrahim would do it in Zuhr and Asr without being rebuked. For Fajr, the hadith of Bilal saying 'as-salatu khayrun min an-nawm' is mentioned, establishing the practice. Then the ruling that alhan (sing-song melody) in the adhan is makruh is given, supported by an athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz who rebuked a mu'adhdhin who sang in the adhan. Finally, the text lists eight types of people whose adhan or iqamah is makruh: (1) one without wudu (muhdith), (2) junub, (3) a child who does not understand the meaning, (4) a madman, (5) a drunkard, (6) a woman, (7) a fasiq (open sinner), and (8) one who sits without excuse. For each, proofs are given: hadith that 'none should call the adhan except one with wudu', athar from Ata, the permissibility of a discerning boy's adhan, the hadith that women have no adhan or iqamah, and the hadith 'let the best among you call the adhan'. The commentary explains that the adhan of a junub is even more severely makruh than that of a muhdith, and that the child must understand the adhan. The fasiq is one whose sin is open and people dislike him.

Key Terms
تثويب (tathwib): The practice of repeating the call to prayer after the adhan, e.g., saying 'as-salah, as-salah ya musallin' to remind the congregation.
الحان (alhan): Melodious chanting or singing in the adhan beyond normal modulation, considered makruh.
محدث (muhdith): A person in a state of ritual impurity (without wudu).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true regarding the adhan of a woman?
A) It is invalid (batil).
B) It is valid but makruh tanzih (disliked).
C) It is wajib upon her.
D) It is sunnah muakkadah.

Key Takeaway
The adhan from eight categories of persons is valid but disliked (makruh tanzih); tathwib is recommended; excessive melody (alhan) is also makruh.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Eight Types of People Whose Adhan Is Makruh
Lists eight makruh categories with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight categories of people whose adhan is makruh and identify the proof (hadith or athar) that supports each ruling.

Core Idea
A person's state of purity, understanding, and righteousness affects the desirability of their adhan.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text lists eight types of individuals whose adhan (and iqamah) is considered makruh (disliked). Each category is supported by a hadith, an athar from a Companion or Tabi'i, or a qiyas. Understanding these rulings helps ensure the adhan is called with proper reverence and that the caller is in a suitable state.

Guided Path
1
Identify each category from the list
The passage lists eight distinct types: (1) one without wudu, (2) junub, (3) child who does not understand adhan, (4) insane person, (5) intoxicated person, (6) woman, (7) fasiq (open sinner), (8) one who sits without excuse.
The types are not mutually exclusive; some conditions can overlap.
2
Note the ruling for each category
For each type, the ruling is generally makruh. Exceptions: a child who understands adhan is not makruh; a woman's adhan is valid but makruh; the fasiq's adhan is makruh only if his sinfulness is apparent.
The passage does not specify the exact level (tanzih or tahrimi), but it defaults to makruh tanzih.
3
Match each category to its proof
The passage provides proofs sequentially: (1&2) hadith from Abu Hurairah, (3-5) athar from al-Sha'bi, (6) hadith from Asma' and athar from Ali, (7) hadith from Ibn Abbas, (8) analogy from the purpose of adhan.
Some proofs are explicit, others are derived by qiyas or implication.
4
Understand the reasoning behind each ruling
For example, the adhan of a junub is makruh because if minor impurity (hadath) makes it makruh, major impurity (janabah) does so a fortiori (qiyas awla). The child, insane, and intoxicated are makruh because they lack understanding or awareness.
This shows the use of analogy and general principles in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Recognize the shared principle
All rulings share the principle that the person calling adhan should be in a state of physical purity, mental awareness, and moral uprightness to maintain the dignity of the call.
This is an example of the school's emphasis on adab (etiquette) in acts of worship.

باب الاذان
تشریح : یہاں آٹھ قسم کے آدمیوں کی اذان کو مکر وہ بتارہے ہیں۔ ہر ایک کی تفصیل یہ ہے۔ [1] جو آدمی بے وضو ہو اس کی اذان اور اقامت دونوں مکروہ ہیں ۔ حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے [۲] جو جنبی ہو یا غسل کی ضرورت ہو اس کی اذان مکروہ ہے ۔ اور اقامت تو مکروہ ہے ہی، کیونکہ جب محدث کی اذان اور اقامت مکروہ ہے تو جنبی کی اذان اور اقامت بدرجہ اولی مکروہ ہوگی ۔ [۳] ایسا بچہ جواز ان کو سمجھتا نہ ہواس کی اذان مکروہ ہے، ہاں جو اس عمر میں ہو کہ اذان کو سمجھتا ہو اس کی اذان مکروہ نہیں ہے ۔[۴] مجنون کی اذان مکروہ ہے، [۵] نشہ کی حالت میں اذان دینا مکروہ ہے۔ [۲] عورت کی اذان دینا مکروہ ہے، اس کے لئے حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے ۔ [۷] فاسق کی اذان مکروہ ہے ، اس سے وہ فاسق مراد ہے جس کا فسق بالکل ظاہر ہو اور لوگ اس سے کراہیت کرتے ہوں -[۸] بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ کر اذان دینا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اذان اعلان کے لئے ہے اس لئے کھڑا ہو کر دینا چاہئے۔
وجه : (۱) [۱] محدث [۲] اور جنسی کی اذان اور اقامت مکروہ ہے، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة عن النبي قال لا يؤذن الا متوضی- ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کراہیتہ الاذان بغیر وضوء، ص ۵۶، نمبر ۲۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغیر وضو کے اذان اور اقامت کہنا اچھا نہیں۔ (۲) یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن عطاء انــه كــره ان يؤذن الرجل و هو على غير وضو ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کره ان يؤذن وھو غیر طاہر ، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۲۱۹۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ بغیر وضو کے اذان مکروہ ہے۔ (۳) [۳] بے سمجھ بچے ، [۴] اور مجنون [۵] نشہ والے کی اذان مکروہ ہے، اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال لا بأس ان يؤذن الغلام اذا احسن الاذان قبل ان يحتلم - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی اذ ان الغلام قبل ان محتکلم ، ج اول ص ۲۰۵، نمبر ۲۳۵۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ اگر اچھا اذان دیتا ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، اسی سے یہ پتہ چلا کہ اذان سمجھتا نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے، اور اسی طرح مجنون اور نشہ والا اذان سمجھتا نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کی اذان بھی مکروہ ہوگی۔ (۴) [۶] عورت کی اذان مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن أسماء قالت قال رسول الله له : ليس على النساء أذان و لا اقامة ولا جمعة و لا اغتسال جمعة ولا تقدمهن امرأة و لكن تقوم وسطهن سنن بیھقی ، باب ليس على النساء اذان ولا اقامته ، ج اول ، ص ۲۰۰، نمبر ۱۹۲۱ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ،٣٢ في النساء من قال ليس علیهن اذان ولا اقامته ، ج اول ص ۲۰۲ نمبر ۲۳۱۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت پر آذان اور اقامت نہیں ہیں۔ (۵) یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ عن على قال : لا توذن و لا تقيم (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ٣٢ في النساء من قال لیس علیھن اذان ولا اقامه ، ج اول، ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۲۳۲۰) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت اذان نہ دے۔ (۶) [۷] فاسق اذان نہ دے اس کا اشارہ اس حدیث میں ہے۔۔ عن ابن عباس قال : قال رسول الله الله : ليوء ذن لكم خياركم و ليوء مكم قراوء کم ۔(ابوداود شریف ، باب من أحق بالا مامه ، ۹۷، نمبر ۵۹۰ / ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب فضل الاذان و ثواب الموء ذنین ، ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۷۲۶ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تم میں سے اچھا ادمی اذان دے، جس کا مطلب یہ نکلا کہ فاسق آدمی اذان نہ دے۔(۷)
Chapter of Adhan. Explanation: Here eight types of people whose adhan is makruh are being mentioned. Details of each are as follows: [1] The adhan and iqamah of a person without wudu are both makruh. Hadith has passed before. [2] The adhan of a junub or one who needs a bath is makruh. The iqamah is also makruh, because when the adhan and iqamah of a person in minor impurity is makruh, then that of a junub is even more so. [3] The adhan of a child who does not understand it is makruh, but if he is of an age where he understands, it is not makruh. [4] The adhan of an insane person is makruh. [5] Adhan in a state of intoxication is makruh. [6] The adhan of a woman is makruh, hadith has passed before. [7] The adhan of a fasiq is makruh, meaning a fasiq whose sinfulness is apparent and people dislike him. [8] Adhan while sitting without an excuse is makruh, because adhan is for announcement so it should be given standing. Evidence: (1) For [1] and [2], the adhan and iqamah of a mukdath and junub are makruh, for this this hadith: from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (s) said: 'None should call the adhan except with wudu.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi karahiyat al-adhan bighayr wudu, p56, no200) From this hadith it is understood that calling adhan and iqamah without wudu is not good. (2) This athar is also: from Ata that he disliked a man calling adhan without wudu. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab man kariha an yu'adhdhin wa huwa ghayr tahir, p192, no2196) In this saying of a Tabi'i, adhan without wudu is makruh. (3) For [3], [4], [5], the adhan of an unintelligent child, insane, and intoxicated person is makruh, for this this athar: from al-Sha'bi said: 'There is no harm in a boy calling adhan if he does it well before he dreams.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab adhan al-ghulam qabla an yahtalim, vol1 p205 no2355) From this saying of a Tabi'i, if he gives a good adhan then there is no harm; from this it is known that if he does not understand adhan it is makruh, and similarly insane and intoxicated do not understand so their adhan is also makruh. (4) For [6], woman's adhan is makruh, for this this hadith: from Asma' said: 'The Messenger of Allah (s) said: Upon women there is no adhan, no iqamah, no Jumu'ah, no ghusl for Jumu'ah, and a woman shall not lead them, rather she stands in their middle.' (Sunan Bayhaqi, Bab laysa 'ala al-nisa' adhan wa la iqama, vol1 p200 no1921 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Fi al-nisa' man qala laysa 'alayhinna adhan wa la iqama, vol1 p202 no2313) In this hadith, women do not have adhan and iqamah. (5) This athar is also: from Ali said: 'She should not call adhan nor iqamah.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Fi al-nisa' man qala laysa 'alayhinna adhan wa la iqama, vol1 p202 no2320) In this saying of a Companion, a woman should not call adhan. (6) For [7], the fasiq should not call adhan, indication from this hadith: from Ibn Abbas said: 'The Messenger of Allah (s) said: Let the best among you call adhan for you, and let the reciters among you lead you.' (Abu Dawud, Bab man ahaqqu bil-imama, p97 no590 / Ibn Majah, Bab fadl al-adhan wa thawab al-mu'adhdhinin, p104 no726) In this hadith, the best person should call adhan, from which it is understood that a fasiq should not call adhan. (7)
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This is a detailed passage enumerating eight types of people whose adhan (call to prayer) and/or iqamah is considered makruh (disliked) according to the Hanafi school. The author first lists all eight in the tashrih (explanation) and then provides proofs (wajh) for each category. The eight types are: (1) one without wudu, (2) one in a state of janabah (major impurity), (3) a child who does not understand the adhan, (4) an insane person, (5) one in a state of intoxication, (6) a woman, (7) a fasiq (open sinner), and (8) one who gives adhan while sitting without an excuse. The proofs include hadith from Abu Huraira that only a mutawaddi (one with wudu) should call adhan, an athar from Ata, a report from al-Sha'bi about a boy calling adhan, a hadith from Asma' that women are not required to call adhan, the saying of Ali, and a hadith from Ibn Abbas about choosing the best person for adhan. The ruling for the eighth type (sitting) is cut off at the page break but the core ruling is clear. The passage demonstrates how the Hanafi school uses primary textual evidence (Qur'an and Hadith) and the opinions of Companions and Tabi'un to derive rulings on the etiquette of adhan.

Key Terms
مکرہ (makruh): Disliked or reprehensible; an act whose abandonment is rewarded but commission is not punished
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, openly, such that people dislike him

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the eight types of people whose adhan is makruh according to this passage?
A) One who is junub
B) One who is blind
C) A woman
D) A fasiq

Key Takeaway
The adhan may be valid even when called by someone in a deficient state, but it is disliked (makruh) in eight specific situations.

Speaking During Adhan and Iqamah
Ruling on speaking during adhan and iqamah with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on speaking during adhan and iqamah, explain why repetition is recommended for adhan but not iqamah, and cite the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Speaking during adhan is makruh; if done, repeating the adhan is recommended, but not the iqamah.

The call to prayer (adhan and iqamah) is a sacred act that prepares the congregation for salah. Scholars have discussed whether speaking during the call is permissible, disliked, or invalidating. This passage presents the Hanafi position that speaking is makruh (disliked) and that repeating the adhan is recommended but not the iqamah, based on narrative evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is speaking during the adhan or iqamah. The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh (disliked). The matn explicitly states: 'والكلام في خلال الاذان و في الاقامة' and the tashrih confirms the ruling.
2
Understand the distinction between adhan and iqamah
If the mu'adhdhin speaks during the adhan, repeating the adhan is mustahabb (recommended). However, if he speaks during the iqamah, repetition is not recommended. The reason given: there is ample time for adhan, but the iqamah is immediately followed by prayer, so repeating would cause delay.
This distinction shows the school's practical consideration for congregational prayer.
3
Examine the first proof (hadith of Ibn Umar)
The proof cites Ibn Umar who, on a cold rainy night, added the words 'ألا صلوا في رحالكم' (Pray in your dwellings) at the end of his adhan. The Hanafi deduce that speaking after the adhan is permissible, and speaking during the adhan is even more disliked (makruh) because it interrupts the call.
The hadith is from Muslim, and the Hanafi use it as a dalil that the adhan is not invalidated by speaking, but that speaking during it is not ideal.
4
Examine the second proof (athar of Ibn Sirin)
Ibn Sirin, a Tabi'i, is reported to have disliked speaking during the adhan until it is finished. This supports the Hanafi ruling that speaking is makruh.
While not a primary source like Quran or mutawatir sunnah, statements of Tabi'in are used as supporting evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Consider the recommendation of repetition
The ruling that repetition is mustahabb (not wajib) means the original adhan remains valid, but it is better to repeat to remove the disliked element. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that undesirable acts in worship can be compensated without invalidating the act.
This nuance prevents unnecessary burden on the mu'adhdhin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تــرجمـه : (۳۴۰) [۳] اور اذان واقامت کے درمیان کلام کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ اذان میں بات کرنے سے اس کا اعادہ مستحب ہے اقامت کا نہیں۔
(۳۴۰) والكلام في خلال الاذان و في الاقامة. ويستحب اعادته دون الاقامة .
تشریح : موذن کا اور اقامت کہنے والے کا درمیان میں بات کرنا مکروہ ہے، اور اگر کر لی تو مستحب ہے کہ اذان کولوٹائے ، کیونکہ اس میں کافی وقت ہے، اور اقامت کو نہ لوٹائے ، کیونکہ نماز کھڑی ہو چکی ہے، لوگوں کو دیر ہوگی۔
وجه : (ا) عن ابن عمر انه نادى بالصلاة في ليلة ذات برد و ريح و مطر فقال في آخر ندائه الا صلوا في رحالكم الا صلوا فى رحالكم . (مسلم شریف ، باب الصلوة في الرحال في المطر ص ۲۸۳، نمبر ۱۶۰۱/۶۹۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بات اذان کے بعد کی ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اذان کے درمیان بات کرنا مکروہ ہے ۔ (۲) عن ابن سیرین انهما كرها ان يتكلم حتى يفرغ - مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ، باب من کره الکلام فی الاذان ، ص ۱۹۳، نمبر ۲۲۰۴) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ اذان میں کلام کرنا مکروہ ہے۔
Translation: (340) [3] And speaking during the adhan and iqamah is makruh. If one speaks during adhan, repeating it is mustahabb (preferable), but not the iqamah. (340) And speaking during the adhan and iqamah. It is mustahabb to repeat it, but not the iqamah. Explanation: The mu'adhdhin and the one calling iqamah speaking in between is makruh, and if they do so, it is mustahabb to repeat the adhan because there is enough time, but not the iqamah because the prayer is about to start and people would be delayed. Proof: (a) From Ibn Umar that he called the prayer on a cold, windy, rainy night and said at the end of his call: 'Pray in your dwellings, pray in your dwellings.' (Muslim, Bab al-salah fi al-rihal fi al-matar, p283 no1601/697) This hadith indicates that speaking after the adhan is makruh, so during is even more so. (2) From Ibn Sirin that they disliked speaking until finishing. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab man kariha al-kalam fi al-adhan, p193 no2204) This saying of a Tabi'i shows that speaking during adhan is makruh.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on speaking during the call to prayer (adhan and iqamah). The matn states that speaking is makruh. If the mu'adhdhin speaks during the adhan, it is recommended (mustahabb) to repeat the adhan, but not the iqamah. The author explains that there is ample time for the adhan to be repeated, but the iqamah is closely followed by the prayer, so repeating it would cause delay for the congregation. The proof is from the hadith of Ibn Umar who added extra words after the adhan, indicating that speaking during the adhan itself would be even more disliked. Also, the authority of Ibn Sirin who explicitly disliked speaking during the adhan. This shows the Hanafi attention to the sanctity of the call and the smooth flow of the prayer.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; performing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the adhan is more important.

Key Takeaway
Speaking during adhan is makruh; if it happens, repeating the adhan is mustahabb to maintain the ideal, but not for iqamah due to immediate prayer.

Adhan for Zuhr on Friday in a City is Makruh
Ruling that adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in a city are makruh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in a city and explain why it is makruh.

Core Idea
On Friday in a city, Zuhr is replaced by Jumu'ah, so its adhan is makruh.

In this lesson, we encounter a practical ruling about Friday prayers. When Jumu'ah is established in a city, the Zuhr prayer is not performed. Consequently, calling the adhan for Zuhr becomes inappropriate and is considered makruh. This lesson clarifies a common point of confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is calling adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in a city. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
2
Understand the underlying reason
Because Jumu'ah replaces Zuhr in a city (misr). Zuhr is not prayed, so its adhan is misplaced.
The explanation in the source says: 'In the city, Jumu'ah is held, not Zuhr, so calling adhan for Zuhr is makruh.'
3
Define 'misr'
A misr is a major city where Jumu'ah is valid. In villages where Jumu'ah is not established, this ruling does not apply.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between misr and qaryah for Jumu'ah.
4
Note the scope
This ruling applies only in a city where Jumu'ah is established. In villages, Zuhr is still prayed, so adhan is not makruh.
Check the adjacent ruling in the anatomy block.

Adhan and Iqamah for Making Up Missed Prayers
Ruling on adhan and iqamah for qada of missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah when making up one or more missed prayers in a single sitting.

Core Idea
For multiple qada prayers in one sitting, only the first gets both adhan and iqamah; subsequent ones require iqamah but not adhan.

When a prayer is missed (qada), the Hanafi school prescribes adhan and iqamah as sunnah. But when several missed prayers are performed consecutively in one sitting, the ruling is nuanced to avoid unnecessary repetition. This passage from the matn gives the concise rule: the first prayer gets the full call, while for the rest, iqamah is still recommended but adhan is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether you are making up a single missed prayer or multiple missed prayers in one sitting (majlis).
The ruling changes based on this.
2
State the default ruling
For a single missed prayer, both adhan and iqamah are called.
This is the same as for prayers performed on time.
3
Apply the exception for multiple prayers
For the first of several prayers, give both adhan and iqamah. For the remaining prayers, give iqamah (leaving it is makruh), but adhan is not required (leaving it is not makruh).
The first adhan suffices for notification; iqamah still signals the immediate start.
4
Memorize the key phrase
The matn says: 'ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم، وكذا لأولى الفوائت، وكره ترك الإقامة لباقيها، ولم يكره ترك الأذان'.
This encapsulates the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۴۲) ایک فوت شدہ نماز کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت کہے، اور ایسے ہی بہت سی فوت شدہ نمازوں کے لئے اذان دے اور اقامت کہے، اور باقی نمازوں کے لئے اقامت چھوڑ نا مکروہ ہے اذان چھوڑ نا مکروہ نہیں ہے، اگر ایک ہی مجلس میں سب کی قضا کر رہا ہو۔ تشریح : اگر ایک نماز فوت ہوگئی ہو اور اس کو قضا کر رہا ہو تو اس کے لئے اذان دے اور ا قامت بھی کہے، دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ بہت سی نمازیں فوت ہوگئی ہوں اور سب کو ایک ہی مجلس میں قضا کر رہا ہو، تو ہر ایک نماز کے لئے الگ الگ اذان دے اور ہر ایک کے
(۳۴۲) ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم وكذا لاولی الفوائت . وکره ترک
Translation: (342) For one missed prayer, he calls adhan and iqamah, and similarly for the first of several missed prayers, he calls adhan and iqamah. And abandoning the rest is makruh for iqamah, but abandoning adhan is not makruh, if he is making them up in one sitting. Explanation: If one prayer is missed and he is making it up, he gives adhan and iqamah for it. Second issue: If many prayers are missed and he is making them all up in one sitting, then for each prayer he gives a separate adhan and for each... (342) And he gives adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah, and similarly for the first of several missed prayers. And abandoning the rest is makruh.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi rulings on adhan and iqamah for making up missed prayers (qada). For a single missed prayer, both adhan and iqamah are required. For multiple missed prayers performed consecutively in one sitting, the first prayer gets both adhan and iqamah, while for the subsequent prayers, it is makruh to leave the iqamah (meaning it is recommended to call iqamah for each), but leaving the adhan for subsequent prayers is not makruh. The explanation clarifies that the reason is to avoid excessive delay and because the first call already suffices for notification.

Key Terms
فائتة (fa'itah): A missed (qada) prayer
مجلس (majlis): A sitting or session where prayers are performed consecutively without interruption

D) It requires no adhan or iqamah.

Key Takeaway
For multiple qada prayers in one sitting, only the first receives adhan; each subsequent prayer requires iqamah but adhan is optional.

Ruling on Speaking During Adhan and Iqamah
States ruling on talking during adhan/iqamah and its repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on talking during adhan and iqamah, identify the recommended action if speech occurs, and explain the evidence from hadith and the practice of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Speaking during adhan or iqamah is makruh; repeating the adhan is mustahabb, but iqamah is not repeated.

While the adhan and iqamah are sacred calls that prepare for prayer, what happens if the mu'adhdhin speaks in the middle? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on incidental speech and the recommended remedy. We will also examine the proofs that support this position, drawn from the actions of the Companions and the statements of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that speaking during the adhan and during the iqamah is makruh. Determine the precise hukm level: makruh tanzihi, meaning it is disliked but not sinful.
Makruh tanzihi is close to permissible; leaving it is rewarded.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Ibn Umar who spoke at the end of his adhan on a rainy night, and (2) the statement of Ibn Sirin that the early Muslims disliked speaking until the adhan finishes.
The hadith is from Muslim, the statement from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From the hadith: Ibn Umar spoke after the adhan, implying that speaking during the adhan is normally not done; it is disliked. From Ibn Sirin: explicit disapproval (karahiyya) of speaking during the adhan.
The proof is from inference (mafhum mukhalafah) and direct statement.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi position is makruh tanzihi, some scholars consider speaking during adhan permissible (mubah). The khilaf does not affect the recommended action of repeating the adhan.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the scope of permissible difference.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that speaking is makruh tanzihi. If speech occurs, it is mustahabb to repeat the adhan but not the iqamah, because the iqamah is immediately before prayer and repetition would cause undue delay.
This ruling is consistent with the zahir al-riwayah and later fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴۰) والكلام في خلال الاذان و في الاقامة. ويستحب اعادته دون الاقامة . ... وجه : (ا) عن ابن عمر انه نادى بالصلاة في ليلة ذات برد و ريح و مطر فقال في آخر ندائه الا صلوا في رحالكم الا صلوا فى رحالكم . (مسلم شریف ، باب الصلوة في الرحال في المطر ص ۲۸۳، نمبر ۱۶۰۱/۶۹۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بات اذان کے بعد کی ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اذان کے درمیان بات کرنا مکروہ ہے ۔ (۲) عن ابن سیرین انهما كرها ان يتكلم حتى يفرغ - مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ، باب من کره الکلام فی الاذان ، ص ۱۹۳، نمبر ۲۲۰۴) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ اذان میں کلام کرنا مکروہ ہے۔

(Muslim) This hadith indicates that speaking after the adhan (is permissible), so speaking during the adhan is makruh. (2) From Ibn Sirin that they (two) disliked speaking until he finishes. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This saying of a Tabi'i indicates that speaking during the adhan is makruh.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its proofs regarding talking during the adhan and iqamah. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) for the mu'adhdhin or the one saying iqamah to speak during the process. If one does speak, it is mustahabb (recommended) to repeat the adhan from the beginning because there is sufficient time before the prayer, but the iqamah should not be repeated because the prayer is about to begin and repeating would cause delay. The proof is derived from the action of Ibn Umar who spoke at the end of his adhan on a rainy night, indicating that speaking during the adhan is normally disliked. Additionally, Ibn Sirin reported that the early Muslims disliked speaking during the adhan until completion.

Key Terms
الاذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer consisting of specific phrases announcing the time of salah.
الاقامة (al-iqamah): The second call immediately before the prayer begins, similar to adhan but with 'qad qamati al-salah' added.
مکروہ (makruh): An action that is disliked and discouraged but not sinful; leaving it is rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It invalidates the iqamah and must be repeated.
B) It is makruh, but the iqamah is not repeated.
C) It is permissible and no action is needed.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Speaking during adhan or iqamah is makruh tanzihi; if speech occurs, repeating the adhan is recommended (mustahabb), but the iqamah is not repeated.

Adhan for Zuhr on Friday in a City
States that adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in a city are makruh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for Zuhr on Friday in a city and identify the conditions that trigger it.

Core Idea
On Friday, the adhan for Zuhr is makruh in a city where Jumu'ah is established.

This short passage from a Hanafi manual lays down a clear rule regarding the call to prayer on Friday. It addresses a potential confusion: in a city where the Friday Jumu'ah prayer is obligatory, calling the adhan for the regular Zhuhr prayer is considered disliked (makruh). Understanding the conditions—being in a 'misr' and on Friday—is essential to correctly apply this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is calling the adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
The ruling covers both adhan and iqamah.
2
Define the key term 'misr'
A misr is a city or town where Jumu'ah is established and considered fard on the residents.
The jurists have conditions for what constitutes a misr, e.g., population size, presence of a ruler, etc.
3
Understand the condition: jumu'ah replaces Zuhr
Since Jumu'ah is the Friday congregational prayer, Zuhr is no longer the obligation of the day. Calling its adhan could create confusion.
This is the rationale behind the makruh ruling.
4
Consider exceptions and scope
The ruling applies only in a city where Jumu'ah is held. Outside the city, or if Jumu'ah is not established, the adhan is not makruh.
Also, individual excuse does not change the collective ruling.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not consider this makruh. The Hanafi School holds it as makruh tanzih.
This is a point of ikhtilaf among the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴۱) ويكرهان لظهر يوم الجمعة في المصر .
(341) And they (adhan and iqamah) are makruh for Zuhr on the day of Friday in the city (proper).
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This is a concise ruling: in a city (misr) where Friday jumu'ah is established, it is makruh to call the adhan and iqamah for the Zuhr prayer on Friday. This is because the jumu'ah prayer replaces zuhr; calling zuhr adhan might create confusion. Outside the city or if jumu'ah is not held, the ruling differs.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or town where Friday jumu'ah is established and considered a metropolitan area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, it is makruh.

D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqamah for Zuhr on Friday in a city where Jumu'ah is established are considered makruh (disliked) in the Hanafi school.

Adhan and Iqamah for Missed Prayers
Ruling on adhan and iqamah for missed prayers individually and in a group

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah for a single missed prayer and for multiple missed prayers, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
For multiple missed prayers, one adhan and separate iqamahs suffice — leaving iqamah is makruh.

When making up missed prayers (qada'), the adhan and iqamah are not simply repeated for each prayer. The Prophet ﷺ demonstrated a concise practice that balances reverence with ease. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on when to give adhan and iqamah for missed prayers, both singly and in batches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (adhan and iqamah for missed prayers) and the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah for adhan for the first, iqamah for each; leaving iqamah is makruh tanzihi).
The ruling distinguishes between a single missed prayer and multiple missed prayers.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited in the text: the hadith from the Battle of the Trench in which the Prophet ordered one adhan and iqamah for each of four missed prayers.
The hadith is reported in Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet gave one adhan and then iqamah for each prayer, indicating that one adhan suffices for multiple missed prayers and iqamah is recommended for each.
The action of the Prophet is the primary evidence for the sunnah practice.
4
Note the practical distinction
Distinguish between a single missed prayer (adhan and iqamah both sunnah) and multiple missed prayers (one adhan for the first, iqamah for each subsequent).
The text states 'wa kadhā li-ūlā al-fawā'it' – similarly for the first of multiple.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa: for multiple missed prayers in one sitting, give one adhan and then iqamah for each prayer. Omitting iqamah is makruh tanzihi.
This is the relied-upon view from the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴۲) ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم وكذا لاولی الفوائت . وکره ترک ... وجه حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال عبد الله ان المشركين شغلوا رسول الله له عن اربع صلوات يوم الخندق حتى ذهب من الليل ماشاء الله فامر بلالا فاذن ثم أقام فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ثم اقام فصلى المغرب ثم أقام فصلى العشاء ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل تفوته الصلوات با یتھن یبد ا ص ۴۳، نمبر ۷۹ ارنسائی شریف ، باب کیف یقضی الفوائت من الصلوۃ ، ص۷۲، نمبر ۶۲۳) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مرتبہ اذان دے اور باقی کے لئے اقامت کہے۔ اور اس کو چھوڑ نا مکروہ ہے۔
(342) And one gives adhan for the missed prayer (single) and iqamah, and likewise for the first of multiple missed prayers. And leaving (iqamah) is makruh. ... The proof is the hadith: 'Abdullah said, 'The polytheists kept the Messenger of Allah engaged from four prayers on the day of al-Khandaq until part of the night had passed. So he ordered Bilal to give adhan, then iqamah, and he prayed Zuhr; then iqamah for Asr; then iqamah for Maghrib; then iqamah for Isha.' (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) From these hadith, it is understood that one adhan is given and iqamah for the rest, and leaving it is makruh.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for missed (faa'itah) prayers. For a single missed prayer, both adhan and iqamah are given. For multiple missed prayers (fawa'it) being made up in one sitting, it is sunnah to give adhan for the first prayer only and iqamah for each subsequent prayer. It is makruh to omit iqamah for any of them, though omitting adhan for the later ones is not makruh. The proof is the action of the Prophet during the Battle of the Trench: he ordered one adhan and then iqamah for each prayer individually. This indicates the recommended practice.

Key Terms
الفائتة (al-faa'itah): A missed prayer that is being made up (qada').
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Multiple missed prayers being made up in one session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If ten prayers are missed and one is making them up in one sitting, how is the adhan given?
A) Adhan for each prayer.
B) One adhan for all, then iqamah for each.
C) No adhan, only iqamah for each.
D) Adhan only for the first.

Key Takeaway
For multiple missed prayers in one sitting, it is sunnah to give one adhan and separate iqamahs; omitting iqamah is makruh tanzihi.

Etiquette for the Listener of Adhan: Repeating and the Hay'alat Response
Ruling with proof: listener's responses to adhan phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah responses for each phrase of the adhan and identify the exceptions for the hay'alat and 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm'.

Core Idea
The listener repeats the adhan except for hay'alat (say 'la hawla...') and 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm' (say 'sadaqta...').

When the adhan is called, the listener is encouraged to respond by repeating the mu'adhdhin's words. However, there are specific exceptions rooted in the Sunnah: the phrases 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' are not repeated; instead, one says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'. Similarly, during Fajr adhan, the phrase 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm' merits a special acknowledgment. This lesson explains these sunnah responses and provides the proof from authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The listener should repeat the adhan words (except for the exceptions). This is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The adhan must be masnun (proper in words and time).
2
Pinpoint the exceptions
The two hay'alat ('hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah') and the phrase 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm' are not to be repeated.
They have special responses as taught by the Prophet.
3
Learn the response for each exception
For the hay'alat, say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'. For 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm', say 'sadaqta wa bararta' or 'ma sha Allah'.
This is based on companion practice and hadith.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
Two ahadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) and from Umar ibn al-Khattab (Muslim, Abu Dawud) explicitly detail the responses.
These are ahadith ahad, but their meaning is clear and accepted by the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴۳) واذا سمع المسنون منه امسک وقال مثله وحوقل في الحیعلتين وقال صدقت و بررت او ماشاء الله عند قول المؤذن الصلوة خير من النوم ... وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدرى ان رسول الله الله قال اذا كـ سمعتم النداء فقولوا مثل ما يقول المؤذن ..... حدثنى بعض اخواننا انه قال لما قال حى على الصلوة قال لا حول و لا قوة الا بالله ، و قال هكذا سمعنا نبيكم الله يقول - ( بخاری شریف، باب ما یقول اذا سمع المنادی ،ص ۱۰۱، نمبر ۶۱۱ نمبر ۶۱۳ را بو داود شریف ، باب ما يقول اذا سمع الموذن ، ص ۸۸ نمبر ۵۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مؤذن جیسا کہے ویسا ہی کہے،صرف حی علی الصلوۃ پر اورجی على الفلاح پر لاحول ولاقوۃ الا باللہ کہے۔ (۲) عن جده عمر بن الخطاب قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قال الموذن الله اكبر ، الله اكبر : فقال احدكم : الله اکبر، الله اكبر ، ثم قال : اشهد ان لا اله الا الله ، قال : اشهد ان لا اله الا الله ثم قال : اشهد ان محمدا رسول الله ، قال : اشهد ان محمدا رسول الله ،ثم قال : حي على الصلاة ، قال لا حول ولا قوة الا بالله ثم قال ، حى على الفلاح ، قال : لا حول و لا قوة الا بالله ثم قال ،الله اکبر، الله اکبر قال الله اكبر، الله اكبر ، ثم قال : لا اله الا الله. قال : لا اله الا الله. من قلبه ، دخل الجنة (مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب القول مثل قول الموذن، الخ، ص ۱۶۳، نمبر ۸۵۰٫۳۸۵ ابوداود شریف، ما یقول اذ اسمع الموذن
(343) And when one hears the masnun (proper) adhan, he stops and says like it, and says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' at the two hay'alat (hayya 'ala al-salah and hayya 'ala al-falah), and says 'sadaqta wa bararta' or 'ma sha Allah' at the mu'adhdhin's saying 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm'. ... Proof: (1) Hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet said, 'When you hear the call, say like the mu'adhdhin says.' ... Some of our brothers narrated that when (the mu'adhdhin) says 'hayya 'ala al-salah', he says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', and said, 'Thus we heard your Prophet say.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) (2) From Umar ibn al-Khattab from the Prophet: ... (detailed list)... 'Whoever says that from his heart enters Paradise.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage explains the sunnah response of the listener upon hearing the adhan. If the adhan is proper (masnun), the listener should pause from other activities and repeat the phrases after the mu'adhdhin, except for the two hay'alat (hayya 'ala al-salah and hayya 'ala al-falah): instead of repeating, one says 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'. Similarly, at the phrase 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm' (used in fajr), the listener says 'sadaqta wa bararta' (you have spoken truth and acted righteously) or 'ma sha Allah'. The proofs are ahadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Umar, showing the Prophet's instruction. Note: If the adhan is irregular (lahn) or not at the proper time, this response is not sunnah.

Key Terms
الحیعلتين (al-hay'alatayn): The two phrases 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the adhan.
مسنون (masnun): Following the sunnah; here referring to adhan that is correct in words and time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'
C) 'Sadaqta wa bararta'
D) Silence

Key Takeaway
The listener's sunnah response to the adhan involves repeating most phrases, but with specific phrases like hay'alat and 'al-salat khayrun min al-nawm' requiring distinct responses.

Du'a of al-Wasilah After Adhan
Hadith on reward for du'a after adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended du'a after adhan, identify its evidence, and explain the promised reward.

Core Idea
Reciting the du'a of al-Wasilah after adhan earns the Prophet's intercession.

This lesson presents a beautiful sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ: a specific supplication after the adhan that carries a tremendous reward. The hadith from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah assures us that whoever recites it will be granted the Prophet's intercession on the Day of Judgment. Understanding this practice deepens our connection to the call to prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that this du'a is recited after the adhan, not by the mu'adhdhin alone but by every listener. The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah).
2
Memorize the du'a text
Learn the exact wording: 'Allahumma Rabba hadhihi'd-da'wati't-tammati wa's-salati'l-qa'imati, ati Muhammadan al-wasilata wa'l-fadilata, wab'athhu maqaman mahmudan alladhi wa'adtah.' This is the core of the lesson.
The Arabic text is provided in the source.
3
Understand key terms
Know the meanings: 'wasilah' (the highest rank in Paradise), 'hay'alatayn' (the two calls: Hayya 'ala as-salah and Hayya 'ala al-falah), and 'hawqalah' (La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah). These appear in the context of adhan response.
These terms are defined in the source.
4
Study the proof
Read the hadith from Jabir (Bukhari and Abu Dawud). The Prophet said: 'Whoever says this when he hears the call, my intercession becomes permissible for him on the Day of Resurrection.' This is the evidence for the ruling and the reward.
The hadith is authentic (zanni thubut).
5
Apply the reward
Internalize that reciting this du'a is a means to gain the Prophet's intercession. This motivates consistent practice after every adhan.
The reward is conditional upon saying the du'a upon hearing the adhan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Section: Conditions of prayer and its pillars) From sleep. (344) Then he should supplicate with al-Wasilah, saying: 'O Allah, Lord of this perfect call and the established prayer, grant Muhammad the wasilah and virtue, and raise him to a praiseworthy station which You have promised him. Section: Conditions of prayer and its pillars p. 88, no. 527) This hadith contains the complete detailing of responding to the adhan. Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its proof concerning a recommended supplication after the adhan. The author first states the action: after responding to the adhan, one should recite the du'a of al-Wasilah. The Arabic text is given. Then a hadith from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah is cited as evidence. The Prophet promised that whoever recites this du'a upon hearing the call to prayer will earn the Prophet's intercession on the Day of Judgment. The hadith is authentic, reported by Bukhari and Abu Dawud. The commentary also explains key terms: 'Hay'alatayn' refers to the two phrases 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', and 'Hawqalah' refers to 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'. The author emphasizes the importance of this practice and its reward. According to the Hanafi school, this du'a is recited after the adhan and before the iqamah, and it is a sunnah mu'akkadah. The reward of intercession is a great incentive for Muslims to be mindful of this practice.

Key Terms
حیعلتین (hay‘alatayn): A dual term referring to the two phrases 'Hayya ‘ala al-salah' and 'Hayya ‘ala al-falah'.
حوقل (hawqalah): A term referring to the phrase 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (There is no power or strength except with Allah).
وسیلہ (wasīlah): A means of nearness, specifically the highest rank in Paradise granted to the Prophet Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
Reciting the du'a of al-Wasilah after adhan is a confirmed sunnah that earns the Prophet's intercession.

Conditions and Pillars of Salah
Systematic listing of shurut and arkan of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions and seven pillars of salah and distinguish between them.

Core Idea
Salah’s validity depends on six preconditions and seven integral pillars.

This lesson defines the foundational elements of prayer: conditions (shurut) that must be fulfilled before starting, and pillars (arkan) that are performed within. Understanding these is essential for every Muslim to ensure their prayer is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
1. Define shurut vs. arkan
Identify that shurut are prerequisites performed before prayer, while arkan are integral parts performed during prayer.
Shurut are sometimes called pre-conditions; arkan are sometimes called integrals.
2
2. List the six shurut
Memorize the six conditions: purity from hadath and najasah, clean place, covering 'awrah, clean clothes, intention, facing qiblah.
Purity covers both body and clothing.
3
3. List the seven arkan
Memorize the seven pillars: takbir al-tahrimah, qiyam, qira'ah, ruku', sujud, final qa'dah, khuruj bi-sun'ih.
Khuruj bi-sun'ih means exiting prayer by one's own action, like saying salam.
4
4. Note the 27 detailed requirements
The text expands to 27 items including sub-conditions like certainty of time and specifying fard/wajib in intention.
These 27 cover both shurut and arkan plus additional details.
5
5. Recognize the authority level
This list is from zahir al-riwayah, the most authoritative transmission within the Hanafi school.
Other schools may have different counts; Hanafi relies on seven arkan.

Section: Explanation of the conditions and pillars of prayer. Essential note: 'Shurut' (conditions) is the plural of 'shart'. They are the obligations performed before prayer. And the obligations that are necessary within prayer are called 'arkan' (pillars). For example, the purity of the worshipper's body. These conditions are six: (1) Purity of the body from both major and minor impurities, (2) Purity of the place, (3) Covering of the private parts, (4) Purity of clothing, (5) Intention for prayer, (6) Facing the qiblah. Some things that are within prayer and are obligatory are called arkan, such as: (1) Takbir al-tahrimah, (2) Standing, (3) Recitation, (4) Bowing, (5) Prostration, (6) Final sitting, (7) Exiting by one's own action. For prayer to be valid, twenty-seven things are required: At a glance... (1) Body, clothing, and place are pure from impurities (both major and minor). (2) Covering of private parts. (3) Facing the qiblah. (4) Praying on time. (5) Certainty of the entry of time. (6) Intention. (7) Saying the takbir al-tahrimah immediately afterwards. (8) Performing takbir al-tahrimah. (9) Intention occurring at the time of takbir, not later. (10) Saying takbir in such a way that one can hear oneself, according to the school. (11) For the follower, intention to follow. (12) Specifying the obligatory prayer. (13) Specifying the wajib, and specifying the optional is not a condition. (14) Standing in all prayers except optional (nafl). (15) Reciting Quran in the two rak'ahs of fard and in all rak'ahs of nawafil and witr. (16) Bowing. (17) Prostrating on something that is solid and the forehead rests on it. (18) The place of prostration should not be more than half a cubit higher than the place of the feet. (19) Placing both hands and both knees on the ground according to the sound narration. (20) Placing some toes on the ground in prostration. (21) Preceding bowing before prostration.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage enumerates the essential conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan) of prayer according to the Hanafi school. First, a distinction is made: shurut are prerequisites performed before the prayer, while arkan are integral parts performed during prayer. Six conditions are listed: purification from hadath and najasah, clean place, covering 'awrah, clean clothes, intention, and facing qiblah. Seven pillars are listed: takbir al-tahrimah, qiyam, qira'ah, ruku', sujud, final qa'dah, and khuruj bi-sun'ih (exiting by one's own action). Then the text expands to 27 requirements for valid prayer, which include detailed sub-conditions such as certainty of time, specifying the fard or wajib, and proper performance of sujud. This is a standard Hanafi matn for memorization. The author's purpose is to provide a comprehensive list to ensure the worshipper's prayer is correct. Notably, the Hanafi school treats wajibat as distinct from fard; here the requirement to specify whether the prayer is fard or wajib is mentioned. The list serves as a practical guide for students.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A prerequisite that must be fulfilled before prayer; omitting it invalidates prayer.
رکن (rukn): An integral part of prayer; omitting it invalidates prayer.
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbīr al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer; a rukn.
خروج بصنعہ (khurūj bi-ṣun‘ihi): Exiting the prayer by one's own deliberate action, e.g., saying salam or intentionally leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this text, how many conditions (shurut) are there for prayer?
A) 5
B) 6
C) 7
D) 27

Key Takeaway
Salah has six preconditions (shurut) and seven pillars (arkan); missing any invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
15 min
The 27 Prerequisites for Valid Prayer
Enumeration of 27 prerequisites with detailed focus on purification conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify each of the 27 prerequisites as a shart (condition), rukn (pillar), or wajib (obligatory element), and state the consequence of omitting each.

Core Idea
Purification from hadath and najasah is a condition—its omission invalidates the prayer entirely.

In this lesson, we examine the twenty-seven things necessary for prayer to be valid according to the Hanafi school. These are not all of equal weight: some are conditions (shurut) that must be present before prayer, some are pillars (arkan) that define the prayer's structure, and some are obligatory elements (wajibat) whose omission requires compensation. We will focus especially on the first condition—purification from ritual impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (najasah)—which is supported by explicit Quranic and prophetic proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the 27 items
Scan the list in the passage and note each requirement. They range from purification (items 1-2) to intention (6), takbir (7-9), standing (14), recitation (15), ruku (16), sujud (17-20), sequence (21), sitting (22-25), attentiveness (26), and belief (27).
The list includes shurut, arkan, and wajibat.
2
Classify by legal category
Determine which items are conditions (shurut) that must exist before prayer, which are pillars (arkan) that constitute its essence, and which are wajibat whose omission requires sajdah al-sahw. For example, purification is a condition, ruku is a pillar, and specifying the prayer is a wajib.
Hanafis distinguish between fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.
3
Analyze the proof for purification
The passage provides Quranic verses (5:6 for wudu/ghusl, 74:4 for garments) and hadith (Dar Qutni on five impurities, Ibn Majah on forbidden places). Note how the imperative form (amr) is used to derive obligation.
This illustrates Hanafi use of dalil naqli.
4
Note intra-Hanafi differences
The text mentions 'according to the authentic narration' regarding placing hands and knees on the ground in sujud. This indicates a preferred narration from Abu Yusuf or Muhammad over Abu Hanifa.
The mufta bihi follows the sound narration.
5
Apply the consequences of omission
For each category, recall the consequence: missing a condition → prayer invalid (batil); missing a pillar → prayer invalid; missing a wajib unintentionally → sajdah al-sahw required; missing a sunnah → no compensation.
This practical understanding is essential for correct fiqh application.

( آیت ۶ ، سورة المائدة ۵ ) (۲) اور حدث اکبر سے پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ وان کنتم جنبا فاطهروا ( آیت ۶ ، سورۃ المائدة (۵) (۳) اور کپڑا نا پاک نہ ہو اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ وثیابک فطهر (آیت۴ سورۃ المد شر۴ ۷ ) (۴) ۔ اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ان نجاستوں سے کپڑا پاک ہو تب نماز ہوگی ۔ يا عمار انما يغسل الثوب مــن خــمــس مـن الـغـائـط والبول والقيء والدم والمنى (دار قطنی ، باب نجاسة البول والامر بالنز ه مندرج اول ص ۱۳۴ نمبر ۴۵۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بدن، کپڑا اور مکان کا ان نجاستوں سے پاک ہونا ضروری ہے۔ (۵) اور جگہ پاک ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ابن الخطاب ان رسول الله لعل الله قال سبع مواطن لا تجوز فيها الصلاة ، ظاهر بيت الله ولمقبرة ، و المزبلة و المجزرة ، و الحمام و عطن الابل ، و محجة الطريق ۔ (ابن ماجۃ شریف، باب مواضع التي تكره فيها الصلاۃ ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۷۴۶) اس حدیث میں سات جگہ نماز پڑھنے سے منع فرمایا ہے اس لئے کہ دو کے علاوہ پاک نہیں ہیں۔ ترجمه : (۳۴۶) یہاں تک کہ دونوں قدم اور دونوں ہاتھ اور دونوں گھٹنوں اور پیشانی ( رکھنے ) کی جگہ بھی اصح روایت پر
The validity of prayer depends on twenty-seven things. For prayer to be valid, twenty-seven (27) things are necessary: At a glance... [1] purification from hadath (minor and major) and purification of body, clothes, and place from impurity. [2] covering the nakedness. [3] facing the qibla. [4] performing prayer on time. [5] certainty of the entry of time. [6] making intention. [7] saying the takbir tahrimah without interval. [13] performing the takbir tahrimah properly. [8] intention must be present at the time of takbir; not delayed after it. [9] the takbir should be said so that one hears oneself, according to the mid school. [10] for the follower, intending to follow the imam. [11] specifying the obligatory prayer. [12] specifying the wajib prayer; specifying nafl is not a condition. [14] standing in all prayers except nafl. [15] reciting Quran in the two rak'ahs of obligatory prayers and in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr. [16] bowing (ruku). [17] prostrating on a firm surface such that the forehead rests. [18] the place of prostration should not be more than half a cubit higher than the feet. [19] placing both hands and both knees (on the ground) according to the authentic narration. [20] placing some toes of the feet on the ground in prostration. [21] preceding ruku before sajdah. Chapter: Conditions and Pillars of Prayer. (345) Purification from hadath and purification of body, garment, and place from impure matter that is not excused. (346) [22] rising from the first prostration close to sitting, according to the sound narration. [23] performing the second prostration. [24] sitting at the end for the extent of the tashahhud. [25] performing the final sitting after all other pillars. [26] performing all pillars while awake. [27] believing that the manner of prayer and all its obligations are obligatory. ☆☆☆ For prayer to be valid, twenty-seven (27) things are necessary: its explanation. Translation: (345) [First] Purification from hadath (minor and major), and purification of body, garment, and place from impure matter that is not excused. Explanation: Hadath is of two types: minor hadath, such as requiring wudu, and major hadath, such as requiring ghusl, like being in a state of janabah, or purification from menses and postpartum bleeding. So the person praying must be purified from both types of hadath. And the garment in which one prays must be pure, and the place in which one prays must also be pure. Evidence: (1) The evidence for purification from minor hadath is the verse: 'When you rise for prayer, wash your faces and your hands up to the elbows...' (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:6). (2) The evidence for purification from major hadath is the verse: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves' (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:6). (3) The evidence that the garment should not be impure is the verse: 'And purify your garments' (Surah Al-Muddaththir 74:4). (4) There is a hadith that prayer is valid only when the garment is purified from these impurities: 'O Ammar, the garment is only washed from five things: feces, urine, vomit, blood, and semen.' (Dar Qutni, chapter on impurity of urine and command to avoid, first part, p. 134, no. 452). From this hadith it is understood that purification of the body, garment, and place from these impurities is necessary. (5) For the purity of the place, there is the hadith: 'From Ibn Umar ibn al-Khattab that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: Seven places where prayer is not permissible: the roof of the House of Allah, the graveyard, the dumping ground, the slaughterhouse, the bathroom, the camel resting place, and the middle of the road.' (Ibn Majah, chapter on disliked places for prayer, p. 107, no. 746). This hadith prohibits praying in these seven places because except for two, they are impure. Translation: (346) Even the places of both feet, both hands, both knees, and the forehead (placing) are also (conditions) according to the most authentic narration.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage serves as a comprehensive enumeration of the prerequisites for the validity of prayer (salah) according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that twenty-seven things are necessary for prayer to be valid, then lists them in a compact form. These include conditions (shurut) such as purification from hadath (impurity), covering the nakedness, facing the qibla, performing prayer on time, certainty of time entry, intention (niyyah), the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah), specifying the obligation, standing (qiyam) for those able, recitation of Quran, bowing (ruku), prostration (sajdah) on a firm surface, proper positioning of limbs in prostration, and the sequence of actions. The list also includes pillars (arkan) like ruku and sujood, and obligatory elements (wajibat) like sitting for tashahhud and believing in the obligations. The author then elaborates on the first condition: purification from hadath (minor and major) and from ritual impurity (najasah) on the body, clothes, and place. He provides Quranic proofs: verse 5:6 for wudu and ghusl, and verse 74:4 for purification of garments. He also cites hadith from Dar Qutni specifying the five impurities that necessitate washing the garment, and a hadith from Ibn Majah listing seven places where prayer is not permissible due to impurity. The passage clearly follows the Hanafi methodology of deriving rulings from primary sources and emphasizing the practical requirements for valid prayer.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A state of ritual impurity that requires purification (wudu for minor, ghusl for major) before prayer.
طهارة (taharah): Ritual purification from both hadath and najasah.
تكبير تحريم (takbir tahrimah): The opening 'Allahu Akbar' that begins the prayer and makes previously permissible actions (like eating) unlawful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of prayer?
A) Purification from both minor and major hadath
B) Facing the qibla
C) Reciting the Quran in every rak'ah of nafl prayer
D) Placing the hands on the knees during ruku

Key Takeaway
The validity of prayer depends on fulfilling all 27 prerequisites, which include conditions, pillars, and obligatory elements, each with specific consequences for omission.

Salah — Prayer

Covering the Awrah: When Internal Exposure Does Not Invalidate
Ruling with proof on covering private parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the awrah during prayer and distinguish between external exposure and internal visibility.

Core Idea
Prayer is valid if the awrah is covered externally, even if seen from within the garment.

In this lesson, we examine the second condition for prayer: covering the awrah. The text clarifies a subtle but important nuance: accidental internal visibility (e.g., through the collar or hem) does not invalidate the prayer, as long as the awrah is covered from the perspective of an external observer. We'll explore the Quranic and Hadith proofs that establish this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is covering the awrah during prayer. The ruling is that it is a condition (shart) for validity, and accidental internal visibility does not invalidate.
The ruling is fard based on the Quranic command.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The Quranic verse (7:31) and a hadith from Aisha (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawood). The verse commands taking adornment at every mosque, interpreted as covering the awrah. The hadith states that a woman's prayer is not accepted without a headcover.
Both proofs are naqli (textual).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the verse prove covering the awrah? 'Take your adornment' is understood as wearing proper clothes covering the awrah. 'Every mosque' is interpreted as 'every prayer'. The hadith explicitly links covering to prayer acceptance.
The Hanafi interpretation connects 'mosque' to 'prayer' because prayer is the primary act in mosques.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? All schools agree covering awrah is obligatory, but they differ on the exact limits of awrah (e.g., woman's face and hands). This text does not address those limits.
The passage promises details later.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The text states the ruling without ikhtilaf on this specific point (internal visibility does not harm). This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The authoritative weight is zahir al-riwayah.

ترجمه : (۳۴۷) [۲] ستر عورت ۔ اور اگر گریبان اور دامن کے نیچے سے اپنی شرمگاہ دیکھے تو کچھ حرج نہیں ۔ تشریح : نماز درست ہونے کے لئے ستر عورت ضروری ہے، اگر اوپر سے ستر تو ڈھکا ہوا ہے لیکن گر بیان سے ستر دیکھ لیا، یا دامن کے نیچے سے ستر دیکھ لیا تو اس سے نماز میں کوئی خلل واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ يا بني آدم خذوا زينتكم عند كل مسجد . ( آیت ۳۱ ،سورۃ الاعراف ۷ ) (۲) اور حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قال رسول الله لا تقبل صلوة حائض الا بخمار - (ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء لا تقبل صلوة المرأة الحائض الا بعمار، ص ۱۰۱ نمبر۳۷۷ و ابو داؤد شریف ، باب المرآة تصلی بغیر خمار، ص۱۰۳، نمبر (۶۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نمازی کو ستر ڈھانکنا ضروری ہے۔ عورت کا ستر کتنا ہے اور مرد کا کتنا ہے اس کی تفصیل بعد میں آئے گی۔
Translation: (347) [2] Covering the awrah. And if he sees his private part from his collar or from the bottom of his hem, there is no harm. Explanation: For prayer to be correct, covering the awrah is necessary. If the awrah is covered from above but he sees it from his collar or from below his hem, then no disruption occurs in the prayer. Proof: (1) In the verse: 'O children of Adam, take your adornment at every mosque' (Quran 7:31). (2) And in the hadith: 'Aisha reported that the Messenger of Allah said: The prayer of a menstruating woman is not accepted without a headcovering' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawood). From this hadith it is learned that the worshiper must cover the awrah. The detail of how much is awrah for a woman and for a man will come later.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the second condition: covering the awrah (private parts) during prayer. The author specifies that if the covering garment is such that the awrah becomes visible from above via the collar or from below via the hem, but the garment is present, the prayer remains valid. This is because the obligation is to cover the awrah with something, not that it must be seen. The proofs are: the Quranic command to take adornment at every mosque, interpreted as covering the awrah during prayer, and the hadith that a woman must cover her head for prayer. The Urdu commentary notes that details of the awrah limits for men and women will follow later. This shows that in the Hanafi school, covering the awrah is a condition for validity, but accidental exposure from within the garment does not invalidate.

Key Terms
ستر العورة (satr al-'awrah): Covering the private parts with appropriate clothing during prayer.

Facing the Qibla: Ayn vs Jihat
Ruling on the third condition: facing the qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the obligation of facing the exact direction of the Ka'bah (ayn) and the general direction (jihat) based on one's ability to see the Ka'bah, and apply the Hanafi ruling in practice.

Core Idea
Facing the exact Ka'bah is fard when visible; otherwise general direction suffices.

Facing the qibla is the third condition of prayer. The Hanafi school makes a clear distinction based on whether you can see the Ka'bah. If you can see it, you must face it exactly. If not, turning toward its general direction is sufficient — even if you are inside Mecca itself. This ruling ensures the obligation is fulfilled according to one's ability, as demonstrated by the Prophet's own practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the passage and note the two groups: those who see the Ka'bah (mushahid) and those who do not (ghair mushahid). The ruling differs for each.
The mushahid is the one who can directly see the Ka'bah without any obstruction.
2
State the ruling for each
For the mushahid, the obligation is to face the exact direction (ayn al-ka'bah). For the ghair mushahid, the obligation is to face the general direction (jihat al-ka'bah).
Even if the ghair mushahid is in Mecca, general direction suffices.
3
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him), after leaving the Ka'bah, prayed two rak'ahs facing the exact direction of the Ka'bah. This shows that precision is required when the Ka'bah is visible.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, hadith 397.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action indicates that when the Ka'bah is visible, one must face it precisely. The hadith is used as evidence for the ruling of the mushahid.
The dalal of the hadith is zanni, meaning it supports the ruling but is not the sole proof.
5
Cross-madhhab consideration
All schools agree on the obligation to face the qibla, but some may require more precision in determining the exact direction for those who cannot see the Ka'bah. The Hanafi view is that general direction suffices.
This is considered muttafaq alayh in essence, with minor differences in detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۴۸) [۳] قبلہ رو ہونا۔ پس جو مکہ مکرمہ میں ہو اور قبلہ دیکھ رہا ہو اس کا فرض ہے عین قبلہ کا ہونا، اور جو کعبہ کو دیکھ نہیں رہا ہو اس کے لئے اس کی جہت کر لینا، چاہے مکہ مکرمہ میں ہی کیوں نہ ہو، صحیح روایت یہی ہے۔ تشریح : جس آدمی کے سامنے کعبہ ہو اس کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ عین کعبہ کی جہت نماز پڑھے، اور جو کعبہ نہیں دیکھ رہا ہو تو چاہے وہ مکہ مکرمہ میں ہی کیوں نہ ہو صرف کعبہ کی طرف منہ کر لینے سے قبلہ کا استقبال ہو جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) جس کو کعبہ نظر آرہا ہو اس کے لئے عین قبلہ کا رخ کرنا ضروری ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال أتى ابن عمر صلى الله فقيل له : هذا رسول الله دخل الكعبة ... ثم خرج فصلى في وجه الكعبة ركعتين ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب قوله تعالى و اتخذوا من مقام ابراهيم مصلی که آیت ۱۲۵ سورة البقرة (۲) ص ۷۰ نمبر ۳۹۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ
Translation: (348) [3] Facing the qibla. So the one who is in Mecca and sees the qibla, his duty is to face its exact direction. And the one who does not see the Ka'bah, it suffices for him to face its direction, even if he is in Mecca itself. This is the correct narration. Explanation: The person in front of the Ka'bah must pray in the exact direction of the Ka'bah. And the one who does not see the Ka'bah, even if he is in Mecca, simply turning his face toward the Ka'bah will be sufficient for facing the qibla. Proof: (1) For the one who sees the Ka'bah, facing the exact qibla is necessary. The proof is this hadith: 'Ibn Umar came while the Messenger of Allah had entered the Ka'bah... then he came out and prayed two rak'ahs facing the direction of the Ka'bah' (Bukhari).
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the third condition: facing the qibla. The author distinguishes between two cases: the person who can see the Ka'bah directly must face its exact physical direction (ayn al-ka'bah). The person who cannot see the Ka'bah, even if within the city of Mecca, only needs to face the general direction (jihat al-ka'bah). This is the correct Hanafi position. The proof is from the action of the Prophet after leaving the Ka'bah. The commentary notes that this distinction applies also to those far away; they face the direction. This ruling is based on the principle that the obligation is to face the Ka'bah itself when possible, otherwise its direction is sufficient.

Key Terms
عين الكعبة (ayn al-ka'bah): The exact physical direction of the Ka'bah itself, as opposed to just its general direction.
جهة الكعبة (jihat al-ka'bah): The general direction (qibla) determined by ijtihad or reckoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person inside the Masjid al-Haram but behind a pillar such that he cannot see the Ka'bah. What is his obligation regarding facing the qibla?
A) He must find a spot to see the Ka'bah
B) He faces the general direction of the Ka'bah
C) He may pray in any direction
D) His prayer is invalid if he does not see it

Key Takeaway
The obligation to face the qibla is fulfilled by facing the exact direction when the Ka'bah is visible, and by facing its general direction when it is not.
