Covering the 'Awrah and the Exception for Internal Sight
Ruling with proof on covering 'awrah and a concession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that covering the 'awrah is a condition for prayer, identify the proofs (Quran 7:31 and hadith), and apply the exception that seeing one's own 'awrah through the collar or hem does not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Covering the 'awrah is fard; internal sight via openings does not break the condition.

This passage establishes a foundational ruling for salah: covering the 'awrah is a necessary condition. Yet it adds a nuance—if the covering is intact from an external perspective, internal sight through the collar or hem does not harm the prayer. The ruling is supported by the Quranic command to take adornment at every mosque and a hadith linking prayer acceptance to covering. Let us unpack the ruling, its proof, and the precise scope of the exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Nature
Read the first part of the matn: 'And covering the 'awrah...' Determine what kind of ruling this is (shart/condition for validity). Note that the text then adds 'and it does not harm if he sees it from his collar or the bottom of his garment'.
The ruling has two components: an obligation and a concession.
2
Examine the First Proof (Quran)
The verse 'O children of Adam, take your adornment at every place of prayer' is cited. Identify the term 'zinah' (adornment) and how the Hanafi school interprets it as covering the 'awrah. Recognize that the imperative form (khudho) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
The dalalh is zanni because the word 'zinah' requires interpretation, but the imperative gives weight.
3
Examine the Second Proof (Hadith)
The hadith from Aisha: 'The prayer of a menstruating woman is not accepted except with a headcover.' Here 'menstruating woman' implies an adult woman (obligated to cover). Analyse how this hadith establishes covering for women and by analogy for men.
The hadith is used to show that covering is a condition (shart) of acceptance.
4
Understand the Exception
The phrase 'does not harm if he sees it from his collar or the bottom of his garment' means that internal sight through openings in the covering (collar, hem) does not nullify the condition. The 'awrah is still covered from external view.
This concession avoids undue hardship; the condition is about external exposure, not the worshipper's own line of sight.
5
Apply the Ruling to Hypothetical
Take a scenario: A man prays in a shirt with a wide collar; while bowing, he sees his navel. Apply the two-part ruling: condition fulfilled (covering intact externally), internal sight does not harm. The prayer remains valid.
Contrast with a transparent garment: then covering is not achieved, and prayer invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴۷) وستر العورة ولا يضر نظرها من جيبه واسفل ذيله . يا بني آدم خذوا زينتكم عند كل مسجد. عن عائشة قال رسول الله ﷺ لا تقبل صلاة حائض إلا بخمار.
(347) And covering the 'awrah, and it does not harm if he sees it from his collar or the bottom of his garment. O children of Adam, take your adornment at every place of prayer. And from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The prayer of a menstruating woman is not accepted except with a headcover.'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof covering two parts: first, covering the 'awrah is a condition for the validity of prayer; second, if a person sees his own 'awrah through the collar or hem of his garment, that does not harm the prayer, as the 'awrah is still covered from the outside. The proofs are the Quranic verse (7:31) commanding adornment at every mosque, interpreted as covering the 'awrah, and the hadith that the prayer of a menstruating woman (who is obligated to cover) is not accepted without a headcover. The Hanafi position is that covering the 'awrah is fard; for men, from navel to knee, for women, all except face and hands. The concession about seeing through the collar or hem is a specific Hanafi ruling to avoid undue hardship.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered during prayer.
جيبه (jayb): The collar or neck opening of a garment.
ذيله (dhayl): The hem or bottom edge of a garment.

Covering the 'awrah is a non-negotiable condition for prayer, but incidental internal sight through garment openings does not break that condition.

Facing the Qiblah: Exact vs. Direction
Distinction between mushahid and non-mushahid regarding facing qiblah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qiblah for those who see the Kaaba and those who do not, and explain the proof from the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
For the one who sees the Kaaba, exact facing is obligatory; for others, direction suffices.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling in salah: how precisely must one face the qiblah? The matn distinguishes between one who sees the Kaaba (mushahid) and one who does not. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct prayer, especially for those in Makkah who cannot see it. We will explore the Quranic and hadith proofs that support this graded obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? (facing the qiblah) and what is the hukm? (fard). The matn states that for the mushahid, it is 'isabat 'ayni' (exact hitting); for non-mushahid, it is 'jihahat' (direction).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 2:144 ('shatra'), then two hadiths: 'Between east and west is qiblah' (Tirmidhi) and the hierarchy of the House, Masjid, Haram (Bayhaqi).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key word 'shatra' indicates direction, not exact pinpoint. This is the linguistic basis for the distinction: the Quran commands facing the direction, not the exact spot.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani held that even the mushahid may not require exact facing; they interpreted 'shatra' as direction for all.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, as supported by later authorities.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah takes Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position. The practical consequence: mushahid must be exact; others (including those in Makkah who do not see the Kaaba) need only direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴۸) واستقبال القبلة فللمكي المشاهد فرضه اصابة عينها ولغير المشاهد جهتها ولو بمكة على الصحيح . فول وجهك شطر المسجد الحرام وحيث ما كنتم فولوا وجوهكم شطره. ما بين المشرق والمغرب قبلة. البيت قبلة لاهل المسجد، والمسجد قبلة لاهل الحرم، والحرم قبلة لاهل الارض في مشارقها ومغاربها من أمتي.
(348) And facing the qiblah. So for the Makkan who is seeing (the Kaaba), his obligation is to hit its exact direction; for the one not seeing, his obligation is its direction, even if in Makkah, according to the correct position. So turn your face toward the Sacred Mosque, and wherever you are, turn your faces toward it. Between the east and the west is the qiblah. The House is the qiblah for the people of the Mosque, the Mosque is the qiblah for the people of the Haram, and the Haram is the qiblah for the people of the earth in its east and west from my ummah.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on facing the qiblah. The matn distinguishes: one who sees the Kaaba (mushahid) must face it exactly (isabat 'ayni); one who does not see it must face its direction (jihahat), and this applies even if in Makkah but not seeing it. The proofs include the Quranic verse (2:144) with the word 'shatra' meaning direction, and the hadith 'between east and west is qiblah' indicating general facing for those far, and the hadith from Bayhaqi showing a hierarchy: the Kaaba for those in the Masjid, the Masjid for those in the Haram, the Haram for all others. The Hanafi ruling is that facing the qiblah is fard; exact facing is required only for the mushahid; for others, a general direction within 90 degrees (45 left/right) suffices.

Key Terms
المشاهد (al-mushahid): One who sees the Kaaba with his own eyes.
شطر (shatra): Direction, side; not precise bearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is inside the Masjid al-Haram but cannot see the Kaaba due to crowd. How should he face?
A) He must face the exact direction of the Kaaba as if he saw it.
B) He may face any direction because he is in the Haram.
C) He must face the general direction of the Masjid al-Haram.
D) He must face the direction he believes the Kaaba is, even if inexact.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to face the qiblah varies by proximity: exact for those who see the Kaaba, direction for all others.

Time for Prayer and Certainty of Entry
Statement that prayer is tied to its time and certainty of entry is required

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prayer time entry requires certainty or ghalabat al-zann and derive it from the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Prayer is valid only with certainty or overwhelming probability that its time has entered.

This passage establishes that every prayer has a specific time and that performing it requires certainty or overwhelming probability that the time has begun. The proof includes both a Quranic verse and a Prophetic hadith, highlighting that time is an essential condition for the validity of the prayer. Understanding this ruling prevents invalidating one's prayer due to doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the five daily prayers. The ruling is that they are fard at fixed times; the existence of the time is a condition for validity.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The Quranic verse (4:103) states that prayer is 'mawquta' (fixed with times). The hadith from Abu Hurairah specifies the boundaries.
The hadith is quoted partially: 'The time of prayer is between these two.'
3
Analyze the legal implication of 'mawquta'
The word 'mawquta' indicates designated times, implying that prayer cannot be performed outside its time as ada' (timely performance).
4
Determine the requirement of certainty
The matn states 'wa i'tiqad dukhulihi' (belief in its entry). This is interpreted as certainty or overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) that the time has entered.
5
Apply to practical scenario
If a person prays while doubting the time, the prayer is invalid even if later proven correct. One must verify time through reliable means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴۹) والوقت واعتقاد دخوله . إن الصلاة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا. عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله ﷺ وقت الصلاة ما بين هذين.
(349) And the time and belief in its entry. Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at designated times. From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The time of prayer is between these two.'
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof that prayer has a prescribed time and that one must be certain of its entry. The matn states two conditions: the existence of the time (al-waqt) and the belief (i'tiqad) that the time has entered. The commentator explains that if one prays before time, the fard is not performed; if after, it becomes qada. Doubt prevents a valid intention and thus the prayer is not valid. The Quranic verse (4:103) uses 'mawquta' to indicate fixed times. The hadith (from Abu Hurairah, though incomplete here) specifies the times. The Hanafi ruling requires certainty or overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) that the time has entered; mere doubt is insufficient.

Key Terms
موقوتا (mawquta): Fixed with specific times; prayer is tied to its time.
اعتقاد (i'tiqad): Belief or conviction; in this context, certainty or overwhelming probability that the time has entered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid because it was within the time.
B) The prayer is invalid because he lacked certainty at the time of prayer.
C) The prayer is valid but must be repeated (qada) out of caution.
D) The prayer is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of the prayer depends on certainty or overwhelming probability of time entry, not on retrospective knowledge.

Time and Certainty: Conditions for Prayer Validity
Ruling with proofs on conditions for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for obligatory prayer validity (time and certainty of its entry) and apply the proof from Quran and Sunnah to identify when a prayer is invalid.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalid without time and without certainty of its entry — doubt breaks the intention.

This lesson examines two essential conditions for obligatory prayer: the presence of the prescribed time and the certainty that it has entered. The Hanafi school emphasises that both are required for the prayer to fulfil the obligation. We will explore the textual proofs from the Quran and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions from the text
Read the opening: 'وقت ہونا' (time must be present) and 'اور وقت داخل ہونے کا یقین ہونا' (certainty of its entry). These are the two conditions (shurut).
Both are listed as separate points in the Urdu summary.
2
Understand the consequence of doubt
The commentary gives an example: if someone is unsure whether Zuhr time has entered and prays anyway, the obligation is not fulfilled because the intention was not firm.
This shows that yaqeen (certainty) is a condition for the intention to be valid.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verse (An-Nisa 4:103): 'ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا'. The word 'mawqutan' indicates that prayer is fixed to specific times, making time a condition.
The dalala is qati (definitive) because the word is clear.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
Two hadith are cited: (1) from Abu Hurairah defining Zuhr's time boundaries, and (2) the hadith of Jibril establishing that prayer times are enclosed between a first and last moment. These reinforce the necessity of praying within the time and knowing its entry.
Both hadith are from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud; they provide the practical definition of waqt.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۴۹) [۴] وقت ہونا ۔ [۵] اور وقت داخل ہونے کا یقین ہونا۔ تشریح : فرض نماز کے لئے وقت ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ وہ وقت کے ساتھ متعلق ہے، اگر وقت ہونے سے پہلے پڑھے گا تو فرض ادا نہیں ہوگا، اور وقت کے بعد پڑھے گا تو قضاء ہوگی ۔ اور دوسری بات یہ کہی کہ اس بات کا یقین ہو کہ وقت ہو چکا ہے، مثلا ظہر کا وقت ہو چکا تھا لیکن آدمی کو شک ہے کہ وقت ہو یا نہیں ہوا اور ظہر کی نماز پڑھ لی تو فرض ادا نہیں ہوگا ، کیونکہ شک کی وجہ سے ظہر کی نیت پختہ طور پر نہیں کر پایا، اس لئے فرض بھی ادا نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : (ا) ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا. (آيت ١٠٣،سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ نماز وقت کے ساتھ متعین ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ نماز وقت کے درمیان گھری ہوئی ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله ان للصلوة اولا و آخرا و ان اول وقت صلاة الظهر حين تزول الشمس و آخر وقتها حين يدخل وقت العصر - ترمذی شریف، باب منه ما جاء فی مواقیت الصلوة عن النبی ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۵) (۳) اخبرنی ابن عباس ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال امنی جبرئیل عند البيت مرتين .... ثم التفت الى جبرئيل فقال يا محمد هذا وقت الانبياء من قبلك والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في مواقيت الصلوة عن النبي ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۴۹ و ابوداؤد شریف، باب المواقیت ،ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز اول وقت اور آخر وقت میں گھری ہوئی ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے اول وقت ہے اور آخر وقت ہے۔
Translation: (349) [4] The time must be present. [5] And certainty of its entry. Explanation: For the obligatory prayer, the time must be present because it is related to time. If one prays before the time, the obligation is not fulfilled, and if after, it will be qada (make-up). The second point is that one must be certain that the time has entered. For example, if the time for Zuhr has entered but a person doubts whether the time has entered or not, and he prays Zuhr, then the obligation is not fulfilled because due to doubt, he did not firmly intend Zuhr, so the obligation is not fulfilled. Proof: (1) 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at fixed times' (An-Nisa 4:103). This verse indicates that prayer is fixed with time. (2) This hadith also: From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, prayer has a beginning and an end, and the beginning of the time of Zuhr is when the sun declines, and its end is when the time of Asr enters' (Tirmidhi, chapter on prayer times from the Prophet, p.42, no.15). (3) Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Jibril led me in prayer at the House twice... then he turned to me and said: O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times' (Tirmidhi, chapter on prayer times from the Prophet, p.42, no.149; Abu Dawud, chapter on prayer times, p.68, no.393). This hadith indicates that prayer is enclosed between the beginning and end times, so there is an initial time and a final time.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs on the conditions of time and certainty of time entry for prayer. The author (translating from the matn) states that time and certainty of its entry are conditions. In the commentary, he explains that a obligatory prayer must be performed within its designated time; praying before invalidates it, and after makes it qada. Additionally, one must be certain that the time has entered. If there is doubt, the intention is not firm, and the prayer does not fulfill the obligation. Three proofs are cited: the Quranic verse (4:103) stating prayer is fixed times, a hadith defining Zuhr time from decline to Asr entry, and the hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer, showing that prayer times are bounded by a first and last moment.

Key Terms
وقت (waqt): The prescribed time period for each obligatory prayer.
یقین (yaqeen): Certainty that the prayer time has entered, eliminating doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person prays Zuhr while doubting whether the time has entered?
A) The prayer is valid if it turns out the time had entered.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid but disliked.
D) The prayer counts as nafl.

Key Takeaway
For an obligatory prayer to be valid, the prescribed time must have entered and one must be certain of its entry; doubt invalidates the intention and the obligation.

Salah — Prayer

Intention and Opening Takbir: Three Obligatory Elements
Ruling with proof on three fard elements for starting prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three fard elements for commencing prayer and explain their proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Intention, takbir tahrimah, and continuity — three inseparable fard elements for valid prayer start.

This passage clarifies the essential obligations when beginning prayer. It is common to know that intention and the opening takbir are required, but the third requirement—that they be performed without any interval—is often overlooked. The author presents clear proofs from hadith and Quran, establishing these as fard (obligatory) acts that directly affect the validity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three fard elements
From the text, extract the three obligations: (1) intention (niyyah), (2) saying the takbir tahrimah, and (3) performing them consecutively with no interval (fasl). Understand that each is individually fard.
Continuity means no eating, drinking, or any action foreign to prayer between intention and takbir.
2
Analyze the proof for intention
Examine the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' (Bukhari, Muslim) and the athar from Ibn Mas'ud. Understand that intention is a condition for the validity of any act of worship, and it must be present at the start of prayer.
Intention is in the heart, not verbal expression.
3
Analyze the proof for takbir tahrimah
Study the Quranic verse 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3) and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification, its opening is takbir...' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). Recognize that takbir tahrimah is the formal entry into prayer and a pillar (rukn).
The takbir is called 'tahrimah' because it prohibits actions outside prayer.
4
Understand the requirement of continuity
Note that the text explicitly states the three obligations together. If an interval occurs (e.g., eating, drinking), the intention is invalidated and must be renewed before saying takbir.
This emphasizes the integrated nature of the opening.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider a case: Someone intends to pray Maghrib, then drinks water before saying Allahu Akbar. According to the text, they must make a new intention and then say the takbir. The prayer is not valid if takbir follows an interrupted intention.
This illustrates the consequence of violating the continuity condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۰) [۲] نیت (۷) اور تکبیر تحریمہ بغیر فصل کے ہو۔ تشریح : یہاں تین باتیں ہیں ، اور تینوں فرض ہیں [۱] ایک ہے نیت کرنا۔ [۲] اور دوسری ہے تکبیر تحریمہ کہنا [۳] اور تیسری بات یہ ہے کہ نیت کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر تحریمہ کہے ، دونوں کے درمیان فصل نہ ہو، مثلا نیت کرنے کے بعد کھانا نہ کھائے ، پانی نہ پئے، یا کوئی ایسا عمل نہ کرے جو عمل نماز کے خلاف نہ ہو، اور اگر کر لیا تو پھر نیت کر کے تکبیر تحریمہ کہے۔ کوئی بھی عبادت بغیر نیت کے نہیں ہوتی ، مثلا دل میں نماز پڑھنے کی نیت نہیں ہے اور نماز کے تمام اعمال کر لے تو نماز نہیں ہوگی ، اس لئے نماز ادا ہونے کے لئے نیت کرنا فرض ہے۔ اور صرف دل میں ارادہ کر لینے کا نام نیت ہے۔ وجه : (۱) نیت فرض ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے۔ سمعت عمر بن خطاب علی المنبر يقول سمعت رسول الله الله يقول انما الاعمال بالنيات ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف کان بدء الوحی الی رسول اللہ ص ۱، نمبر ۱ و مسلم شریف، باب قولہ انما الاعمال بالنیۃ الخ ص ۸۵۳، نمبر ۴۹۲۷/۱۹۰۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اعمال کا دارو مدار نیت پر ہے اسلئے نماز میں داخل ہونے کی نیت کرے گا تو نماز ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ (۲) اس اثر میں بھی اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد اللہ بن مسعود قال : تعودوا الخير فان الخير بالعادة ، و حافظوا على نياتكم فى الصلوة - الطبراني في الكبير، باب خطبة ابن مسعود و من كلامه، ج تاسع ، ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۸۷۵۵/اعلاء السنن ، باب اشتراط النية للصلاة ، ج الثانی، ص ۱۶۳، نمبر ۶۴۲ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں نیت ضروری ہے۔ وجه (۱) تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہے اسکی دلیل یہ آیت ہے وربک فکبر (آیت ۳ ، سورۃ المدثر ہے ) کہ اپنے رب کی بڑائی بیان کیجئے ۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابی سعيد قال قال رسول الله مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم ولا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة فى فريضة او غيرها . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تحریم الصلوة وتحليلها ، ص۶۶ نمبر ۲۳۸ و ابوداؤد شریف، باب الامام يحدث بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر رکعته ، ص ۱۰۰، نمبر ۶۱۸ )
Translation: (350) [2] Intention (7) and the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah) must be without any interval. Explanation: There are three things here, and all three are obligatory (fard). [1] Intention. [2] Saying the takbir tahrimah. [3] That the takbir tahrimah be said immediately with the intention; there should be no interval between them. For example, after making intention, one should not eat, drink, or do any action contrary to prayer. If one does such an action, then he must make intention again and say takbir tahrimah. No act of worship is valid without intention. For instance, if a person does not intend prayer in his heart but performs all the actions of prayer, the prayer is not valid. Therefore, intention is obligatory for prayer. Intention is merely the resolve in the heart. Proof: (1) The proof that intention is obligatory: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Actions are but by intentions' (Bukhari, chapter on how the revelation began, p.1, no.1; Muslim, chapter on his saying 'actions are but by intentions' etc., p.853, no.4927/1907). This hadith indicates that actions depend on intention, so if one intends to enter prayer, the prayer is valid, otherwise not. (2) This athar also proves it: From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: He said: 'Accustom yourselves to good, for good is by habit, and guard your intentions in prayer' (Tabarani in al-Kabir, chapter on Ibn Mas'ud's sermon and his speech, vol.9, p.151, no.8755; I'la al-Sunan, chapter on the condition of intention for prayer, vol.2, p.163, no.642). This athar shows that intention in prayer is necessary. Proof (1) that takbir tahrimah is obligatory: The verse 'And your Lord magnify' (Al-Muddaththir 74:3) meaning, extol your Lord's greatness. (2) The hadith: From Abu Sa'id: He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its opening is takbir, and its closing is taslim, and there is no prayer for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a Surah in an obligatory or other prayer' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the opening and closing of prayer, p.66, no.238; Abu Dawud, chapter on the imam who has an event after raising his head from the last rak'ah, p.100, no.618).
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs on the obligation of intention (niyyah) and the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah) without interruption. The author states three obligatory elements: (1) intention, (2) saying the takbir tahrimah, and (3) that they be consecutive with no interval. The commentary explains that after intending, one must not engage in any extraneous action; if one does, the intention must be renewed. Intention is defined as resolve in the heart. Proofs for intention's obligation include the famous hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' and an athar from Ibn Mas'ud urging to guard intentions in prayer. For takbir tahrimah, the verse 'And your Lord magnify' is cited, as well as the hadith that 'the opening of prayer is takbir' and that no prayer is valid without reciting al-Fatihah and a surah.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): The resolve in the heart to perform a specific prayer (or worship).
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir tahrimah): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' to commence prayer, which prohibits actions outside prayer.
فصل (fasl): An interval between intention and takbir, such as eating or talking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on saying the takbir tahrimah after a period of silence following intention?
A) The takbir is valid as long as the intention remains.
B) The takbir is invalid because there must be no interval.
C) The takbir is valid only if one recites something else.
D) The takbir is invalid only if one performs an action contrary to prayer.

Key Takeaway
Intention, takbir tahrimah, and their immediate connection are three fard elements that must be observed for the prayer to be valid according to the Hanafi school.

The Three Essential Obligations of Prayer: Intention, Takbir, and Consecutiveness
States the three obligatory elements for entering prayer: intention, takbir, and their conjunction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three obligatory elements for entering prayer (niyyah, takbir tahrrimah, and their consecutive performance) and identify the proofs for each from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Intention and opening takbir must be consecutive; a gap with a foreign action invalidates the start of prayer.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah lays out the foundational obligations that must be fulfilled when beginning any prayer. It clarifies that intention (niyyah) and the opening takbir (tahrrimah) are obligatory, and that they must be performed without interruption. Understanding these three elements is essential for the validity of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three obligations
List the three matters the author declares obligatory: making intention, saying the opening takbir, and performing them consecutively without a gap.
The text explicitly numbers them as three obligatory matters.
2
Locate the proofs for intention
Find the hadith cited: 'Actions are by intentions' (Bukhari, Muslim) and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud about habituating oneself to good and guarding intentions in prayer.
These prove that intention is essential for the validity of worship.
3
Locate the proofs for the opening takbir
Find the Qur'anic verse 'And magnify your Lord' (Q. 74:3) and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrrimah is takbir, its tahlil is taslim' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud), plus the report from Ibrahim that forgetting the takbir requires repeating the prayer.
The imperative form indicates obligation.
4
Understand the consequence of a gap
The author states that if a foreign action (eating, drinking, etc.) occurs between intention and takbir, the consecutiveness is broken; one must renew intention and takbir.
This shows the requirement of immediate succession (muwalat).

باب) شروط الصلوة واركانها (۳۵۰) والنية والتحريمة بلا فاصل رسول الله الله ان للصلوة اولا و آخرا و ان اول وقت صلاة الظهر حين تزول الشمس و آخر وقتها حين يدخل وقت العصر - ترندی شریف، باب منه ما جاء فی مواقیت الصلوة عن النبی ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۵) (۳) اخبرنی ابن عباس ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال امنی جبرئیل عند البيت مرتين .... ثم التفت الى جبرئيل فقال يا محمد هذا وقت الانبياء من قبلك والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء في مواقيت الصلوة عن النبي مالي ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۴۹ را بو داؤد شریف، باب المواقیت ،ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز اول وقت اور آخر وقت میں گھری ہوئی ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے اول وقت ہے اور آخر وقت ہے۔ ترجمه : (۳۵۰) [۲] نیت (۷) اور تکبیر تحریمہ بغیر فصل کے ہو۔ تشریح : یہاں تین باتیں ہیں ، اور تینوں فرض ہیں [۱] ایک ہے نیت کرنا۔ [۲] اور دوسری ہے تکبیر تحریمہ کہنا [۳] اور تیسری بات یہ ہے کہ نیت کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر تحریمہ کہے ، دونوں کے درمیان فصل نہ ہو، مثلا نیت کرنے کے بعد کھانا نہ کھائے ، پانی نہ پئے، یا کوئی ایسا عمل نہ کرے جو عمل نماز کے خلاف نہ ہو، اور اگر کر لیا تو پھر نیت کر کے تکبیر تحریمہ کہے۔ کوئی بھی عبادت بغیر نیت کے نہیں ہوتی ، مثلا دل میں نماز پڑھنے کی نیت نہیں ہے اور نماز کے تمام اعمال کر لے تو نماز نہیں ہوگی ، اس لئے نماز ادا ہونے کے لئے نیت کرنا فرض ہے۔ اور صرف دل میں ارادہ کر لینے کا نام نیت ہے۔ وجه : (۱) نیت فرض ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے۔ سمعت عمر بن خطاب علی المنبر يقول سمعت رسول الله الله يقول انما الاعمال بالنيات ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف کان بدء الوحی الی رسول اللہ ص ۱، نمبر ار مسلم شریف، باب قولہ انما الاعمال بالنیۃ الخ بص ۸۵۳، نمبر ۴۹۲۷/۱۹۰۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اعمال کا دارو مدار نیت پر ہے اسلئے نماز میں داخل ہونے کی نیت کرے گا تو نماز ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ (۲) اس اثر میں بھی اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد اللہ بن مسعود قال : تعودوا الخير فان الخير بالعادة ، و حافظوا على نياتكم فى الصلوة - الطبراني في الكبير، باب خطبة ابن مسعود و من کلامه، ج تاسع ،، ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۸۷۵۵/اعلاء السنن ، باب اشتراط النية للصلاة ، ج الثانی، ص ۱۶۳، نمبر ۶۴۲ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں نیت ضروری ہے۔ وجه (۱) تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہے اسکی دلیل یہ آیت ہے وربک فکبر (آیت ۳ ، سورۃ المدثر ہے ) کہ اپنے رب کی بڑائی بیان کیجئے ۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابی سعيد قال قال رسول الله مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم ولا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة فى فريضة او غيرها . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تحریم الصلوة وتحليلها ، ص۶۶ نمبر ۲۳۸ رابو داؤد شریف، باب الامام يحدث بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر رکعته ، ص ۱۰۰، نمبر ۶۱۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز شروع کرنے کے لئے تکبیر تحریمہ کہنا فرض ہے۔ (۳) عن ابراهيم قال : اذا نسي تكبيرة الافتتاح استأنف ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۸ فی الرجل ینسی تکبیرة الافتتاح، ج اول ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۲۴۶۵ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من نسی تكبيرة الافتتاح، ج ثانی ، ص ۴۶، نمبر ۲۵۴۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تکبیر افتتاح بھول جائے تو نماز دہرائے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہے۔ لغت : تکبیر تحریمہ: تحریمہ باندھنے کے لئے جو اللہ اکبر کہتے ہیں، یہ تکبیر تحریمہ ہے، یہ فرض ہے ، اس کے بغیر نماز نہیں ہوگی ۔ تحریمہ باندھنا: ناف کے نیچے جو ہاتھ باندھتے ہیں اس کو تحریمہ باندھنا کہتے ہیں، یہ سنت ہے۔ رکوع: آدمی اتنا جھکے کہ ہاتھ گھٹنے پر پہنچ جائے تو یہ رکوع میں جانا ہو گیا، اب تکبیر تحریمہ جائز نہیں، اور ہاتھ ابھی گھٹنے پر نہیں پہنچ رہا ہے تو ابھی تک قیام کی حالت ہے، یہاں تک تکبیر تحریمہ کہہ سکتا ہے۔
Chapter: Conditions of Prayer and Its Pillars. (350) And intention and the tahrrimah without a gap. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Prayer has a beginning and an end...' [hadith on prayer times]. Then the translation: (350) [2] Intention (7) and the opening takbir without a gap. Explanation: There are three matters, all obligatory: [1] making intention, [2] saying the opening takbir, [3] saying the takbir immediately after intention, with no gap—e.g., not eating, drinking, or doing any action contrary to prayer. If such a gap occurs, one must renew intention and say the takbir. No worship is valid without intention; if one performs all actions of prayer without intending prayer in the heart, the prayer is not valid. So intention is obligatory. The proof for intention being obligatory: the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' from Umar (Bukhari and Muslim), and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud. The proof for the takbir being obligatory: the verse 'And magnify your Lord' (Q. 74:3) and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrrimah is takbir, its tahlil is taslim' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). Also the report from Ibrahim: 'If one forgets the opening takbir, he must repeat the prayer.' Linguistic notes: Tahrrimah: the 'Allahu Akbar' said to enter prayer; it is obligatory. Tahrrimah bandhna (tying the tahrrimah): placing the hands below the navel; this is sunnah. Ruku': bending until the hands reach the knees; before that, one is still in standing and can say the takbir.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses the foundational obligations of entering prayer. The matn lists three obligations: (1) making intention (niyyah), (2) saying the opening takbir (tahrrimah), and (3) performing them consecutively without a gap. The commentary explains that all three are obligatory (fard). It provides proofs: for intention, the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud; for the takbir, the Qur'anic verse 'And magnify your Lord' and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrrimah is takbir, and its tahlil is taslim'; and for consecutiveness, the requirement that no foreign action intervenes between them. The linguistic note clarifies that 'tahrrimah' refers to the act of saying 'Allahu Akbar' to begin prayer, while 'tahrrimah bandhna' (tying the tahrrimah) refers to placing the hands under the navel, which is sunnah. The passage also defines the bowing posture (ruku') as bending enough for the hands to reach the knees; if one bends less, takbir is still permissible in the standing position.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention: the resolve in the heart to perform a specific prayer for Allah.
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir tahrrimah): The opening 'Allahu Akbar' that initiates prayer and prohibits worldly actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone makes intention for prayer but then eats before saying the opening takbir?
A) Prayer is valid because intention is present.
B) Prayer is invalid because of a gap.
C) Prayer is valid but requires repeating the intention.
D) Prayer is valid and no need to repeat takbir.

Key Takeaway
Intention and opening takbir are obligatory and must be consecutive without any intervening foreign action.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Saying the Opening Takbir While Standing Before Bowing
Ruling with proof from Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the opening takbir must be pronounced while standing and apply the hadith proof to determine the validity of the prayer.

Core Idea
The opening takbir must be said in full standing; bowing before completion invalidates the prayer.

This lesson focuses on a specific condition for the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram). The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, requires that the takbir be said while standing upright (qiyam) and before bending for ruku'. Understanding this condition is essential for the validity of one's prayer, as it ties the entrance into prayer to a deliberate posture of humility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify that the act is saying the opening takbir. The ruling is that it must be performed while standing upright and before beginning the bowing posture.
The act itself is a pillar (rukn) of the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA) that the Prophet ﷺ, when he stood for prayer, would say the takbir. This hadith is recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni certainty in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'when he stood for prayer, he would say the takbir' directly links the act of saying takbir to the state of standing. This indicates that the takbir is to be uttered while in the upright position.
The Prophet's consistent practice (fi'l) serves as a proof for obligation in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If a person begins to bow (ruku') before completing the takbir, the prayer is invalid because the condition of standing was not fulfilled at the moment of the takbir.
This condition applies to every prayer that includes an opening takbir, including fard, wajib, and sunnah prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۵۱) تکبیر تحریمہ کھڑے کھڑے کہے رکوع میں جھکنے سے پہلے۔ الله تشریح : تکبیر تحریمہ قیام کی حالت میں کہے، اور رکوع میں جھکنے سے پہلے کہے۔ وجه : عن علي بن ابي طالب قال كان رسول الله عله الا الا اذا قام الى الصلوة کبر ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما یستفتح به الصلوة من الدعاء، ص ۱۱۸، نمبر ۷۶۰ ) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ قیام کی حالت میں تکبیر کہے۔
Translation: (351) He says the opening takbir while standing, before bending for bowing. Explanation: He says the opening takbir in the standing position, and before bending for bowing. Proof: From Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he would say the takbir.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that the takbir is said while standing.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This is a ruling statement requiring the opening takbir to be performed while standing upright (qiyam) and before initiating the bowing posture (ruku'). The proof is the hadith of Ali that the Prophet would say the takbir when he stood for prayer, indicating the takbir is linked to the standing position. The Hanafi school holds that the takbir is a condition for entering prayer and must be said while standing; if one bows before completing the takbir, the prayer is not valid.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyam): Standing upright in prayer, required for fard prayers for those able.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What if someone begins to bow before completing the opening takbir?
A) The prayer is valid if the takbir is completed quickly.
B) The prayer is invalid because the takbir was not said while standing.
C) The prayer is valid but deficient.
D) The prayer is valid if the standing was partial.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir must be said while standing; bowing before its completion invalidates the prayer.
